格林童话（四） | Grimm's Fairy Tales Ⅳ
<<
>>
快乐大哥 Brother Lustig
从前发生过一次大规模的战争，战争结束的时候，很多士兵都退伍了。快乐大哥也一样退了伍，除了一小根面包棍和四个硬币之外，他离开的时候什么也没得到。圣彼得乔装打扮成了一个可怜的乞丐，快乐大哥走近的时候，他圣彼得便向他乞讨。快乐大哥答复道：“亲爱的乞丐，我能给你什么呢？我过去是名士兵，可已经退伍了，除了这小块面包棍和四个硬币以外，我什么也没有了，等这些也用完的时候，我就不得不像你一样去乞讨了。可我还是要给你些东西的。”于是他把面包棍分成了四份，给了圣彼得一份，此外又给了他一个硬币。圣彼得谢过他后，继续向前行路，他又打扮成另一个乞丐，等在快乐大哥要经过的路上。快乐大哥走近时，圣彼得便如从前一样向他乞讨。快乐大哥又说了一遍先前说过的话，又给了他四分之一的面包棍和一个铜板。圣彼得谢过他，继续前行，但是再次把自己乔装打扮成一个不同模样的乞丐，等在路上，向快乐大哥乞讨。快乐大哥也给了他第三份面包棍和第三个硬币。圣彼得感谢了他，快乐大哥继续赶路，他只剩下了四分之一的面包棍和一个铜板。拿着这点东西他走进了一家小旅馆，吃了面包，并要了一个铜板的啤酒。当都吃完后，他便继续他的旅程，这时圣彼得也打扮成了退伍士兵的样子，看到快乐大哥后，对他说：“你好，兄弟，你能不能给我一点面包和一个硬币去买点喝的呢？”快乐大哥回答道：“我到哪儿去弄呢？我已经退伍了，除了一根面包棍和四个硬币之外，我什么都没得到。我在路上遇到了三个乞丐，我每人给了四分之一的面包和一个硬币。我在小旅馆里把最后四分之一块面包吃掉了，用最后一个硬币换成酒喝了。我的口袋现在都空了，要是你也什么都没有的话，那我们可以一起乞讨的。”圣彼得回答道：“不用，我们还不必要那么做。我懂一点医术，我可以凭借这一点很快赚够我需要的钱。”快乐大哥说：“事实上，我对医术毫不了解啊，所以我只得独自去乞讨了。”圣彼得说：“就和我一起吧，如果我能挣到些什么的话，会分给你一半的。”快乐大哥说：“那真好。”于是他们一起上路了。 There was one on a time a great war, and when it came to an end, many soldiers were discharged.Then Brother Lustig also received his dismissal, and besides that, nothing but a small loaf of contract-bread, and four kreuzers in money, with which he departed.St. Peter had, however, placed himself in his way in the shape of a poor beggar, and when Brother Lustig came up, he begged alms of him.Brother Lustig replied, “Dear beggar man, what am I to give you?I have been a soldier, and have received my dismissal, and have nothing but this little loaf of contract-bread, and four kreuzers of money; when that is gone, I shall have to beg as well as you.Still I will give you something.”Thereupon he divided the loaf into four parts, and gave the apostle one of them, and a kreuzer likewise.St. Peter thanked him, went onwards, and threw himself again in the soldier’s way as a beggar, but in another shape; and when he came up begged a gift of him as before.Brother Lustig spoke as he had done before, and again gave him a quarter of the loaf and one kreuzer.St. Peter thanked him, and went onwards, but for the third time placed himself in another shape as a beggar on the road, and spoke to Brother Lustig.Brother Lustig gave him also the third quarter of bread and the third kreuzer.St. Peter thanked him, and Brother Lustig went onwards, and had but a quarter of the loaf, and one kreuzer.With that he went into an inn, ate the bread, and ordered one kreuzer’s worth of beer.When he had had it, he journeyed onwards, and then St. Peter, who had assumed the appearance of a discharged soldier, met and spoke to him thus: “Good day, comrade, canst thou not give me a bit of bread, and a kreuzer to get a drink?”“Where am I to procure it?” answered Brother Lustig; “I have been discharged, and I got nothing but a loaf of ammunition bread and four kreuzers in money.I met three beggars on the road, and I gave each of them a quarter of my bread, and one kreuzer.The last quarter I ate in the inn, and had a drink with the last kreuzer.Now my pockets are empty, and if thou also hast nothing we can go a-begging together.”“No,” answered St. Peter, “we need not quite do that.I know a little about medicine, and I will soon earn as much as I require by that.”“Indeed,” said Brother Lustig, “I know nothing of that, so I must go and beg alone.”“Just come with me,” said St. Peter, “and if I earn anything, thou shalt have half of it.”“All right,” said Brother Lustig, so they went away together.
后来他们来到了一处农舍，听到屋里传来很大的哀悼声和痛哭声。于是他们走了进去，原来屋里有个病危的男人，躺着快咽气了，他的太太正放声大哭。圣彼得说：“别哭哭啼啼了，我能让他重新好起来。”他从口袋里掏出一种药膏，很快就治愈了这个病人，他甚至都能够下床，完全健健康康的了。夫妻俩很高兴，说：“我们怎样才能报答你呢？我们要给你些什么呢？”可是圣彼得什么都不要，夫妇俩越是要给，他就越是推辞。然而快乐大哥用肘推了推圣彼得，说：“收一点东西吧，我们也确实很需要啊。”最后农妇拿来一只小羊羔，劝说圣彼得一定要收下，可他还是不要。于是快乐大哥戳了他一下，说：“收下吧，你这个傻子，我们很需要啊！”圣彼得最后说：“好吧，我就收下这只羊羔，但是我不背呀。如果你坚持要收，那你就得背着它了。”快乐大哥说：“那不是问题啊。”“我很容易就背得起它了，”接着就把羊羔扛到了肩膀上。然后他们就出发了，来到了一片树林里，快乐大哥开始感到羊羔有些重了，并且他也饿了，于是对圣彼得说：“看，这是一个不错的地方啊，我们就在这儿把羊羔煮煮吃了吧。”圣彼得回答道：“你想煮就煮吧，但是我不会啊。你要是煮的话，这里有个锅给你，煮好之前的这会儿功夫我就去周围转转吧。但是必须记住，直到我回来了你才能开始吃羊肉，我会适时回来的。”快乐大哥说：“好的，那你走吧，我懂烹调的，我能应付得好。”于是圣彼得离开了，快乐大哥宰了小羊羔，生起火来，将肉扔进锅里，把肉煮沸。可羊肉都完全煮熟了，圣彼得还是没有回来，于是快乐大哥从锅里捞出肉来切开了，看到了羊心。他说：“这据说是最好吃的部分了，”并尝了尝，但最后他把整个羊心都吃掉了。圣彼得终于回来了，他说：“你可以把整只羊都吃了，我只要那个羊心，给我吧。”于是快乐大哥拿起刀叉，假装很急切地在羊肉里寻找，但是没能找到，后来他忽然说：“没有羊心。”圣彼得说：“可它能在哪儿呢？”快乐大哥答道：“我不知道，不过你看，我们俩真是傻瓜呀，竟要找羊心，我们都不记得了，小羊羔是没有心的！”圣彼得说：“噢，这真是新奇！每个动物都长着心，为什么小羊羔就没长呢？”快乐大哥说：“没长，确实没长，兄弟，小羊羔是没有心的。认真想一想，你会想起来的，它的确没长心。”圣彼得说：“那好吧，如果没有羊心，我就不想吃什么了，你自己吃吧。”快乐大哥说：“我现在吃不完的，就放到背包里带走。”他吃了半只羊羔，把剩下的放到了背包里。 Then they came to a peasant’s house inside which they heard loud lamentations and cries; so they went in, and there the husband was lying sick unto death, and very near his end, and his wife was crying and weeping quite loudly.“Stop that howling and crying,” said St. Peter, “I will make the man well again,” and he took a salve out of his pocket, and healed the sick man in a moment, so that he could get up, and was in perfect health.In great delight the man and his wife said, “How can we reward you?What shall we give you?”But St. Peter would take nothing, and the more the peasant folks offered him, the more he refused.Brother Lustig, however, nudged St. Peter, and said, “Take something; sure enough we are in need of it.”At length the woman brought a lamb and said to St. Peter that he really must take that, but he would not.Then Brother Lustig gave him a poke in the side, and said, “Do take it, you stupid fool; we are in great want of it!”Then St. Peter said at last, “Well, I will take the lamb, but I won’t carry it; if thou wilt insist on having it, thou must carry it.”“That is nothing,” said Brother Lustig.“I will easily carry it,” and took it on his shoulder.Then they departed and came to a wood, but Brother Lustig had begun to feel the lamb heavy, and he was hungry, so he said to St. Peter, “Look, that’s a good place, we might cook the lamb there, and eat it.”“As you like,” answered St. Peter, “but I can’t have anything to do with the cooking; if thou wilt cook, there is a kettle for thee, and in the meantime I will walk about a little until it is ready.Thou must, however, not begin to eat until I have come back, I will come at the right time.”“Well, go, then,” said Brother Lustig, “I understand cookery, I will manage it.”Then St. Peter went away, and Brother Lustig killed the lamb, lighted a fire, threw the meat into the kettle, and boiled it.The lamb was, however, quite ready, and the apostle Peter had not come back, so Brother Lustig took it out of the kettle, cut it up, and found the heart.“That is said to be the best part,” said he, and tasted it, but at last he ate it all up.At length St. Peter returned and said, “Thou mayst eat the whole of the lamb thyself, I will only have the heart, give me that.”Then Brother Lustig took a knife and fork, and pretended to look anxiously about amongst the lamb’s flesh, but not to be able to find the heart, and at last he said abruptly, “There is none here.”“But where can it be?” said the apostle.“I don’t know,” replied Brother Lustig, “but look, what fools we both are, to seek for the lamb’s heart, and neither of us to remember that a lamb has no heart!”“Oh,” said St. Peter, “that is something quite new!Every animal has a heart, why is a lamb to have none?”“No, be assured, my brother,” said Brother Lustig, “that a lamb has no heart; just consider it seriously, and then you will see that it really has none.”“Well, it is all right,” said St. Peter, “if there is no heart, then I want none of the lamb; thou mayst eat it alone.”“What I can’t eat now, I will carry away in my knapsack,” said Brother Lustig, and he ate half the lamb, and put the rest in his knapsack.
他们继续赶路，这时圣彼得变出了一条大大的河来，河水流淌着，正好挡住了他们的去路，他们被迫要蹚水过去。圣彼得说：“你先走吧。”快乐大哥答道：“我不，你得先走。”他想：“要是水太深了，我就留在后面不过了。”于是圣彼得大步蹚着水过去了，水只到了他的膝盖处。快乐大哥因此也开始过河，可河水越来越深，都涨到他的咽喉处了。他喊道：“兄弟，救救我啊！”圣彼得说：“那你会承认是你吃了羊心吗？”他说：“不，我没吃。”于是河水又涨高了，高到他的嘴巴处。快乐大哥又喊：“救救我，兄弟。”圣彼得说：“那你承认你吃了羊心吗？”他答道：“不，我没吃。”圣彼得无论如何是不会让他淹死的，于是把水退去，帮他渡过了河。 They went farther, and then St. Peter caused a great stream of water to flow right across their path, and they were obliged to pass through it.Said St. Peter, “Do thou go first.”“No,” answered Brother Lustig, “thou must go first,” and he thought, “if the water is too deep I will stay behind.”Then St. Peter strode through it, and the water just reached to his knee.So Brother Lustig began to go through also, but the water grew deeper and reached to his throat.Then he cried, “Brother, help me!”St. Peter said, “Then wilt thou confess that thou hast eaten the lamb’s heart?”“No,” said he, “I have not eaten it.”Then the water grew deeper still and rose to his mouth.“Help me, brother,” cried the soldier.St. Peter said, “Then wilt thou confess that thou hast eaten the lamb’s heart?”“No,” he replied, “I have not eaten it.”St. Peter, however, would not let him be drowned, but made the water sink and helped him through it.
他们继续赶路，来到了一个国家，他们听说国王的女儿病重，快要咽气了。快乐大哥便对圣彼得说：“嗨，兄弟！这对我们来说可是一次机会啊。如果我们能治好她的病，那一辈子都会有人供养我们了呀！”但是对他而言，圣彼得走得特别慢，快乐大哥说：“好兄弟，快点，快些，那样我们才可能及时赶到啊。”尽管快乐大哥尽可能地又催他又推他，可圣彼得却越走越慢了，最后他们听说公主已经死掉了。快乐大哥说道：“现在我们完了！都怪你走得那么慢！”圣彼得答道：“安静点吧，我不仅仅能治愈病人；我还能让死人起死回生。”快乐大哥说：“好吧，如果你能做到，那还行，你这次至少得为我们赢回半个王国。”于是他们走进了王宫，王宫里的每个人都沉浸在巨大的悲痛中，圣彼得告诉国王他能让公主起死回生。于是他被带到了公主身边，他说：“给我拿一口锅和一些水来。”这些东西准备好后，他命令所有人都离开，除了快乐大哥之外不允许任何人在他旁边。然后他截下了公主的四肢，把它们扔到了水里，在锅下面生起火，煮了起来。在肉从骨头上脱落下来后，他便取出了这些漂亮的白骨放在桌上，然后把它们按原本的顺序排列到了一起。完成这些后，他走上前去，说了三遍：“以圣父圣子圣灵的名义，死去的人啊，站起来吧。”到第三遍的时候，公主真的站了起来，活生生的，既健康又漂亮。国王非常高兴，便对圣彼得说：“你想要什么报酬。即使是要我的半个王国，我也会给你的。”但是圣彼得却说：“我什么也不要。”快乐大哥暗自想：“噢，你这个笨蛋！”他捅了捅圣彼得，说：“别犯傻了！即使你什么都不需要了，我还需要呢。”圣彼得无论如何什么也不要，可是国王看出来了，另一个人是很想收点什么的，于是他命令财务大臣把快乐大哥的背包里装满了金子。然后他们继续赶路了，走到一处森林的时候，圣彼得对快乐大哥说：“现在，我们把金子分一分吧。”他答道：“好的，我们分一分吧。”于是圣彼得分起金子来，他把金子分成了三堆。快乐大哥暗自想：“他现在脑子里想什么疯事呢？他分成了三堆，可我们就两个人啊！”圣彼得说：“我已经准确地分好了，我一堆，你一堆，吃羊心的那个人也有一堆。” Then they journeyed onwards, and came to a kingdom where they heard that the King’s daughter lay sick unto death.“Hollo, brother!” said the soldier to St. Peter, “this is a chance for us; if we can heal her we shall be provided for, for life!”But St. Peter was not half quick enough for him, “Come, lift your legs, my dear brother,” said he, “that we may get there in time.”But St. Peter walked slower and slower, though Brother Lustig did all he could to drive and push him on, and at last they heard that the princess was dead.“Now we are done for!” said Brother Lustig; “that comes of thy sleepy way of walking!”“Just be quiet,” answered St. Peter, “I can do more than cure sick people; I can bring dead ones to life again.”“Well, if thou canst do that,” said Brother Lustig, “it’s all right, but thou shouldst earn at least half the kingdom for us by that.”Then they went to the royal palace, where every one was in great grief, but St. Peter told the King that he would restore his daughter to life.He was taken to her, and said, “Bring me a kettle and some water,” and when that was brought, he bade everyone go out, and allowed no one to remain with him but Brother Lustig.Then he cut off all the dead girl’s limbs, and threw them in the water, lighted a fire beneath the kettle, and boiled them.And when the flesh had fallen away from the bones, he took out the beautiful white bones, and laid them on a table, and arranged them together in their natural order.When he had done that, he stepped forward and said three times, “In the name of the holy Trinity, dead woman, arise.”And at the third time, the princess arose, living, healthy and beautiful.Then the King was in the greatest joy, and said to St. Peter, “Ask for thy reward; even if it were half my kingdom, I would give it thee.”But St. Peter said, “I want nothing for it.”“Oh, thou tomfool!” thought Brother Lustig to himself, and nudged his comrade’s side, and said, “Don’t be so stupid!If thou hast no need of anything, I have.”St. Peter, however, would have nothing, but as the King saw that the other would very much like to have something, he ordered his treasurer to fill Brother Lustig’s knapsack with gold.Then they went on their way, and when they came to a forest, St. Peter said to Brother Lustig, “Now, we will divide the gold.”“Yes,” he replied, “we will.”So St. Peter divided the gold, and divided it into three heaps.Brother Lustig thought to himself, “What craze has he got in his head now?He is making three shares, and there are only two of us!”But St. Peter said, “I have divided it exactly; there is one share for me, one for thee, and one for him who ate the lamb’s heart.”
快乐大哥马上说：“噢，我吃了羊心！”然后迅速地把金子收了过去。他又说：“你要相信我说的话。”圣彼得说：“要是羊羔不长心的话，这怎么可能是真的呢？”“嗯，什么啊，兄弟，你在想些什么啊？羊羔像其他动物一样都长着心的，凭什么只有它们不长心呢？”圣彼得说：“好吧，但愿如此。你自己留着金子吧，但是我不会再和你同行了，我要自己走了。”快乐大哥答道：“随便你，好兄弟。再会了。” “Oh, I ate that!” replied Brother Lustig, and hastily swept up the gold.“You may trust what I say.”“But how can that be true,” said St. Peter, “when a lamb has no heart?”“Eh, what, brother, what can you be thinking of?Lambs have hearts like other animals, why should only they have none?”“Well, so be it,” said St. Peter, “keep the gold to yourself, but I will stay with you no longer; I will go my way alone.”“As you like, dear brother,” answered Brother Lustig.Farewell.”
于是圣彼得踏上了另一段路途，快乐大哥想：“他自己走开了倒不错，他的确是一个奇怪的人啊。”他有了足够的钱，却不知道如何打理这些钱，他挥霍无度，随意送人，随着时间流逝，他再次一无所有了。后来他走到一个国家，听说国王的女儿去世了。他想：“噢，嗬！这对我来说也许是件好事呢。我会让她起死回生，会得到我应得的报酬啊。”于是他去见国王，主动说能让公主起死回生。国王已听说过，有个四处周游的退伍士兵能让人起死回生，他以为快乐大哥就是那个人。但是由于他对快乐大哥并没有信心，便事先同谋士们商量了一下，他们说既然公主已经死了，倒不妨让他试一试。于是快乐大哥命人端来一口盛着水的锅，又命令所有人出去，他仿照圣彼得的做法，截下了公主的四肢，扔到水里，在下面生起一堆火来。水烧开了，肉脱落下来，他便取出骨头放到桌上，可他不知道如何排列骨头的顺序，都排错了，错得一塌糊涂。然后他站在骨头前，说道：“以圣父圣子圣灵的名义，死去的人啊，我命令你站起来。”他说了三遍，可骨头仍一动不动。于是他又说了三遍，可依旧徒劳，他喊道：“你这讨厌的姑娘，站起来！站起来，不然你会更倒霉的！”当他这么说的时候，圣彼得忽然以先前退伍士兵的模样出现了。他从窗户穿进来，说：“你这个无法无天的家伙，你在干什么啊？你把她的骨头排扔得这么乱，怎能让她复活啊？”他答道：“好兄弟，我已经尽我最大的努力了。”“这次我会帮你摆脱困境，但是我要跟你讲明一点，如果你还要做这类事情，那你就会倒霉的，你也不能因为此事向国王索要或者接受任何报酬！”随即圣彼得把骨头按正确顺序排列好，对公主说了三遍：“以圣父圣子圣灵的名义，死去的人啊，站起来吧。”公主便站了起来，像以前一样健康漂亮。圣彼得又从窗户穿了出去，快乐大哥看到一切都进行得这么顺利很是高兴，但是想到竟不能为此得到任何报酬，又很是烦恼。他想：“我倒想知道这个家伙脑袋里想的是什么，因为他一只手给你的东西，又会用另一手拿回去，真是毫无道理！”国王要给快乐大哥任何他想要的东西，他却什么也不敢要.可是，他设法通过暗示和诡计使得国王下令把他的背包里装满了金子，他带着那些金子上路了。当他走出去的时候，圣彼得正站在门旁，说道：“看看你是个什么样的人，我没告诉你什么都不能收吗，你却装了满背包的金子！”快乐大哥答道：“人们非要给我装上，我能怎么办？”“好吧，我告诉你，如果你再干这种事情，你就会为此付出代价的！”“啊，兄弟，别担心了，我现在已经有钱了，我干嘛还给自己找麻烦去洗骨头啊？”圣彼得说：“是的，这些金子够花一长段时间了！为了你以后再不会去做那些禁止的事情，我要赐予你的背包一种魔力，也就是，你想要里面有什么，那就会有什么。再见了，你以后不会再看到我了。”快乐大哥说：“再见。”他暗自想：“你走了我倒高兴呢，你真是个怪人，我当然不会跟着你了。”但是，对他背包被赋予的那种魔力，他并未多想。 Then St. Peter went a different road, but Brother Lustig thought, “It is a good thing that he has taken himself off, he is certainly a strange saint, after all.”Then he had money enough, but did not know how to manage it, squandered it, gave it away, and and when some time had gone by, once more had nothing.Then he arrived in a certain country where he heard that a King’s daughter was dead.“Oh, ho!” thought he, “that may be a good thing for me; I will bring her to life again, and see that I am paid as I ought to be.”So he went to the King, and offered to raise the dead girl to life again.Now the King had heard that a discharged soldier was traveling about and bringing dead persons to life again, and thought that Brother Lustig was the man; but as he had no confidence in him, he consulted his councillors first, who said that he might give it a trial as his daughter was dead.Then Brother Lustig ordered water to be brought to him in a kettle, bade every one go out, cut the limbs off, threw them in the water and lighted a fire beneath, just as he had seen St. Peter do.The water began to boil, the flesh fell off, and then he took the bones out and laid them on the table, but he did not know the order in which to lay them, and placed them all wrong and in confusion.Then he stood before them and said, “In the name of the most holy Trinity, dead maiden, I bid thee arise,” and he said this thrice, but the bones did not stir.So he said it thrice more, but also in vain: “Confounded girl that you are, get up!” cried he, “Get up, or it shall be worse for you!”When he had said that, St. Peter suddenly appeared in his former shape as a discharged soldier; he entered by the window and said, “Godless man, what art thou doing?How can the dead maiden arise, when thou hast thrown about her bones in such confusion?”“Dear brother, I have done everything to the best of my ability,” he answered.“This once, I will help thee out of thy difficulty, but one thing I tell thee, and that is that if ever thou undertakest anything of the kind again, it will be the worse for thee, and also that thou must neither demand nor accept the smallest thing from the King for this!”Thereupon St. Peter laid the bones in their right order, said to the maiden three times, “In the name of the most holy Trinity, dead maiden, arise,” and the King’s daughter arose, healthy and beautiful as before.Then St. Peter went away again by the window, and Brother Lustig was rejoiced to find that all had passed off so well, but was very much vexed to think that after all he was not to take anything for it.“I should just like to know,” thought he, “what fancy that fellow has got in his head, for what he gives with one hand he takes away with the other, there is no sense whatever in it!”Then the King offered Brother Lustig whatsoever he wished to have, but he did not dare to take anything; however, by hints and cunning, he contrived to make the King order his knapsack to be filled with gold for him, and with that he departed.When he got out, St. Peter was standing by the door, and said, “Just look what a man thou art; did I not forbid thee to take anything, and there thou hast thy knapsack full of gold!”“How can I help that,” answered Brother Lustig, “if people will put it in for me?”“Well, I tell thee this, that if ever thou settest about anything of this kind again thou shalt suffer for it!”“Eh, brother, have no fear, now I have money, why should I trouble myself with washing bones?”“Faith,” said St. Peter, “the gold will last a long time!In order that after this thou mayst never tread in forbidden paths, I will bestow on thy knapsack this property, namely, that whatsoever thou wishest to have inside it, shall be there.Farewell, thou wilt now never see me more.”“Goodbye,” said Brother Lustig, and thought to himself, “I am very glad that thou hast taken thyself off, thou strange fellow; I shall certainly not follow thee.”But of the magical power which had been bestowed on his knapsack, he thought no more.
快乐大哥带着他的那些钱财四处周游，像以前一样挥霍浪费。最后他只剩下四个铜板了，经过一家小酒馆的时候，他想：“这些钱也得花掉的。”于是要了三个铜板的酒，还有一个铜板的面包。他正坐在那里喝酒的时候，烤鹅肉的香味儿传到了鼻子里。快乐大哥四处张望了一下，看到店主的烤炉里杵着两只鹅呢。这时他记起圣彼得说过，他想要背包里有什么，那就会有什么，于是他说：“噢，嗬！我一定要拿这鹅来试一试。” Brother Lustig travelled about with his money, and squandered and wasted what he had as before.When at last he had no more than four kreuzers, he passed by an inn and thought, “The money must go,” and ordered three kreuzers’ worth of wine and one kreuzer’s worth of bread for himself.As he was sitting there drinking, the smell of roast goose made its way to his nose.Brother Lustig looked about and peeped, and saw that the host had two geese standing in the oven.Then he remembered that his comrade had said that whatsoever he wished to have in his knapsack should be there, so he said, “Oh, ho! I must try that with the geese。”
因此他走了出去，走到门外后，他说：“我想要那两只烤鹅从烤炉里来到我的背包里。”说完后，他解开背包向里一看，两只烤鹅就在里面。他说：“啊，真灵啊！现在我可是幸运了！”他走到一块草地上，拿出了烤鹅肉。他正吃着的时候，走来了两个学徒工，他们用饥饿的眼神望着还没被动过的第二只烤鹅。快乐大哥暗自想道：“我吃一只就足够了。”于是把这两个人叫过来，说：“拿着这只鹅吧，为我的健康祈祷就好。”他们谢过他，提着烤鹅去了一家小酒馆，为自己点了半瓶啤酒和一个面包，拿出烤鹅吃了起来。老板娘看到他们后，对她丈夫说：“那两个人在吃鹅呢，去看看是不是从我们烤炉里拿的。”店主跑过去，发现烤炉居然是空的！他喊道：“什么！你们这两个贼，想不花分文地就吃了我们的鹅吗？现在就付钱；不然我就用绿榛树枝狠狠地抽你们一顿。”两人说道：“我们不是贼啊，一个退伍士兵给我们的鹅，他就在外面的草地上。”“你们别这样来蒙骗我！那个士兵刚才来过这里，但他又走出了店门，像是个诚实的人。我亲眼看到他走出去的，你们两个才是贼，付钱！”可他们付不起钱，于是他拿起一根棍子，把他们打出了屋子。 So he went out, and when he was outside the door, he said, “I wish those two roasted geese out of the oven and in my knapsack,” and when he had said that, he unbuckled it and looked in, and there they were inside it.“Ah, that’s right!” said he, “now I am a made man!” and went away to a meadow and took out the roast meat.When he was in the midst of his meal, two journeymen came up and looked at the second goose, which was not yet touched, with hungry eyes.Brother Lustig thought to himself, “One is enough for me,” and called the two men up and said, “Take the goose, and eat it to my health.”They thanked him, and went with it to the inn, ordered themselves a half bottle of wine and a loaf, took out the goose which had been given them, and began to eat.The hostess saw them and said to her husband, “Those two are eating a goose; just look and see if it is not one of ours, out of the oven.”The landlord ran thither, and behold the oven was empty!“What!” cried he, “you thievish crew, you want to eat goose as cheap as that?Pay for it this moment; or I will wash you well with green hazel sap.”The two said, “We are no thieves, a discharged soldier gave us the goose, outside there in the meadow.”“You shall not throw dust in my eyes that way!The soldier was here but he went out by the door, like an honest fellow.I looked after him myself; you are the thieves and shall pay!”But as they could not pay, he took a stick, and cudgeled them out of the house.
快乐大哥又上路了，他来到一座宏伟的城堡前，在城堡不远处有一家不起眼的小旅店。他走进旅店，要住一宿，可店主拒绝收留他，说道：“已经没有空屋了，这里都住满了贵客。”快乐大哥说：“我很吃惊啊，他们到你这里却不到那座辉煌的城堡去。”店主答道：“啊，事实是如此，但是在这里睡一晚完全不会有事。到目前为止，所有尝试着去那里的人还没有能活着走出来的呢。” Brother Lustig went his way and came to a place where there was a magnificent castle, and not far from it a wretched inn.He went to the inn and asked for a night’s lodging, but the landlord turned him away, and said, “There is no more room here, the house is full of noble guests.”“It surprises me that they should come to you and not go to that splendid castle,” said Brother Lustig.“Ah, indeed,” replied the host, “but it is no slight matter to sleep there for a night; no one who has tried it so far, has ever come out of it alive.”
快乐大哥说：“要是别人已经尝试过了，那我也要尝试一下。” “If others have tried it,” said Brother Lustig, “I will try it too.”
店主说：“别管了，你会送命的。”快乐大哥说：“我不会立马就死掉的，给我钥匙吧，再给我一些可口的食物和酒。”于是店主给了他钥匙，还有食物和酒。快乐大哥便带着这些去了城堡，尽情地享用了晚餐，最后他困了，可是由于没有床，他便躺在了地上。他很快就睡着了，可是夜里被一阵很大的噪声惊扰了。他醒来的时候看到屋里有九个模样丑陋的魔鬼，他们围成一个圈，正绕着他跳舞。快乐大哥说：“好啊，你们随便跳多久都行，但是谁也不能靠近我。”但是这些魔鬼却不断地越来越靠近他，他们可怕的脚几乎都要踏到了他的脸上。他说道：“停下来，你们这些可恶的魔鬼。”可他们越来越过分了。于是快乐大哥发怒了，他喊道：“喂！我很快就会让你们安静下来的。”他拿起一只椅子腿，朝他们中间打了过去。 “Leave it alone,” said the host, “it will cost you your neck.”“It won’t kill me at once,” said Brother Lustig, “just give me the key, and some good food and wine.”So the host gave him the key, and food and wine, and with this Brother Lustig went into the castle, enjoyed his supper, and at length, as he was sleepy, he lay down on the ground, for there was no bed.He soon fell asleep, but during the night was disturbed by a great noise, and when he awoke, he saw nine ugly devils in the room, who had made a circle, and were dancing around him.Brother Lustig said, “Well, dance as long as you like, but none of you must come too close.”But the devils pressed continually nearer to him, and almost stepped on his face with their hideous feet.“Stop, you devils’ ghosts,” said he, but they behaved still worse.Then Brother Lustig grew angry, and cried, “Hola! But I will soon make it quiet,” and got the leg of a chair and struck out into the midst of them with it。”
灰姑娘 Cinderella
从前有个富人，他的太太病重，感觉自己将不久于人世，就把独生女儿叫到床前，嘱咐道：“亲爱的孩子，你一定要为人善良虔诚，这样，敬爱的上帝都会保佑你的，我也会在天堂注视着你，保护你！”然后，她就合上眼，去世了，从此，每天小姑娘都要去妈妈的坟前哭泣，她也一直保持着善良和虔诚。冬天来临的时候，坟上覆盖了一层皑皑白雪；春天到来的时候，白雪融化了，有钱人也新娶了一位太太。 The wife of a rich man fell sick, and as she felt that her end was drawing near, she called her only daughter to her bedside and said, “Dear child, be good and pious, and then the good God will always protect thee, and I will look down on thee from heaven and be near thee.”Thereupon she closed her eyes and departed.Every day the maiden went out to her mother’s grave, and wept, and she remained pious and good.When winter came the snow spread a white sheet over the grave, and when the spring sun had drawn it off again, the man had taken another wife.
新太太带了两个女儿一起进门，两个女孩都是外表漂亮，心地狠毒。从此，那个可怜女孩的苦日子就开始了。“我们要和这只蠢鹅一起坐在客厅里吗？”那两个狠毒的女孩说，“不劳而获的蠢东西，滚去厨房呆着吧！”她们夺走她的漂亮裙子，只丢给她一条灰旧的睡衣和一双木鞋。“看那个骄傲的公主，她穿得好时髦啊！”她们大喊着，大笑着，把她赶进厨房。可怜的女孩，就这样成天从早到晚地在厨房忙活着，天不亮就得起床，挑水，烧火，煮饭，清洗。除此之外，那两个女孩还想方设法地伤害她。她们对她冷嘲热讽，还把豌豆和扁豆一起打翻在灰堆里，让她坐在地上一颗颗地捡起来分开。晚上，女孩工作得精疲力竭却没有床可睡，她只能睡在灶边的灰堆里。所以，她看起来总是一身尘土，脏兮兮的，人们都叫她“灰姑娘”。一天，她们的父亲要去赶集，临走之前，问那两个继女需要带什么。一个说：“好看的裙子！”另一个说：“珠宝首饰！”“你呢，灰姑娘？”父亲问，“想要什么呢？”“父亲，你就把在回家路上碰掉你帽子的第一根树枝折回来给我吧。”于是父亲就给那两个女儿买了漂亮的裙子和珠宝首饰，回家的路上，他骑马穿过一片茂密的绿丛林，一根榛树枝将他的帽子刮了下来。于是他折下树枝，带回家去。到家之后，他把两个继女想要的东西交给她们，把折来的榛树枝给了灰姑娘。灰姑娘谢过父亲，转身去到妈妈的坟前，将树枝种在坟头，她哭啊哭，眼泪滴下来，将树枝都打湿了。小树枝在眼泪的滋润下竟然长成一棵挺拔的小树。灰姑娘每天都要来到树下，边哭边祈祷，有一只白色的小鸟常常会飞到枝头，只要灰姑娘许个愿，小鸟就会带给她想要的东西。 The woman had brought two daughters into the house with her, who were beautiful and fair of face, but vile and black of heart.Now began a bad time for the poor step-child.“Is the stupid goose to sit in the parlour with us?” said they.“He who wants to eat bread must earn it; out with the kitchen-wench.”They took her pretty clothes away from her, put an old grey bedgown on her, and gave her wooden shoes.“Just look at the proud princess, how decked out she is!” they cried, and laughed, and led her into the kitchen.There she had to do hard work from morning till night, get up before daybreak, carry water, light fires, cook and wash.Besides this, the sisters did her every imaginable injury—they mocked her and emptied her peas and lentils into the ashes, so that she was forced to sit and pick them out again.In the evening when she had worked till she was weary she had no bed to go to, but had to sleep by the fireside in the ashes.And as on that account she always looked dusty and dirty, they called her Cinderella.It happened that the father was once going to the fair, and he asked his two step-daughters what he should bring back for them.“Beautiful dresses,” said one, “Pearls and jewels,” said the second.“And thou, Cinderella,” said he, “what wilt thou have?”“Father, break off for me the first branch which knocks against your hat on your way home.”So he bought beautiful dresses, pearls and jewels for his two step-daughters, and on his way home, as he was riding through a green thicket, a hazel twig brushed against him and knocked off his hat.Then he broke off the branch and took it with him.When he reached home he gave his step-daughters the things which they had wished for, and to Cinderella he gave the branch from the hazel-bush.Cinderella thanked him, went to her mother’s grave and planted the branch on it, and wept so much that the tears fell down on it and watered it.And it grew, however, and became a handsome tree.Thrice a day Cinderella went and sat beneath it, and wept and prayed, and a little white bird always came on the tree, and if Cinderella expressed a wish, the bird threw down to her what she had wished for.
有一次，这里的国王举办了一场历时三天的盛宴，邀请了王国里所有年轻漂亮的女孩，好让王子从中挑选一个女孩做他的新娘。灰姑娘的两个姐姐听说自己也在被邀请的行列，兴奋不已，她们对灰姑娘喊道：“快帮我们梳好头发，擦干净鞋子，系好鞋扣，我们要去王宫赴宴啦！”灰姑娘都一一照办了，可是她还是哭了，因为她也想跟她们一起去参加舞会，她恳求继母能带她一起去。“你还想去，灰姑娘？”继母说，“就你那一身脏兮兮的灰，还想去赴宴？你一没裙子，二没鞋子，还想去跳舞？”可是灰姑娘一个劲地恳求，最后，继母说：“我把一碗扁豆倒在灶灰里，如果你两小时以内都捡起来了，你就能跟我们一起去。”女孩从后门来到花园，喊道：“听话的鸽子和斑鸠，天空中所有的鸟儿，请帮我把扁豆捡起来吧！ It happened, however, that the King appointed a festival which was to last three days, and to which all the beautiful young girls in the country were invited, in order that his son might choose himself a bride.When the two step-sisters heard that they too were to appear among the number, they were delighted, called Cinderella and said, “Comb our hair for us, brush our shoes and fasten our buckles, for we are going to the festival at the King’s palace.”Cinderella obeyed, but wept, because she too would have liked to go with them to the dance, and begged her step-mother to allow her to do so.“Thou go, Cinderella!” said she; “Thou art dusty and dirty and wouldst go to the festival?Thou hast no clothes and shoes, and yet wouldst dance!”As, however, Cinderella went on asking, the step-mother at last said, “I have emptied a dish of lentils into the ashes for thee, if thou hast picked them out again in two hours, thou shalt go with us.”The maiden went through the back-door into the garden, and called, “You tame pigeons, you turtle-doves, and all you birds beneath the sky, come and help me to pick
好的放进碗里，坏的吞进肚里。” The good into the pot, The bad into the crop.”
只见两只白鸽先从厨房的窗户飞进来，然后，斑鸠啊，天上飞的各种鸟儿都呼呼地飞来了，涌进厨房，停在灶边的灰堆里。鸽子点着头开始捡豆子，捡啊捡啊捡啊，其他的鸟儿也跟着捡起来，捡啊捡啊捡啊，把好的扁豆都叼进了碗里。一个小时不到，豆子就捡完了，鸟儿们全都飞走了。灰姑娘高高兴兴地把碗端给继母看，满以为继母会带她一起去赴宴。可是继母又说：“不行！灰姑娘，没有好看的衣服，根本不能跳舞，只会让别人笑话你。”灰姑娘又难过地哭起来，于是继母又说：“我把两碗扁豆都倒进灶灰里面，要是你能在一个小时内捡完，你就能跟我们一起去。”继母心想：“这次她是肯定干不完的。”她将两碗扁豆都倒进了灶灰里，灰姑娘又穿过后门来到花园，大喊道：“听话的鸽子、斑鸠，和天空中的所有鸟儿啊，请来帮助我把扁豆捡起来吧！ Then two white pigeons came in by the kitchen-window, and afterwards the turtle-doves, and at last all the birds beneath the sky, came whirring and crowding in, and alighted amongst the ashes.And the pigeons nodded with their heads and began pick, pick, pick, pick, and the rest began also pick, pick, pick, pick, and gathered all the good grains into the dish.Hardly had one hour passed before they had finished, and all flew out again.Then the girl took the dish to her step-mother, and was glad, and believed that now she would be allowed to go with them to the festival.But the step-mother said, “No, Cinderella, thou hast no clothes and thou canst not dance; thou wouldst only be laughed at.”And as Cinderella wept at this, the step-mother said, “If thou canst pick two dishes of lentils out of the ashes for me in one hour, thou shalt go with us.”And she thought to herself, “That she most certainly cannot do.”When the step-mother had emptied the two dishes of lentils amongst the ashes, the maiden went through the back-door into the garden and cried, “You tame pigeons, you turtle-doves, and all you birds under heaven, come and help me to pick
好的放进碗里，坏的吞进肚里。” The good into the pot, The bad into the crop.”
只见两只白鸽先从厨房的窗户飞进来，然后，斑鸠啊，天上飞的各种鸟儿都呼呼地飞来了，涌进厨房，停在灶边的灰堆里。鸽子点着头开始捡豆子，捡啊捡啊捡啊，其他的鸟儿也跟着捡起来，捡啊捡啊捡啊，把好的扁豆都叼进了碗里。半个小时不到，鸟儿们就全部捡完，然后再一次飞走了。女孩高高兴兴地把碗端给继母看，满以为这次她能跟她们一起去赴宴了。但是继母却说：“这也没用啊！我不会带你去的，你连裙子都没有，怎么跳舞？你会让我们感到羞耻的！”继母不再搭理灰姑娘，带着她两个骄傲的女儿匆匆走了。 Then two white pigeons came in by the kitchen-window, and afterwards the turtle-doves, and at length all the birds beneath the sky, came whirring and crowding in, and alighted amongst the ashes.And the doves nodded with their heads and began pick, pick, pick, pick, and the others began also pick, pick, pick, pick, and gathered all the good seeds into the dishes, and before half an hour was over they had already finished, and all flew out again.Then the maiden carried the dishes to the step-mother and was delighted, and believed that she might now go with them to the festival.But the step-mother said, “All this will not help thee; thou goest not with us, for thou hast no clothes and canst not dance; we should be ashamed of thee!”On this she turned her back on Cinderella, and hurried away with her two proud daughters.
家里只剩下灰姑娘孤零零一个人了，她走到妈妈的坟前，在榛树下喊道： As no one was now at home, Cinderella went to her mother’s grave beneath the hazel-tree, and cried,
“小树枝，摇一摇，晃一晃！给我一条金丝银线织的裙子吧！” “Shiver and quiver, little tree, Silver and gold throw down over me.”
于是小鸟儿飞来，送给她一条金丝银线织就的漂亮裙子，还有一双用银线丝缎编成的舞鞋。灰姑娘飞快地穿上它们去了宴会。继母和两个女儿都没认出她来，还以为她是外国来的公主，因为她穿着那条金色的裙子看起来美极了。她们压根没想到这就是灰姑娘，以为她还在家里，坐在地上从灰堆里捡着扁豆。王子走向灰姑娘，牵起她的手，一起翩翩起舞。他不愿再跟其他女孩跳舞，一直紧紧地握着灰姑娘的手。如果有其他人来请灰姑娘跳舞，王子就说：“这是我的舞伴。” Then the bird threw a gold and silver dress down to her, and slippers embroidered with silk and silver.She put on the dress with all speed, and went to the festival.Her step-sisters and the step-mother however did not know her, and thought she must be a foreign princess, for she looked so beautiful in the golden dress.They never once thought of Cinderella, and believed that she was sitting at home in the dirt, picking lentils out of the ashes.The prince went to meet her, took her by the hand and danced with her.He would dance with no other maiden, and never left loose of her hand, and if any one else came to invite her, he said, “This is my partner.”
灰姑娘一直跳到夜幕降临，她必须回家了。王子说：“请让我送你回去吧！”因为他想知道这位美丽女孩到底来自哪里。灰姑娘从王子身边逃开了，但却跳进了自家的鸽舍。王子就等在那儿，直到灰姑娘的父亲回到家。王子告诉他说，那位不知名的女孩跳进了他家的鸽舍。男人心想：“莫非是灰姑娘？”他们只好找来斧子和锄头，劈开鸽舍，可是却根本没找到人。当继母和两个女儿回到家里时，灰姑娘正穿着那身脏衣服睡在灰堆里呢，一盏油灯在架子上发出昏暗的光。原来灰姑娘当时迅速地从鸽舍后面跳出来，跑到榛树下，脱下漂亮的舞裙，放到坟墓上，让小鸟儿衔走了。然后她又换上那身灰衣服，回到厨房的灰堆里。 She danced till it was evening, and then she wanted to go home.But the King’s son said, “I will go with thee and bear thee company,” for he wished to see to whom the beautiful maiden belonged.She escaped from him, however, and sprang into the pigeon-house.The King’s son waited until her father came, and then he told him that the stranger maiden had leapt into the pigeon-house.The old man thought, “Can it be Cinderella?” and they had to bring him an axe and a pickaxe that he might hew the pigeon-house to pieces, but no one was inside it.And when they got home Cinderella lay in her dirty clothes among the ashes, and a dim little oil-lamp was burning on the mantle-piece, for Cinderella had jumped quickly down from the back of the pigeon-house and had run to the little hazel-tree, and there she had taken off her beautiful clothes and laid them on the grave, and the bird had taken them away again, and then she had placed herself in the kitchen amongst the ashes in her grey gown.
第二天，舞会再度举行。她的父母和两个姐姐都离开后，灰姑娘又来到榛树下，喊道： Next day when the festival began afresh, and her parents and the step-sisters had gone once more, Cinderella went to the hazel-tree and said—
“小树枝，摇一摇，晃一晃！给我一条金丝银线织的裙子吧！” “Shiver and quiver, my little tree, Silver and gold throw down over me.”
这次小鸟儿衔来的裙子比昨天那条还要好看许多。当灰姑娘穿着漂亮的舞裙出现在宴会的时候，人人都惊叹于她的美丽。王子一直在等着她呢，她一到场，王子就牵起她的手跳起舞来，再不跟别的女孩跳了。别人来请灰姑娘跳舞时，王子就说：“她是我的舞伴。”天黑的时候，灰姑娘要回家了，王子跟着她，想知道她是哪家的姑娘。但是她又一次从他身边逃走了，溜进房子后面的花园里。花园里种着一棵漂亮的大梨树，果实累累。灰姑娘爬上了梨树，像松鼠一样敏捷，王子根本没看清她去哪儿了。王子又等啊等，直到灰姑娘的父亲回来后，王子对他说：“那位不知名的女孩又跑不见了，我想她爬上了这棵梨树。”父亲心想：“莫非是灰姑娘？”他找人拿来斧子，砍倒了梨树，可是根本没人在上面。当他们回到厨房时，灰姑娘还是像以前一样，睡在灰堆里。原来她从梨树的另一边跳了下来，在榛树枝下将漂亮的舞裙还给了小鸟，穿回了原来那身灰色的脏衣服。 Then the bird threw down a much more beautiful dress than on the preceding day.And when Cinderella appeared at the festival in this dress, every one was astonished at her beauty.The King’s son had waited until she came, and instantly took her by the hand and danced with no one but her.When others came and invited her, he said, “She is my partner.”When evening came she wished to leave, and the King’s son followed her and wanted to see into which house she went.But she sprang away from him, and into the garden behind the house.Therein stood a beautiful tall tree on which hung the most magnificent pears.She clambered so nimbly between the branches like a squirrel that the King’s son did not know where she was gone.He waited until her father came, and said to him, “The stranger-maiden has escaped from me, and I believe she has climbed up the pear-tree.”The father thought, “Can it be Cinderella?” and had an axe brought and cut the tree down, but no one was on it.And when they got into the kitchen, Cinderella lay there amongst the ashes, as usual, for she had jumped down on the other side of the tree, had taken the beautiful dress to the bird on the little hazel-tree, and put on her grey gown.
第三天，当父母和两个姐姐又出门去参加舞会后，灰姑娘又来到母亲的坟前，对小榛树喊道： On the third day, when the parents and sisters had gone away, Cinderella went once more to her mother’s grave and said to the little tree—
“小树枝，摇一摇，晃一晃！给我一条金丝银线织的裙子吧！” “Shiver and quiver, my little tree, Silver and gold throw down over me.”
这次小鸟儿给她带来的是比前两次更华丽、更漂亮的舞裙，还有一双纯金的舞鞋。当灰姑娘穿着漂亮的裙子出现在宴会时，所有人都惊讶得说不出话来了。王子还是只和她跳舞。如果有别人来请灰姑娘跳舞，他就说：“她是我的舞伴。” And now the bird threw down to her a dress which was more splendid and magnificent than any she had yet had, and the slippers were golden.And when she went to the festival in the dress, no one knew how to speak for astonishment.The King’s son danced with her only, and if any one invited her to dance, he said, “She is my partner.”
天黑了，灰姑娘要回家了，王子还是坚持要送她回去，可是这次灰姑娘还是迅速地溜走了，王子根本就追不上。但王子这次想出了一个办法，他早命人在楼梯上涂满了沥青。所以在灰姑娘跑下楼梯的时候，她左脚的舞鞋就被粘在了楼梯上。王子拾起那只鞋子，发现这只纯金做的舞鞋是那么小巧而精致。第二天一早，王子拿着那只舞鞋，找到了灰姑娘的父亲，对他说：“你的哪个女儿能穿上这只鞋子，我就娶她为妻。”灰姑娘的两个姐姐高兴坏了，因为她们的脚也很漂亮。先是大女儿进屋试穿鞋子，她的母亲站在一旁看着，可是女孩的大脚趾穿不进去，那鞋对她来说太小了。她的母亲递给她一把小刀，说：“把那脚趾头削了吧！反正做了王后也不用走路了。”女孩割下脚趾头，勉强把脚塞进鞋里，忍着痛出来见王子。王子真把她当成了新娘了，和她一起骑着马回宫去了。但他们途中经过了灰姑娘母亲的坟墓，在那棵榛树上，有两只鸽子唱道： When evening came, Cinderella wished to leave, and the King’s son was anxious to go with her, but she escaped from him so quickly that he could not follow her.The King’s son had, however, used a strategem, and had caused the whole staircase to be smeared with pitch, and there, when she ran down, had the maiden’s left slipper remained sticking.The King’s son picked it up, and it was small and dainty, and all golden.Next morning, he went with it to the father, and said to him, “No one shall be my wife but she whose foot this golden slipper fits.”Then were the two sisters glad, for they had pretty feet.The eldest went with the shoe into her room and wanted to try it on, and her mother stood by.But she could not get her big toe into it, and the shoe was too small for her.Then her mother gave her a knife and said, “Cut the toe off; when thou art Queen thou wilt have no more need to go on foot.”The maiden cut the toe off, forced the foot into the shoe, swallowed the pain, and went out to the King’s son.Then he took her on his his horse as his bride and rode away with her.They were, however, obliged to pass the grave, and there, on the hazel-tree, sat the two pigeons and cried,
“转身瞧一瞧，转身瞧一瞧，鞋里冒出血啊， “Turn and peep, turn and peep, There’s blood within the shoe,
她穿这鞋真是太小，真正的新娘还在家里藏！” The shoe it is too small for her, The true bride waits for you.”
王子看了看她的脚，果然看见鲜血如泉涌。他掉转马头，把假新娘送回家，说那不是他真正的新娘，要让另外一个女孩试试鞋子。另一个女孩进屋试鞋，她的脚趾头倒是放得进去，只是脚后跟太大了，塞不进去。她的母亲递给她一把小刀，说：“把脚后跟削掉一块吧！反正做了王后也不用走路了。”女孩把脚后跟削去了一些，勉强将脚塞进鞋里，忍着痛出去见王子。王子把她当成了新娘，骑着马带着她一起回王宫，在经过灰姑娘母亲的坟墓时，两只白鸽又在榛树上唱道： Then he looked at her foot and saw how the blood was streaming from it.He turned his horse round and took the false bride home again, and said she was not the true one, and that the other sister was to put the shoe on.Then this one went into her chamber and got her toes safely into the shoe, but her heel was too large.So her mother gave her a knife and said, “Cut a bit off thy heel; when thou art Queen thou wilt have no more need to go on foot.”The maiden cut a bit off her heel, forced her foot into the shoe, swallowed the pain, and went out to the King’s son.He took her on his horse as his bride, and rode away with her, but when they passed by the hazel-tree, two little pigeons sat on it and cried,
“转身瞧一瞧，转身瞧一瞧，鞋里冒出血来啊， “Turn and peep, turn and peep, There’s blood within the shoe,
她穿这鞋真是太小，真正的新娘还在家里藏！” The shoe it is too small for her, The true bride waits for you.”
王子低头一看，果然有鲜血正从鞋里冒出来，把女孩的白袜子都染红了。王子调转马头，再次将假新娘送回家。“她不是我要找的人，”王子问，“你家里还有其他女儿吗？”“没了，”父亲回答道，“只剩下亡妻留下的一个矮小的独女，一直在厨房做着最脏的活，不过她不可能是你要找的新娘。”王子让他把那个女儿叫来，可是继母阻拦道：“哦，那可不好！她太脏了，见不得人的！”可是王子坚持要见到那个女孩，于是灰姑娘被叫来了。灰姑娘把自己的脸和手都洗净了，走到王子跟前，深施一礼，再从王子手中接过了金舞鞋。她坐在小凳上，脱下厚重的木鞋，把脚伸进金舞鞋里，不大不小正合适。当她站起身来，王子仔细打量着她的脸蛋，认出她就是那位曾经连着三天和他翩翩起舞的女孩，不禁高兴地喊道：“这才是我的新娘啊！”继母和两个女儿惊呆了，气得脸色煞白，而王子则将灰姑娘扶上马，一起回王宫去了。经过榛树的时候，两只白鸽在树上唱道： He looked down at her foot and saw how the blood was running out of her shoe, and how it had stained her white stocking.Then he turned his horse and took the false bride home again.“This also is not the right one,” said he, “have you no other daughter?”“No,” said the man, “There is still a little stunted kitchen-wench which my late wife left behind her, but she cannot possibly be the bride.”The King’s son said he was to send her up to him; but the mother answered, “Oh, no, she is much too dirty, she cannot show herself!”He absolutely insisted on it, and Cinderella had to be called.She first washed her hands and face clean, and then went and bowed down before the King’s son, who gave her the golden shoe.Then she seated herself on a stool, drew her foot out of the heavy wooden shoe, and put it into the slipper, which fitted like a glove.And when she rose up and the King’s son looked at her face he recognized the beautiful maiden who had danced with him and cried, “That is the true bride!”The step-mother and the two sisters were terrified and became pale with rage; he, however, took Cinderella on his horse and rode away with her.As they passed by the hazel-tree, the two white doves cried—
“转身瞧一瞧，转身瞧一瞧，鞋里再没血迹；她穿着刚刚好，真正的新娘终于找着！” “Turn and peep, turn and peep, No blood is in the shoe, The shoe is not too small for her, The true bride rides with you,”
两只白鸽唱完，飞下来，一只停在灰姑娘的左肩，一只停在右肩，不肯离去。 and when they had cried that, the two came flying down and placed themselves on Cinderella’s shoulders, one on the right, the other on the left, and remained sitting there.
在王子和灰姑娘的婚礼上，灰姑娘那两个恶毒的姐姐也来了。她们想攀龙附凤，从灰姑娘这捞点好处。等这对新婚夫妇来到教堂时，那两个女孩中的老大站在右边，老二站在左边，灰姑娘肩上的两只鸽子分别飞去啄瞎了她们的一只眼睛。等新婚夫妇举行完仪式回宫的时候，两个恶毒姐妹中的老大站在了左边，老二站在右边。鸽子又飞下去啄瞎了她们的另一只眼。由于她们的歹毒心肠和欺诈行为，她们最后只能一辈子当瞎子了。 When the wedding with the King’s son had to be celebrated, the two false sisters came and wanted to get into favour with Cinderella and share her good fortune.When the betrothed couple went to church, the elder was at the right side and the younger at the left, and the pigeons pecked out one eye of each of them.Afterwards as they came back, the elder was at the left, and the younger at the right, and then the pigeons pecked out the other eye of each.And thus, for their wickedness and falsehood, they were punished with blindness as long as they lived.
画眉嘴国王 King Thrushbeard
从前有个国王，他有个女儿，非常漂亮，但同样也非常傲慢，觉得没有求婚者能配得上她。她赶走了一个又一个求婚者，还嘲笑讥讽他们。 A King had a daughter who was beautiful beyond all measure, but so proud and haughty withal that no suitor was good enough for her.She sent away one after the other, and ridiculed them as well.
有一次，国王举办了一个盛宴，邀请了四面八方想要来求亲的年轻人。他们被按照身份地位的高低排成一排：首先是国王，接下来依次是公爵，王子，伯爵，男爵和贵族。然后公主开始巡视队伍，但她对每个人都会有些意见。她说第一个太胖：“真是个啤酒桶。”又说第二个太高：“瘦瘦长长没有内涵。”说第三个太矮：“又矮又肥反应迟钝。”说第四个面色太苍白：“白得像个死人一样。”说第五个是个红脸：“像只斗鸡。”说第六个身板不太直：“像火炉边被烤干的绿树枝。” Once the King made a great feast and invited thereto, from far and near, all the young men likely to marry.They were all marshalled in a row according to their rank and standing; first came the kings, then the grand-dukes, then the princes, the earls, the barons, and the gentry.Then the King’s daughter was led through the ranks, but to every one she had some objection to make; one was too fat, “The wine-cask,” she said.Another was too tall, “Long and thin has little in.”The third was too short, “Short and thick is never quick.”The fourth was too pale, “As pale as death.”The fifth too red, “A fighting-cock.”The sixth was not straight enough, “A green log dried behind the stove.”
她对每个人都这样言辞刻薄，但让她最开心的是拿一位善良的国王开玩笑。这位国王站在队伍里相当靠前的位置，他的下巴有点弯。“哈哈！”公主大笑着喊道，“他的下巴长得像画眉嘴！”从此，大家就都叫他“画眉嘴国王”。 So she had something to say against every one, but she made herself especially merry over a good king who stood quite high up in the row, and whose chin had grown a little crooked.“Well,” she cried and laughed, “he has a chin like a thrush’s beak!” and from that time he got the name of King Thrushbeard.
但老国王见到自己的女儿只会嘲笑别人，并且对聚在这里的求婚者一个都看不上，他非常生气，发誓要将女儿许配给第一个来宫门前的乞丐。 But the old King, when he saw that his daugher did nothing but mock the people, and despised all the suitors who were gathered there, was very angry, and swore that she should have for her husband the very first beggar that came to his doors.
几天之后，一个拉小提琴的流浪汉来到窗下卖唱，想求得一点施舍。老国王听到了，便说：“让他进来。”于是流浪汉进来了，穿着破破烂烂的脏衣服，在国王和公主面前唱歌。唱完后，他便讨要赏赐。老国王说：“你的歌声让我很满意，所以我打算把我的女儿嫁给你为妻。” A few days afterwards a fiddler came and sang beneath the windows, trying to earn a small alms.When the King heard him he said, “Let him come up.”So the fiddler came in, in his dirty, ragged clothes, and sang before the King and his daughter, and when he had ended he asked for a trifling gift.The King said, “Your song has pleased me so well that I will give you my daughter there, to wife.”
公主吓得发抖，然而老国王却说：“我发过誓要将你许给第一个来宫前乞讨的乞丐，我会信守诺言的。”公主此时说什么都没用了。牧师很快就被召来了，公主不得不当场就和流浪汉举行了婚礼。婚礼结束后，老国王说：“现在你已经是乞丐的妻子了，再留在我的王宫里成何体统？你还是跟你的丈夫走吧。” The King’s daughter shuddered, but the King said, “I have taken an oath to give you to the very first beggar-man, and I will keep it.”All she could say was in vain; the priest was brought, and she had to let herself be wedded to the fiddler on the spot.When that was done the King said, “Now it is not proper for you, a beggar-woman, to stay any longer in my palace, you may just go away with your husband.”
乞丐拉着公主的手走出王宫，公主只得无奈地跟着他走。走了一会，他们来到一片大森林，公主问道：“这么美的大森林是谁的啊？”“是画眉嘴国王的。如果你当初嫁给他，早就是你的了。”“唉，我真是命苦啊！如果当初嫁给画眉嘴国王就好了！” The beggar-man led her out by the hand, and she was obliged to walk away on foot with him.When they came to a large forest she asked, “To whom does that beautiful forest belong?”“It belongs to King Thrushbeard; if you had taken him, it would have been yours.”“Ah, unhappy girl that I am, if I had but taken King Thrushbeard!”
然后他们又经过一片草地，公主又问：“这么漂亮的草地是谁的啊？”“是画眉嘴国王的。如果你当初嫁给他，早就是你的了。”“唉，我真是命苦啊！如果当初嫁给画眉嘴国王就好了！” Afterwards they came to a meadow, and she asked again, “To whom does this beautiful green meadow belong?”“It belongs to King Thrushbeard; if you had taken him, it would have been yours.”“Ah, unhappy girl that I am, if I had but taken King Thrushbeard!”
不久，两人来到一个大城市，公主又问：“这么繁华的大城市是谁的啊？”“是画眉嘴国王的。如果你当初嫁给他，早就是你的了。”“唉，我真是命苦啊！如果当初嫁了画眉嘴国王就好了！” Then they came to a large town, and she asked again, “To whom does this fine large town belong?”“It belongs to King Thrushbeard; if you had taken him, it would have been yours.”“Ah, unhappy girl that I am, if I had but taken King Thrushbeard!”
“你这么说我可不乐意了。”乞丐说，“你老想着要嫁给别人，难道我待你不够好吗？”最后，他们来到一个小茅屋前，公主说道：“我的天哪！这么小的房子！这间简陋破烂的房子是谁的啊？”乞丐回答道：“这是我的房子，也是你的了。以后就在这儿过日子。” “It does not please me,” said the fiddler, “to hear you always wishing for another husband; am I not good enough for you?”At last they came to a very little hut, and she said, “Oh goodness!what a small house; to whom does this miserable, mean hovel belong?”The fiddler answered, “That is my house and yours, where we shall live together.”
那扇门很低，公主得弯下腰才能进去。“仆人呢？”公主问。“哪来的仆人？”乞丐回答，“什么都得自己干。赶紧去生火，然后烧水做饭，我实在累了。”可是公主根本不懂什么烧火做饭，乞丐只得自己动手，凑合着把活儿干完了。两人吃完这顿勉强填饱肚子的饭，就上床睡觉了。但第二天一大早，乞丐就叫醒公主，让她去做家务。 She had to stoop in order to go in at the low door.“Where are the servants?” said the King’s daughter.“What servants?” answered the beggar-man; “you must yourself do what you wish to have done.Just make a fire at once, and set on water to cook my supper, I am quite tired.”But the King’s daughter knew nothing about lighting fires or cooking, and the beggar-man had to lend a hand himself to get anything fairly done.When they had finished their scanty meal they went to bed; but he forced her to get up quite early in the morning in order to look after the house.
两人就这么凑合着过了几天，最后终于一无所有了。乞丐说：“我的妻子， 我们不能再像这样光吃饭不挣钱了。你去编点柳筐卖吧。”于是他出门砍了些柳条拿回家中。公主便学着编柳筐，但她细嫩的小手被粗糙的柳条扎得伤痕累累。 For a few days they lived in this way as well as might be, and came to the end of all their provisions.Then the man said, “Wife, we cannot go on any longer eating and drinking here and earning nothing.You weave baskets.”He went out, cut some willows, and brought them home.Then she began to weave, but the tough willows wounded her delicate hands.
“看来不行！”乞丐说，“你还是学学纺纱吧，或许你合适做这个。”公主便坐下，学着纺纱，可是不久她柔嫩的手指就被粗线割伤了，鲜血直流。“唉！”乞丐说，“你什么都干不来，娶了你可真是赔本买卖。现在我去试着弄点瓦罐和陶器，你就去集市里坐在那儿卖陶器好了。”“天哪！”公主心想，“要是我们国家的人来这个集市买东西，看见我坐在那儿卖罐子，他们会怎样笑话我啊？”可是没办法，毕竟要吃饭啊，公主别无选择。 “I see that this will not do,” said the man; “you had better spin, perhaps you can do that better.”She sat down and tried to spin, but the hard thread soon cut her soft fingers so that the blood ran down.“See,” said the man, “you are fit for no sort of work; I have made a bad bargain with you.Now I will try to make a business with pots and earthenware; you must sit in the market-place and sell the ware.”“Alas,” thought she, “if any of the people from my father’s kingdom come to the market and see me sitting there, selling, how they will mock me?”But it was of no use, she had to yield unless she chose to die of hunger.
第一回的买卖做得不错，公主长得漂亮，人们乐意来买她的货，人们也不讨价还价，有很多人甚至光给钱不拿货呢。夫妻俩就靠着这次挣到的钱维持了一段时间的生活。有一天，丈夫又进了一大批新陶器。公主坐在集市一角，周围摆满了货物，等着买主。突然，一个醉醺醺的轻骑兵骑着马，向摊子直冲了过来。马直接从陶器上踏过，陶器全都成了碎片。公主大哭起来，害怕得不知如何是好。“天哪！我该怎么办啊？”她哭道，“我的丈夫不知道要怎样骂我了！” For the first time she succeeded well, for the people were glad to buy the woman’s wares because she was good-looking, and they paid her what she asked; many even gave her the money and left the pots with her as well.So they lived on what she had earned as long as it lasted, then the husband bought a lot of new crockery.With this she sat down at the corner of the market-place, and set it out round about her ready for sale.But suddenly there came a drunken hussar galloping along, and he rode right amongst the pots so that they were all broken into a thousand bits.She began to weep, and did now know what to do for fear.“Alas!what will happen to me?” cried she; “what will my husband say to this?”
她跑回家，告诉了乞丐这不幸的遭遇。“谁会在集市的角落里卖陶器啊？”乞丐说，“哭什么呀？我很明白你是一点用都没有！所以我去王宫打听过了，问他们需不需要一个厨娘，他们已经答应要你了，这样你就可以吃到免费的饭了。” She ran home and told him of the misfortune.“Who would seat herself at a corner of the market-place with crockery?” said the man; “leave off crying, I see very well that you cannot do any ordinary work, so I have been to our King’s palace and have asked whether they cannot find a place for a kitchen-maid, and they have promised me to take you; in that way you will get your food for nothing.”
于是国王的女儿就去王宫做厨娘了。她不得不低声下气地帮厨师们打杂，干的是最脏的活儿。她在衣服的两个兜里一边各拴了一个小罐子，好把残汤剩饭带回家。她和乞丐就靠这个维持生活。 The King’s daughter was now a kitchen-maid, and had to be at the cook’s beck and call, and do the dirtiest work.In both her pockets she fastened a little jar, in which she took home her share of the leavings, and upon this they lived.
有一天，国王的大儿子要举办婚礼，于是这个可怜的女人走到大厅门口，向大厅里张望。大厅里灯火通明。嘉宾们进了大厅，一个比一个好看，都穿得华丽非凡。公主想起自己的命运，心里非常难过。她痛恨起自己当初的狂妄和无礼，使自己今天落到如此卑微而贫困的境地。 It happened that the wedding of the King’s eldest son was to be celebrated, so the poor woman went up and placed herself by the door of the hall to look on.When all the candles were lit, and people, each more beautiful than the other, entered, and all was full of pomp and splendour, she thought of her lot with a sad heart, and cursed the pride and haughtiness which had humbled her and brought her to so great poverty.
仆人们端着美味佳肴进进出出，她却只能闻着香气。仆人们有时会扔给她一点食物，她都装进罐子里，准备带回家。 The smell of the delicious dishes which were being taken in and out reached her, and now and then the servants threw her a few morsels of them: these she put in her jars to take home.
这时，王子进来了，他穿着绫罗绸缎，脖子上戴着金项链。当他看见站在门前的这位美人，就牵起他的手，想和他跳舞。但是公主却拒绝了，身子因害怕而后退。因为她发现这位王子正是曾向她求亲的画眉嘴国王，那时她轻蔑地把他赶走了。公主的挣扎都是白费，她被他拉着手拽进了宴会大厅，突然她的衣兜被扯破了，罐子摔落在地，汤洒了出来，残羹剩饭溅得满地都是。众人见到如此情景，都大声嘲笑起来。公主羞愧难当，恨不能挖个地缝钻进去。她夺门而逃，一个男子在楼梯上把她截住，又将她带回了大厅，她定睛一看，还是那个画眉嘴国王。国王亲切地对她说：“别害怕！我，还有那个和你一起住在破茅屋里的乞丐，其实是同一个人。正是因为爱你，我才那么乔装打扮。那个踩碎你陶器的轻骑兵也是我。我所做的一切都是为了帮你改掉你傲慢无礼的德性，也是要你为当年嘲弄我付出代价。” All at once the King’s son entered, clothed in velvet and silk, with gold chains about his neck.And when he saw the beautiful woman standing by the door he seized her by the hand, and would have danced with her; but she refused and shrank with fear, for she saw that it was King Thrushbeard, her suitor whom she had driven away with scorn.Her struggles were of no avail, he drew her into the hall; but the string by which her pockets were hung broke, the pots fell down, the soup ran out, and the scraps were scattered all about.And when the people saw it, there arose general laughter and derision, and she was so ashamed that she would rather have been a thousand fathoms below the ground.She sprang to the door and would have run away, but on the stairs a man caught her and brought her back; and when she looked at him it was King Thrushbeard again.He said to her kindly, “Do not be afraid, I and the fiddler who has been living with you in that wretched hovel are one.For love of you I disguised myself so; and I also was the hussar who rode through your crockery.This was all done to humble your proud spirit, and to punish you for the insolence with which you mocked me.”
公主失声痛哭，说：“我是犯了大错的人，不配做你的妻子啊。”但是国王却说：“别难过了，苦日子已经过去了。现在来庆祝我们的婚礼吧。”宫女们走过来，给她穿上最华美的裙子。这时，她的父亲老国王以及王公大臣们也来了，都祝愿公主和画眉嘴国王婚姻幸福。欢乐的宴会正式开始了。真希望我和亲爱的读者们也能在那里！ Then she wept bitterly and said, “I have done great wrong, and am not worthy to be your wife.”But he said, “Be comforted, the evil days are past; now we will celebrate our wedding.”Then the maids-in-waiting came and put on her the most splendid clothing, and her father and his whole court came and wished her happiness in her marriage with King Thrushbeard, and the joy now began in earnest.I wish you and I had been there too.
圣母玛利亚抚养的孩子 Our Lady’s Child
在一片大森林前，住着一位樵夫和他的妻子，他们有一个三岁的独生女。可是，由于家里太贫困，他们连面包也吃不上了，更不知道怎样养活女儿。一天早上，樵夫满腹心事地到森林里干活。他正在砍柴，面前忽然出现一位漂亮的高个子女人，她头戴着一顶闪闪发光的王冠，对樵夫说：“我是圣母玛利亚，耶稣基督的母亲。你们生活艰苦贫困，把孩子交给我吧，我愿意带她走，做她的母亲，关心她。”樵夫同意了，便将孩子带来交给了圣母玛利亚，她带着女孩飞上了天堂。女孩在天堂过着幸福的生活，她吃的是甜面包，喝的是甜牛奶，穿的衣服都是金子做的，还有小天使们陪伴着玩耍。女孩十四岁那年，一次，圣母玛利亚将她叫到面前，说道：“亲爱的孩子，我要出一趟远门，所以把开启天堂十三道大门的钥匙交给你来掌管。你可以打开十二道门，欣赏其中的壮美，但是，这把小钥匙能打开的那第十三道门，你是不能碰的。你要当心，别打开它，否则会给自己带来灾祸。”女孩答应会听话的，圣母玛利亚走后，她便开始一间间地去欣赏天堂的美景。她每天打开一扇门，直到最后，十二扇门都被她开过了。每道门里都坐着一个门徒，周身发出强光，女孩欣喜地看着这幕光辉美妙的景象，经常陪伴女孩玩的小天使们也和女孩一起高兴。后来，只剩下第十三道门没被打开过，女孩很想知道门后到底藏着什么，便对天使们说：“我不会敞开这道门，我也不会进去，只是打开一条缝隙，那样我们就能通过门缝往里瞧一瞧了。”小天使说：“噢，不要啊，那样做是违反戒律的。圣母玛利亚不允许打开那道门，那会给你带来灾祸的。”女孩沉默了，可她心里的欲望依然强烈，让她备受折磨，一刻不得安宁。一次，天使们都不在，女孩心想：“现在就剩下我自己了，我要打开门瞧一下。我这样做的话也没人会知道的。”她找出钥匙拿在手里，插进锁孔里拧开了锁。于是，门被打开了，她看到圣父、圣子和圣灵三位一体正坐在火焰上。她呆愣了片刻，惊讶地望着里面的一切。接着她伸出手指碰了碰火光，她的手指立即变成了金子。女孩随即非常地害怕。她猛地关上那扇门跑开了。可她还是害怕，也没有心思做其他事情，只听心脏怦怦跳个不停，手指上的金子也消失不掉，她又是搓又是洗的，可就是弄不掉。 Hard by a great forest dwelt a woodcutter with his wife, who had an only child, a little girl three years old.They were so poor, however, that they no longer had daily bread, and did not know how to get food for her.One morning the woodcutter went out sorrowfully to his work in the forest, and while he was cutting wood, suddenly there stood before him a tall and beautiful woman with a crown of shining stars on her head, who said to him, “I am the Virgin Mary, mother of the child Jesus.Thou art poor and needy, bring thy child to me, I will take her with me and be her mother, and care for her.”The woodcutter obeyed, brought his child, and gave her to the Virgin Mary, who took her up to heaven with her.There the child fared well, ate sugar cakes, and drank sweet milk, and her clothes were of gold, and the little angels played with her.And when she was fourteen years of age, the Virgin Mary called her one day and said, “Dear child, I am about to make a long journey, so take into thy keeping the keys of the thirteen doors of heaven.Twelve of these thou mayest open, and behold the glory which is within them, but the thirteenth, to which this little key belongs, is forbidden thee.Beware of opening it, or thou wilt bring misery on thyself.”The girl promised to be obedient, and when the Virgin Mary was gone, she began to examine the dwellings of the kingdom of heaven.Each day she opened one of them, until she had made the round of the twelve.In each of them sat one of the Apostles in the midst of a great light, and she rejoiced in all the magnificence and splendour, and the little angels who always accompanied her rejoiced with her.Then the forbidden door alone remained, and she felt a great desire to know what could be hidden behind it, and said to the angels, “I will not quite open it, and I will not go inside it, but I will unlock it so that we can just see a little through the opening.”“Oh no,” said the little angels, “that would be a sin.The Virgin Mary has forbidden it, and it might easily cause thy unhappiness.”Then she was silent, but the desire in her heart was not stilled, but gnawed there and tormented her, and let her have no rest.And once when the angels had all gone out, she thought, “Now I am quite alone, and I could peep in.If I do it, no one will ever know.”She sought out the key, and when she had got it in her hand, she put it in the lock, and when she had put it in, she turned it round as well.Then the door sprang open, and she saw there the Trinity sitting in fire and splendour.She stayed there awhile, and looked at everything in amazement; then she touched the light a little with her finger, and her finger became quite golden.Immediately a great fear fell on her.She shut the door violently, and ran away.Her terror too would not quit her, let her do what she might, and her heart beat continually and would not be still; the gold too stayed on her finger, and would not go away, let her rub it and wash it never so much.
不久后，圣母利亚出远门回来了。她把女孩叫到面前，跟她要回天堂门的钥匙。女孩把钥匙递给她的时候，圣母望着她的眼睛，说道：“你是不是打开第十三道门了？”女孩答道：“没有。”圣母把手放到女孩胸前，感到她心跳得很快，便明白了女孩违背了她的命令，打开了那道门。于是，她再次问道：“你真的没有打开那道门吗？”女孩第二次说道：“没有。”圣母又看到了女孩那根因触碰天光而变成金子的手指，她便清楚了女孩已违反了戒律，便第三次问道：“你真的没有打开过吗？”女孩第三次答道：“没有。”于是，圣母玛利亚说：“你没有听我的话，不仅如此，你还对我撒谎，你不配再呆在天堂了。” It was not long before the Virgin Mary came back from her journey.She called the girl before her, and asked to have the keys of heaven back.When the maiden gave her the bunch, the Virgin looked into her eyes and said, “Hast thou not opened the thirteenth door also?”“No,” she replied.Then she laid her hand on the girl’s heart, and felt how it beat and beat, and saw right well that she had disobeyed her order and had opened the door.Then she said once again, “Art thou certain that thou hast not done it?”“Yes,” said the girl, for the second time.Then she perceived the finger which had become golden from touching the fire of heaven, and saw well that the child had sinned, and said for the third time “Hast thou not done it?”“No,” said the girl for the third time.Then said the Virgin Mary, “Thou hast not obeyed me, and besides that thou hast lied, thou art no longer worthy to be in heaven.”
后来，女孩就渐渐睡熟了，她醒来时已是躺在人间的一片荒野里。她想喊叫，却发不出声音。女孩跳起来想跑，却发现四周都是无法穿越的茂密荆棘筑成的篱笆，拦住了她的去路。女孩被困在了荒野里，那里长着一棵古老的空心树，这就成了她的居所。夜晚来临时，她便钻到树洞里过夜。暴雨天气时，她也钻到里面去躲避风雨。但这毕竟是很不幸的生活啊，每当想起过去住在天堂的幸福时光，还有和小天使们一起玩耍的情景，她就会心酸地哭泣。女孩只能靠草根和野果维持生活，这些是她仅能找到的充饥之物了。秋天的时候，她就拾落下来的胡桃和树叶，把它们收藏在树洞里。这些胡桃就成了她冬天的食物，当雪花飞舞、四处结冰的时候，她就像只可怜的小动物似的躲在树叶中间以免被冻僵。不久后，她的衣服也穿破了，碎布一点一点地掉下来。不过，很快天气就转暖了，女孩走出树洞坐到大树跟前，她的长发像一件披风似的披散在身上。她就这样度过了一年又一年，深切感受到了世间的痛苦和艰辛。又到了树木发出新芽的时候，一天，当地的国王到森林里狩猎，追赶一头小鹿。可小鹿跑进灌木丛中躲了起来，国王跳下马，用剑把灌木劈开，给自己砍出了一条通路。他最后走进去的时候，看到一个非常漂亮的女孩正坐在树下。她金色的头发一直垂到脚下，盖住了她的身体。国王一动不动地站在那里，满是惊讶地看着女孩，他问女孩：“你是谁？你为什么会坐在这里呢？” Then the girl fell into a deep sleep, and when she awoke she lay on the earth below, and in the midst of a wilderness.She wanted to cry out, but she could bring forth no sound.She sprang up and wanted to run away, but whithersoever she turned herself, she was continually held back by thick hedges of thorns through which she could not break.In the desert, in which she was imprisoned, there stood an old hollow tree, and this had to be her dwelling place.Into this she crept when night came, and here she slept.Here, too, she found a shelter from storm and rain, but it was a miserable life, and bitterly did she weep when she remembered how happy she had been in heaven, and how the angels had played with her.Roots and wild berries were her only food, and for these she sought as far as she could go.In the autumn she picked up the fallen nuts and leaves, and carried them into the hole.The nuts were her food in winter, and when snow and ice came, she crept amongst the leaves like a poor little animal that she might not freeze.Before long her clothes were all torn, and one bit of them after another fell off her.As soon, however, as the sun shone warm again, she went out and sat in front of the tree, and her long hair covered her on all sides like a mantle.Thus she sat year after year, and felt the pain and the misery of the world.One day, when the trees were once more clothed in fresh green, the King of the country was hunting in the forest, and followed a roe, and as it had fled into the thicket which shut in this part of the forest, he got off his horse, tore the bushes asunder, and cut himself a path with his sword.When he had at last forced his way through, he saw a wonderfully beautiful maiden sitting under the tree; and she sat there and was entirely covered with her golden hair down to her very feet.He stood still and looked at her full of surprise, then he spoke to her and said, “Who art thou? Why art thou sitting here in the wilderness?”
可女孩并没有回答，因为她已无法张开嘴。国王继续问道：“你愿意和我一起回我的王宫吗？”这次，女孩只是轻轻点了点头。国王把女孩抱到马背上，和她一起骑马回宫去。回到宫里后，国王命人给女孩穿上漂亮的衣服，还送给她很多礼物。虽然女孩不能说话，可她仍然是那么地漂亮迷人，国王深深地爱上了她，不久后，他就娶女孩为妻了。 But she gave no answer, for she could not open her mouth.The King continued, “Wilt thou go with me to my castle?”Then she just nodded her head a little.The King took her in his arms, carried her to his horse, and rode home with her, and when he reached the royal castle he caused her to be dressed in beautiful garments, and gave her all things in abundance.Although she could not speak, she was still so beautiful and charming that he began to love her with all his heart, and it was not long before he married her.
大约过了一年的时间，王后生下了一个男婴。晚上她独自一人躺在床上的时候，圣母玛利亚出现了，说道：“如果你告诉我实情，承认你打开过第十三道门，那我就让你张开嘴，恢复说话能力。可如果你还要坚持错下去，固执地否认，那我就把你新出生的婴儿抱走。”圣母准许王后说话了，可她仍旧不悔改，说道：“没有，我没有打开第十三道门。”于是，圣母玛利亚从王后怀里抱走了新生儿，然后就消失了。第二天早上，大家找不到孩子了，人们便悄声议论着说，王后是个食人魔，她吃掉了自己的孩子。王后听到了这些议论，却无法为自己辩解，还好国王并不相信这些流言，因为他深爱着王后。 After a year or so had passed, the Queen brought a son into the world.Thereupon the Virgin Mary appeared to her in the night when she lay in her bed alone, and said, “If thou wilt tell the truth and confess that thou didst unlock the forbidden door, I will open thy mouth and give thee back thy speech, but if thou perseverest in thy sin, and deniest obstinately, I will take thy new born child away with me.”Then the queen was permitted to answer, but she remained hard, and said, “No, I did not open the forbidden door;” and the Virgin Mary took the new born child from her arms, and vanished with it.Next morning when the child was not to be found, it was whispered among the people that the Queen was a man-eater, and had killed her own child.She heard all this and could say nothing to the contrary, but the King would not believe it, for he loved her so much.
一年过去了，王后再次产下一个男婴，当晚圣母玛利亚又出现了，她问道：“如果你承认自己打开过第十三道门，我就把孩子还给你，让你可以开口说话。如果你还是不知悔改、继续否认，那我就把这个新生儿也带走。”可王后依然说：“没有，我没有打开第十三道门。”圣母玛利亚又从她怀里抱走孩子，消失了。第二天早上，人们发现这个婴儿又不见了，便大声议论，说王后吃掉了婴儿，大臣们也要求给王后治罪。然而，国王还是深爱着她，他不相信传言，命令大臣们不准再提及此事，否则格杀勿论。 When a year had gone by the Queen again bore a son, and in the night the Virgin Mary again came to her, and said, “If thou wilt confess that thou openedst the forbidden door, I will give thee thy child back and untie thy tongue; but if you continuest in sin and deniest it, I will take away with me this new child also.”Then the Queen again said, “No, I did not open the forbidden door;” and the Virgin took the child out of her arms, and away with her to heaven.Next morning, when this child also had disappeared, the people declared quite loudly that the Queen had devoured it, and the King’s councillors demanded that she should be brought to justice.The King, however, loved her so dearly that he would not believe it, and commanded the councillors under pain of death not to say any more about it.
又过去一年，王后产下一个漂亮的女婴，夜里，圣母玛利亚第三次来到她面前，说道：“随我来。”她拉着王后来到了天堂，让她看看自己的两个儿子，他们朝王后微笑，正在玩着地球仪。王后高兴极了，圣母玛利亚说：“你还是不肯心软吗？如果你肯承认自己打开了第十三道门，我就把两个儿子还给你。”可是，王后第三次答道：“没有，我没打开过第十三道门。”于是，圣母又将她送回人间，同样地，抱走了她的第三个孩子。 The following year the Queen gave birth to a beautiful little daughter, and for the third time the Virgin Mary appeared to her in the night and said, “Follow me.”She took the Queen by the hand and led her to heaven, and showed her there her two eldest children, who smiled at her, and were playing with the ball of the world.When the Queen rejoiced thereat, the Virgin Mary said, “Is thy heart not yet softened?If thou wilt own that thou openedst the forbidden door, I will give thee back thy two little sons.”But for the third time the Queen answered, “No, I did not open the forbidden door.”Then the Virgin let her sink down to earth once more, and took from her likewise her third child.
第二天早上，孩子消失的消息又传到了百姓的耳朵里，所有人都大喊道：“王后是个食人魔。她必须要受到惩罚。”国王也无法再阻止大臣们。于是，王后接受了审判，由于她无法说话，不能为自己辩解，她被判在柴堆上烧死。柴堆垒好了，王后被捆在木桩上，大火在她周围燃烧起来，这时王后那高傲的坚冰才被融化，她心中满是悔恨，心想：“要是我在死前承认自己的错误就好了。”因此，她能够开口说话了，便大声喊道：“是的，圣母玛利亚，我打开了那道门。”天空立刻降起大雨熄灭了火焰，她的头上出现一道亮光，圣母玛利亚身边跟着王后的两个儿子，怀里抱着那个新生的女儿下来了。她对王后和蔼地说道：“承认自己的过错并能悔改的人都会得到宽恕的。”然后，她把三个孩子还给了王后，也恢复了她说话的能力，让王后从此过上了幸福的生活。 Next morning, when the loss was reported abroad, all the people cried loudly, “The Queen is a man-eater. She must be judged,”And the King was no longer able to restrain his councillors.Thereupon a trial was held, and as she could not answer, and defend herself, she was condemned to be burnt alive.The wood was got together, and when she was fast bound to the stake, and the fire began to burn round about her, the hard ice of pride melted, her heart was moved by repentance, and she thought, “If I could but confess before my death that I opened the door.”Then her voice came back to her, and she cried out loudly, “Yes, Mary, I did it;” and straight way rain fell from the sky and extinguished the flames of fire, and a light broke forth above her, and the Virgin Mary descended with the two little sons by her side, and the new-born daughter in her arms.She spoke kindly to her, and said, “He who repents his sin and acknowledges it, is forgiven.”Then she gave her the three children, untied her tongue, and granted her happiness for her whole life.
莴笋姑娘 Rapunzel
从前有一对夫妇，他们一直希望能生一个孩子，却总是没能如愿。后来，上帝满足了他们的心愿，妻子怀孕了。夫妇俩房子的后墙上有一扇窗户，透过那扇窗户能看到一座满是漂亮花草的整洁花园。可是，花园被高墙围住了，没人敢爬进去，因为花园的主人是一个有着巨大魔力、让世人都害怕的女巫。一天，女人站在窗前望着下面的花园，她看到一块地里长着很漂亮的莴笋，莴笋看起来是那么新鲜翠绿，女人很想吃几口。她想吃莴笋的欲望越来越强烈，可由于没办法得到，女人日渐消瘦下去，看起来又苍白又痛苦。于是，丈夫很担心，便问道：“亲爱的妻子，你这是怎么了？”妻子回答说：“唉，我要是吃不到下面花园里的莴笋，我就要死了。”丈夫深爱着妻子，他心想：“我不能让妻子送命，不管付出什么代价，我也要给她偷一点莴笋回来。”晚上，他爬下高墙来到了女巫的花园里，匆匆采了一把莴笋，带给了妻子。妻子立即就调制好莴笋，有滋有味地吃起来。可是，妻子觉得太好吃了，第二天她比以前还更想吃了。丈夫为了安慰妻子，只得再去一次花园。他借着暮色爬下了高墙，可刚着地，他就惊恐地发现女巫正站在他面前。女巫满脸愤怒地问道：“你怎么敢爬到我的花园里偷莴笋？你要付出代价的！” There were once a man and a woman who had long in vain wished for a child.At length the woman hoped that God was about to grant her desire.These people had a little window at the back of their house from which a splendid garden could be seen, which was full of the most beautiful flowers and herbs.It was, however, surrounded by a high wall, and no one dared to go into it because it belonged to an enchantress, who had great power and was dreaded by all the world.One day the woman was standing by this window and looking down into the garden, when she saw a bed which was planted with the most beautiful rampion (rapunzel), and it looked so fresh and green that she longed for it, and had the greatest desire to eat some.This desire increased every day, and as she knew that she could not get any of it, she quite pined away, and looked pale and miserable.Then her husband was alarmed, and asked, “What aileth thee, dear wife?”“Ah,” she replied, “if I can’t get some of the rampion, which is in the garden behind our house, to eat, I shall die.”The man, who loved her, thought, “Sooner than let thy wife die, bring her some of the rampion thyself, let it cost thee what it will.”In the twilight of the evening, he clambered down over the wall into the garden of the enchantress, hastily clutched a handful of rampion, and took it to his wife.She at once made herself a salad of it, and ate it with much relish.She, however, liked it so much—so very much, that the next day she longed for it three times as much as before.If he was to have any rest, her husband must once more descend into the garden.In the gloom of evening, therefore, he let himself down again; but when he had clambered down the wall he was terribly afraid, for he saw the enchantress standing before him.“How canst thou dare,” said she with angry look, “to descend into my garden and steal my rampion like a thief? Thou shalt suffer for it!”
男人答道：“啊，请可怜可怜我吧，我也是迫不得已才这样做的。我的妻子透过窗户看到了你种的莴笋，她非常想吃，要是吃不到她会死的。”女巫听后，怒火渐渐平息了，她对男人说：“如果真是你说的这种情况，你可以随便来采莴笋，我只有一个条件，你必须要把你妻子生下的孩子给我，我会好好对待他，会像母亲一样照顾他。”男人很害怕，便一口答应了女巫的要求。女人到了临产的时候，女巫马上出现了，还给女孩取名叫“莴笋”，然后带她离开了。 “Ah,” answered he, “let mercy take the place of justice, I only made up my mind to do it out of necessity.My wife saw your rampion from the window, and felt such a longing for it that she would have died if she had not got some to eat.”Then the enchantress allowed her anger to be softened, and said to him, “If the case be as thou sayest, I will allow thee to take away with thee as much rampion as thou wilt, only I make one condition, thou must give me the child which thy wife will bring into the world; it shall be well treated, and I will care for it like a mother.”The man in his terror consented to everything, and when the woman was brought to bed, the enchantress appeared at once, gave the child the name of Rapunzel, and took it away with her.
莴笋慢慢长大，成了天底下最漂亮的女孩。在她十二岁那年，女巫将她关进了森林中的一座高塔里，高塔既没有楼梯也没有门，只在塔顶上开了一扇小窗户。女巫想进塔的时候，就会站在塔下，高喊：“莴笋，莴笋，放下你的长发，让我上去。” Rapunzel grew into the most beautiful child beneath the sun.When she was twelve years old, the enchantress shut her into a tower, which lay in a forest, and had neither stairs nor door, but quite at the top was a little window.When the enchantress wanted to go in, she placed herself beneath it and cried,“Rapunzel, Rapunzel, Let down thy hair to me.”
莴笋长着一头漂亮的长发，长发如同金线一般，她听到女巫的喊声后便解开长辫子，将长发绕到上面窗户的一个挂钩上，长发就向下垂下两厄尔来长，女巫顺着它就可以爬进塔里了。 Rapunzel had magnificent long hair, fine as spun gold, and when she heard the voice of the enchantress she unfastened her braided tresses, wound them round one of the hooks of the window above, and then the hair fell twenty ells down, and the enchantress climbed up by it.
过了一两年，一个王子来到森林里，他恰巧骑马经过高塔。这时，传来一阵迷人的歌声，王子静静地驻足听起歌来。那正是寂寞的莴笋为了打发时间而唱出的甜美歌声。王子想爬上去见见女孩，便四处寻找塔门，可一个都找不到。他只好骑马回宫了，可那歌声深深地触动了王子的心灵，他每日都要到森林里去听女孩唱歌。一次，他正站在树下时，女巫走了过来，王子听女巫喊道：“莴笋，莴笋，放下长发，让我上去吧。”于是，莴笋垂下长发，女巫顺着长发爬了上去。王子说道：“如果这就是通往塔顶的梯子，那我也要碰碰运气了。”第二天夜幕降临时，王子来到塔前，喊道：“莴笋，莴笋，放下长发吧。”长发立即垂下来，王子便顺着长发攀了上去。起初，莴笋看到他很害怕，因为她从未见过一个男子。但王子像朋友一般友好地和她交谈，还告诉她说，自己被歌声深深地触动了，内心不得安宁，只好上来看她一眼。莴笋不再害怕了，王子问她是否愿意嫁给他，莴笋见王子又年轻又英俊，便心想：“他一定比教母还爱我。”便答应了王子，把手放到了王子手中。莴笋说：“我很愿意跟你走，可我不知道怎样才能爬下去。你每次来时都给我带一卷丝线吧，我用丝线编一架梯子，梯子编好后我就能下去了，然后你带我骑马离开。”他们约定好，王子每天夜里到高塔上来，因为女巫总是在白天来。女巫并未察觉到异常，一次，莴笋对她说：“教母，你说为什么我拉你上来比拉那个王子上来更费力呢？——他一下子就爬上来了。” After a year or two, it came to pass that the King’s son rode through the forest and went by the tower.Then he heard a song, which was so charming that he stood still and listened.This was Rapunzel, who in her solitude passed her time in letting her sweet voice resound.The King’s son wanted to climb up to her, and looked for the door of the tower, but none was to be found.He rode home, but the singing had so deeply touched his heart, that every day he went out into the forest and listened to it.Once when he was thus standing behind a tree, he saw that an enchantress came there, and he heard how she cried,“Rapunzel, Rapunzel, Let down thy hair.”Then Rapunzel let down the braids of her hair, and the enchantress climbed up to her.“If that is the ladder by which one mounts, I will for once try my fortune,” said he, and the next day when it began to grow dark, he went to the tower and cried,“Rapunzel, Rapunzel, Let down thy hair.”Immediately the hair fell down and the King’s son climbed up.At first Rapunzel was terribly frightened when a man such as her eyes had never yet beheld, came to her; but the King’s son began to talk to her quite like a friend, and told her that his heart had been so stirred that it had let him have no rest, and he had been forced to see her.Then Rapunzel lost her fear, and when he asked her if she would take him for her husband, and she saw that he was young and handsome, she thought, “He will love me more than old Dame Gothel does;” and she said yes, and laid her hand in his.She said, “I will willingly go away with thee, but I do not know how to get down.Bring with thee a skein of silk every time that thou comest, and I will weave a ladder with it, and when that is ready I will descend, and thou wilt take me on thy horse.”They agreed that until that time he should come to her every evening, for the old woman came by day.The enchantress remarked nothing of this, until once Rapunzel said to her, “Tell me, Dame Gothel, how it happens that you are so much heavier for me to draw up than the young King’s son—he is with me in a moment.”
“啊！你这个坏孩子。”女巫喊道，“你在说什么？我以为把你同整个世界都隔离开了，你竟欺骗我。”女巫生气地拽住莴笋漂亮的长发，在自己左手上缠绕了两圈，右手抓起一把剪刀，咔嚓一声，莴笋的长发被剪断了，飘落到地上。女巫无情地把可怜的莴笋流放到一片荒地里，莴笋只得在那里悲惨度日。 “Ah！thou wicked child,” cried the enchantress ,“What do I hear thee say!I thought I had separated thee from all the world, and yet thou hast deceived me.”In her anger she clutched Rapunzel’s beautiful tresses, wrapped them twice round her left hand, seized a pair of scissors with the right, and snip, snap, they were cut off, and the lovely braids lay on the ground.And she was so pitiless that she took poor Rapunzel into a desert where she had to live in great grief and misery.
可是，女巫赶走莴笋后，当晚却将剪下的长发绑在了窗户挂钩上。王子来了，喊道：“莴笋，莴笋，放下你的长发吧。”女巫放下了头发。王子顺着长发爬进塔里，可是在他面前的不是亲爱的莴笋，而是那个老女巫，女巫恶狠狠地地盯着他。她嘲讽地喊道：“啊哈！你又来找心上人吧，可惜那美丽的小鸟已不在这里了，野猫把她抓去了，还要剜掉你的双眼。莴笋不见了，你休想再见到她。”王子心痛极了，他绝望地跳下高塔。他死里逃生，可是却被荆棘刺瞎了双眼。于是，他漫无目的地在森林里游荡，只是吃些树根和浆果充饥，一刻不停地为失去心上人而悲叹。他就这样在痛苦中熬过了几年。后来，他终于走到了莴笋生活的那片荒野里，她和自己生下的一男一女双胞胎过着凄惨的生活。他听到一个非常熟悉的声音，便循着那声音走去，王子走近时，莴笋一眼认出了他，搂住他的脖子哭起来。两滴泪水落进了王子的眼睛里，他的双眼忽然复明了，又能像以前一样看见东西了。他带着莴笋回到自己的王国，他们受到了老百姓热情的欢迎。从此以后，他们过着幸福美满的生活。 On the same day, however, that she cast out Rapunzel, the enchantress in the evening fastened the braids of hair which she had cut off, to the hook of the window, and when the King’s son came and cried,“Rapunzel, Rapunzel, Let down thy hair,”she let the hair down.The King’s son ascended, but he did not find his dearest Rapunzel above, but the enchantress, who gazed at him with wicked and venomous looks.“Aha!” she cried mockingly, “Thou wouldst fetch thy dearest, but the beautiful bird sits no longer singing in the nest; the cat has got it, and will scratch out thy eyes as well.Rapunzel is lost to thee; thou wilt never see her more.”The King’s son was beside himself with pain, and in his despair he leapt down from the tower.He escaped with his life, but the thorns into which he fell, pierced his eyes.Then he wandered quite blind about the forest, ate nothing but roots and berries, and did nothing but lament and weep over the loss of his dearest wife.Thus he roamed about in misery for some years, and at length came to the desert where Rapunzel, with the twins to which she had given birth, a boy and a girl, lived in wretchedness.He heard a voice, and it seemed so familiar to him that he went towards it, and when he approached, Rapunzel knew him and fell on his neck and wept.Two of her tears wetted his eyes and they grew clear again, and he could see with them as before.He led her to his kingdom where he was joyfully received, and they lived for a long time afterwards, happy and contented.
强壮的汉斯 Strong Hans
从前，有对夫妻，他们只有一个孩子，住在一个人迹罕至的山谷中。有一次，母亲要去树林里捡杉树树枝，便带上刚两岁的小汉斯一道出门了。当时正值春暖花开，汉斯一看到那么多五颜六色的花儿就很高兴，母亲带着他渐渐走进了树林深处。突然，两个强盗从树丛中跳出来，一把抓住了母亲和孩子，强行拖着他们走向了终年都荒无人烟的黑森林深处。可怜的女人不住地哀求强盗放过她们母子俩，不过强盗铁石心肠，哪里听得进她的祈祷和恳求，只凶恶地赶着他们向前走。走了大概两英里远，穿越了无数的丛林荆棘，他们终于来到一座大石壁前。石壁上有道门，强盗敲了敲门，门就立即开了，他们又穿越了一条很长的暗道，最后进到一个大洞穴。一堆炉火照亮了那里。四周岩壁上悬挂的刀、剑，还有其他的致命武器，在炉火的照耀下闪着寒光。岩洞中央有四个强盗正围着一张黑色的桌子赌博，坐上位的是强盗头子。强盗头子一看到这个女人，就走过来和她说话，叫她不用害怕，他们不会伤害她。但她得帮他们收拾家务，只要做得井井有条，他们是绝不会为难她的。接着，他们给她一些吃的，还指给她看一张床，说她和孩子可以睡在那里。 There were once a man and a woman who had an only child, and lived quite alone in a solitary valley.It came to pass that the mother once went into the wood to gather branches of fir, and took with her little Hans, who was just two years old.As it was spring-time, and the child took pleasure in the many—coloured flowers, she went still further onwards with him into the forest.Suddenly two robbers sprang out of the thicket, seized the mother and child, and carried them far away into the black forest, where no one ever came from one year’s end to another.The poor woman urgently begged the robbers to set her and her child free, but their hearts were made of stone, they would not listen to her prayers and entreaties, and drove her on farther by force.After they had worked their way through bushes and briars for about two miles, they came to a rock where there was a door, at which the robbers knocked and it opened at once.They had to go through a long dark passage, and at last came into a great cavern, which was lighted by a fire which burnt on the hearth.On the wall hung swords, sabres, and other deadly weapons which gleamed in the light, and in the midst stood a black table at which four other robbers were sitting gambling, and the captain sat at the head of it.As soon as he saw the woman he came and spoke to her, and told her to be at ease and have no fear, they would do nothing to hurt her, but she must look after the house-keeping, and if she kept everything in order, she should not fare ill with them.Thereupon they gave her something to eat, and showed her a bed where she might sleep with her child.
那女人就这样跟强盗一起呆了很多年，汉斯已经长成了高大健壮的男子汉。母亲经常给他讲故事，还教他念一本从山洞中找到关于骑士的旧故事书。汉斯长到九岁时，用杉树枝给自己削了一根粗大的木棍，藏在床背后，然后他去问母亲：“亲爱的母亲，告诉我，我的父亲是谁，我一定要知道！”母亲沉默了，她不能告诉他，让他有回家的念头，而且，那些无法无天的强盗根本不可能放他走的。但一想到汉斯见不到自己的亲身父亲，母亲就心如刀割。晚上，等强盗们劫财归来，汉斯紧握他的大木棍，来到强盗头子面前，说：“我要知道我的父亲是谁！你现在要不说的话，我就一棍子打死你！”强盗头子大笑，照着耳根狠狠地打了汉斯一拳，把汉斯打得滚到了桌子下面。汉斯站起身来，一声不吭，心想：“再等一年，我还要试试！我会比现在强的！”很快一年就过去了，汉斯重新拿出那根棍子，擦掉上面的灰尘，凝视了一会，自言自语道：“这是一根多么结实的棍子啊！”晚上，强盗们都回来了，抱着酒坛一罐接一罐地狂饮，一个个都醉得头晕目眩的。汉斯手握木棍，又来到强盗头子面前，问他自己的父亲是谁。强盗头子又重重地给了汉斯耳根一拳，把他打到桌下。不过不久，汉斯就站起身来，用大棍狠狠地揍头子和强盗们，把他们打得无法动弹。母亲站在墙角，对儿子的勇敢和坚强充满了敬佩。汉斯把强盗教训了一顿后，对母亲说：“我说过我不是闹着玩的！现在我得知道我的父亲是谁了！”“我亲爱的孩子，”母亲说，“我们快点走吧！我们现在就出发去找他，一定可以找到他！”母亲从强盗头子身上搜出大门的钥匙；汉斯拿来一个大袋子，往袋子里装满了金银珠宝，还有其他美丽的玩意。然后他背着袋子上路了。他们终于走出了山洞，从黑漆漆的山洞来到阳光下，汉斯看到的是多么美丽的景象啊：郁郁葱葱的森林、五颜六色的花儿、叽叽喳喳的小鸟，还有天空中的朝阳！他站住了，痴痴地陶醉在这一片美景之中。母亲回想着回家的路，经过几个钟头的长途跋涉，他们终于回到了那个人迹罕至的小山谷，回到了他们的小屋子。当时他的父亲就坐在门口。父亲认出自己失踪多年的妻子，又得知汉斯就是自己的儿子，他高兴得热泪直流，因为他本以为他们早已不在人世了呢！虽然还未满十二岁，汉斯已经整整比父亲高出一头了。他们一起进入小屋，汉斯刚将沉甸甸的袋子放在炉边的凳子上，那整个屋子就开始瓦解。先是凳子断裂开来，然后地板也裂开缝，那沉甸甸的袋子就一直掉进了地窖里。“我的天啊！”父亲大叫道，“这是怎么了？你把我们的房子弄塌了吗？”“亲爱的父亲，别为这个担心！”汉斯安慰道，“那个袋子里装的钱远远够你盖一座新房子了！”于是父亲和汉斯马上着手建造新房，还买了牛和田地，有了自己的农庄。汉斯去田里耕地的时候，走在牛后头，用力将犁推进深土，这样牛拉起犁来几乎不要用力。第二年春天，汉斯对父亲说：“剩下的钱你慢慢花吧！麻烦请人帮我造一根重一点的手杖，我想出去走走了。”汉斯想要的手杖做好后，他就离开了父亲的房子。他走呀走，就来到一片茂密的黑森林。突然他听见吱吱嘎嘎破裂的响声。他四处一望，才看见是一棵杉树，从树梢到树根被扭成了麻绳一般。再往上看，只见一个大个子正拎着树干，像扭柳树枝一样轻松地盘弄着。“喂！”汉斯对他喊道，“你在上面干什么呢？”那个人回答道，“我昨天砍了一堆柴，今天来搓根麻绳好把它们捆起来。”“嘿，我喜欢这个家伙！”汉斯心想，“他倒有些力气。”于是他对那人喊道：“别忙活了，跟我一起走吧！”大个子就跳了下来，竟然比高大的汉斯还高出整整一个头！“就叫你‘扭树人’吧！”汉斯对他说。于是他们一起结伴向前走，猛然间听到铁锤重重敲击的声响，每敲一下，大地都跟着震动。很快，他们来到一块巨大的岩石旁，一个巨人正站在那里用拳头一下一下地打着岩石，打得石头一块块纷纷坠下。汉斯问他在做什么，巨人回答道：“我晚上睡觉的时候，那些狼啊熊啊什么的野兽都围着我身边闻来闻去，简直不让我睡个好觉！所以我就想造个房子，睡在里面，那样就能安稳些了。”“哦，是啊！”汉斯心想，“这个家伙也能为我所用。”于是汉斯对他说：“别管你的房子了，跟我们一起走吧！就叫你‘碎石人’好了。”巨人同意了，于是他们三人就一起在森林里闲逛，所过之处，野兽都吓得四散逃窜。晚上，他们来到一座废弃已久的老城堡，躺在大厅里歇息。第二天一早，汉斯走进了花园里。花园里杂草丛生，荆棘密布。汉斯正在花园里到处走着，突然一头野猪径直冲向汉斯，但汉斯一棍子打过去，野猪就应声倒地了。汉斯扛着野猪回到城堡，他们就生火将野猪烤熟了，饱餐了一顿。从那之后，他们就安排每天轮着由两个人出去找吃的，一个人呆家里给大家做饭，他们一个人一天能吃九磅肉呢！第一天，“扭树人”呆家里，汉斯和“碎石人”出去打猎。正当“扭树人”忙着做饭的时候，一个皱皱巴巴的小老头走进城堡来，问他要点肉吃。“滚远点，狡猾的骗子！”他答道，“你根本用不着吃肉。”但是，让“扭树人”怎么都想不到的是，这个不起眼的小矮子竟然向他猛扑过来，挥拳痛打了他一顿，而他根本无法招架，只有倒在地上喘气的份儿！小矮子把心里受的气发泄完了，才愤然离去。等那两个打猎的人回家之后，“扭树人”对今天发生的被小矮子痛打的丢人事只字未提，他想：“等轮到他们在家做饭，遇到那个野蛮的小个子，也让他们尝尝苦头！”这样的想法让他开心起来。 The woman stayed many years with the robbers, and Hans grew tall and strong.His mother told him stories, and taught him to read an old book of tales about knights which she found in the cave.When Hans was nine years old, he made himself a strong club out of a branch of fir, hid it behind the bed, and then went to his mother and said, “Dear mother, pray tell me who is my father; I must and will know.”His mother was silent and would not tell him, that he might not become home-sick; moreover she knew that the godless robbers would not let him go away, but it almost broke her heart that Hans should not go to his father.In the night, when the robbers came home from their robbing expedition, Hans brought out his club, stood before the captain, and said, “I now wish to know who is my father, and if thou dost not at once tell me I will strike thee down.”Then the captain laughed, and gave Hans such a box on the ear that he rolled under the table.Hans got up again, held his tongue, and thought, “I will wait another year and then try again, perhaps I shall do better then.”When the year was over, he brought out his club again, rubbed the dust off it, looked at it well, and said, “It
