is a stout strong club.”At night the robbers came home, drank one jug of wine after another, and their heads began to be heavy.Then Hans brought out his club, placed himself before the captain, and asked him who was his father?But the captain again gave him such a vigorous box on the ear that Hans rolled under the table, but it was not long before he was up again, and beat the captain and the robbers so with his club, that they could no longer move either their arms or their legs.His mother stood in a corner full of admiration of his bravery and strength.When Hans had done his work, he went to his mother, and said, “Now I have shown myself to be in earnest, but now I must also know who is my father.”“Dear Hans,” answered the mother, “come, we will go and seek him until we find him.”She took from the captain the key to the entrance-door, and Hans fetched a great meal-sack and packed into it gold and silver, and whatsoever else he could find that was beautiful, until it was full, and then he took it on his back.They left the cave, but how Hans did open his eyes when he came out of the darkness into daylight, and saw the green forest, and the flowers, and the birds, and the morning sun in the sky.He stood there and wondered at everything just as if he had not been very wise.His mother looked for the way home, and when they had walked for a couple of hours, they got safely into their lonely valley and to their little house.The father was sitting in the doorway.He wept for joy when he recognized his wife and heard that Hans was his son, for he had long regarded them both as dead.But Hans, although he was not twelve years old, was a head taller than his father.They went into the little room together, but Hans had scarcely put his sack on the bench by the stove, than the whole house began to crack the bench broke down and then the floor, and the heavy sack fell through into the cellar.“God save us!” cried the father, “what’s that?Now thou hast broken our little house to pieces!”“Don’t grow any grey hairs about that, dear father,” answered Hans; “there, in that sack, is more than is wanting for a new house.”The father and Hans at once began to build a new house; to buy cattle and land, and to keep a farm.Hans ploughed the fields, and when he followed the plough and pushed it into the ground, the bullocks had scarcely any need to draw.The next spring, Hans said, “Keep all the money and get a walking-stick that weighs a hundred-weight made for me that I may go a—travelling.”When the wished-for stick was ready, he left his father’s house, went forth, and came to a deep, dark forest.There he heard something crunching and cracking, looked round, and saw a fir-tree which was wound round like a rope from the bottom to the top, and when he looked upwards he saw a great fellow who had laid hold of the tree and was twisting it like a willow-wand.“Hollo!” cried Hans, “what art thou doing up there?” the fellow replied, “I got some faggots together yesterday and am twisting a rope for them.”“That is what I like,” thought Hans, “he has some strength,” and he called to him, “Leave that alone, and come with me.”The fellow came down, and he was taller by a whole head than Hans, and Hans was not little.“Thy name is now Fir-twister,” said Hans to him.Thereupon they went further and heard something knocking and hammering with such force that the ground shook at every stroke.Shortly afterwards they came to a mighty rock, before which a giant was standing and striking great pieces of it away with his fist.When Hans asked what he was about, he answered, “At night, when I want to sleep, bears, wolves, and other vermin of that kind come, which sniff and snuffle about me and won’t let me rest; so I want to build myself a house and lay myself inside it, so that I may have some peace.”“Oh, indeed,” thought Hans, “I can make use of this one also;” and said to him, “Leave thy house-building alone, and go with me; thou shalt be called Rock—splitter.”The man consented, and they all three roamed through the forest, and wherever they went the wild beasts were terrified, and ran away from them.In the evening they came to an old deserted castle, went up into it, and laid themselves down in the hall to sleep.The next morning Hans went into the garden.It had run quite wild, and was full of thorns and bushes.And as he was thus walking round about, a wild boar rushed at him; he, however, gave it such a blow with his club that it fell directly.He took it on his shoulders and carried it in, and they put it on a spit, roasted it, and enjoyed themselves.Then they arranged that each day, in turn, two should go out hunting, and one should stay at home, and cook nine pounds of meat for each of them.Fir-twister stayed at home the first, and Hans and Rock-splitter went out hunting.When Fir-twister was busy cooking, a little shrivelled-up old mannikin came to him in the castle, and asked for some meat.“Be off, sly hypocrite,” he answered, “thou needest no meat.”But how astonished Fir-twister was when the little insignificant dwarf sprang up at him, and belaboured him so with his fists that he could not defend himself, but fell on the ground and gasped for breath!The dwarf did not go away until he had thoroughly vented his anger on him.When the two others came home from hunting, Fir-twister said nothing to them of the old mannikin and of the blows which he himself had received, and thought, “When they stay at home, they may just try their chance with the little scrubbing-brush;” and the mere thought of that gave him pleasure already.
第二天是“碎石人”留在家里做饭，果然也遭遇了“扭树人”一样的经历。他因为拒绝给小矮子肉吃，被狠狠地揍了一顿。晚上打猎归来，“扭树人”一看“碎石人”的样子，就知道他果然也被收拾了。但他们俩都没说什么，并想着：“也让汉斯尝尝那个人的厉害！” The next day Rock-splitter stayed at home, and he fared just as Fir-twister had done, he was very ill-treated by the dwarf because he was not willing to give him any meat.When the others came home in the evening, Fir-twister easily saw what he had suffered, but both kept silence, and thought, “Hans also must taste some of that soup.”
第三天是汉斯留在家里。当他在厨房忙着做饭、擦洗碗盆，小矮子又来了，开口就要吃肉。汉斯心想：“看他真是个可怜人呢！我就把我的那份分点给他吃吧，也不影响那两个家伙的。”于是汉斯就分了一点肉给他。小矮子狼吞虎咽地吃完那份之后，还问汉斯要肉吃，好心的汉斯又给了他一块，并说这是很大的一块，应该够他吃了。哪知小矮子吃完这块肉，又向汉斯要。“你可真是贪得无厌！”汉斯这次拒绝了。恶狠狠的小矮子打算向他猛扑过去，就像以前教训扭树人和碎石人一样教训汉斯，可是这次他是找错对象了。汉斯轻轻松松几个拳头迎过去，就打得小矮子跳下了城堡的台阶。汉斯本打算一路追过去，但由于身材高大，反被小矮子绊了一跤。等汉斯站起来，小矮子已经跑远了。汉斯紧追不舍，一直追到森林里，眼见他钻进了石头上的一个洞里。汉斯只能回家了，不过他在这里做了标记。等那两个家伙回到家里，看见汉斯竟然泰然无事，都大为吃惊。汉斯把今天发生的事跟他们讲了，那两个家伙也不再隐瞒自己经历了什么。汉斯大笑，说：“你们真是该打！怎么那么小气呢？一点肉都舍不得施舍！也真丢脸了，长这么高大威猛，还被那个小矮人给收拾了！”于是，他们带上篮子和绳子，一起来到了小矮人溜进去的地洞。他们让汉斯带着他的棍子坐进篮子里，用绳子将篮子放下洞里去。当汉斯到了岩洞底，发现了一扇门。他打开门，竟然看到一位美如天仙，不，应该是美得无法描述的姑娘坐在那里。而那个小矮人正坐在她身边，像海猫一样阴险地盯着汉斯诡笑。姑娘的身子被铁链绑着，悲伤地看着汉斯，汉斯顿生怜惜之心，心想：“今天非把这个可怜的姑娘从这个邪恶的小矮子手里救出来不可！”于是汉斯一棍子向小矮人猛击过去，小矮人一下就倒地而亡了。姑娘身上的铁链也立刻解开了，而汉斯早被她的美迷住了！姑娘说她本是个国王的女儿，被一个野蛮的伯爵偷抢过来，因为她拒不搭理伯爵，就被囚禁在这个岩洞里。伯爵派了这个小矮人看守她，让她受尽了痛苦。汉斯将姑娘放进篮子，让两个同伴把她拉了上去。等篮子再次放下来的时候，汉斯却对两个家伙起了疑心，他想：“他们上次就已经欺骗了我，隐瞒了有关小矮人的事，天知道这次他们会怎么对付我？”汉斯就把棍子放进了篮子里，叫他们拉上去。多亏汉斯长了个心眼，篮子拉到半路，果然被摔下来了。如果汉斯自己坐里面的话，肯定没命了。只是汉斯现在也不知道该怎么从这么深的地方上去，他思来想去，一筹莫展。“那真是悲伤，”汉斯心想，“如果我只能在这里等死的话。”他在岩洞里没头绪地走来走去，偶然又回到了当时姑娘所在的房间，他看到小矮人手指上戴着一枚闪亮的戒指。汉斯取下戒指，套在自己手指上，他转动着手上的戒指，突然听到头顶传来沙沙的声响。他抬头一看，竟然是几个精灵围着他翩然盘旋着，它们说他是她们的主人，问他有什么愿望。汉斯一时惊讶得说不出话来，等回过神来，他要她们马上带他出洞去。她们立刻遵命，汉斯恍然感觉自己飞起来了。然而，当汉斯回到地面上的时候，那两个家伙早没了人影。“扭树人”和“碎石人”都已经逃之夭夭，还带走了美丽的姑娘。但汉斯转动了戒指，精灵又出现了，并告诉他那两个家伙在大海上。汉斯一刻不停地拼命追赶，终于到了海边，只看见远远的天边，浮有一叶小舟，里面就坐着他那两个背信弃义的同伴。汉斯怒火冲天，想也没想就提着棍子跳入海中，准备游过去收拾他们，但手中的棍子实在太沉了，拖着他直向海底沉去，差点儿淹死他。在这紧要关头，汉斯转动神戒，精灵立刻出现将他救起，并风驰电掣般地把他带到那两个家伙的船边。汉斯挥舞手中的大棍，给了那两个邪恶的家伙他们应有的教训，然后把他们扔下了大海。那个美丽的姑娘被吓坏了，汉斯再一次拯救了她，坐着船将她送回家，并见到了她的父母。后来他们结婚了，生活得非常幸福美满。 Hans, who had to stay at home the next day, did his work in the kitchen as it had to be done, and as he was standing skimming the pan, the dwarf came and without more ado demanded a bit of meat.Then Hans thought, “He is a poor wretch, I will give him some of my share, that the others may not run short,” and handed him a bit.When the dwarf had devoured it, he again asked for some meat, and good-natured Hans gave it to him, and told him it was a handsome piece, and that he was to be content with it.But the dwarf begged again for the third time.“Thou art shameless!” said Hans, and gave him none.Then the malicious dwarf wanted to spring on him and treat him as he had treated Fir—twister and Rock-splitter, but he had got to the wrong man.Hans, without exerting himself much, gave him a couple of blows which made him jump down the castle steps.Hans was about to run after him, but fell right over him, for he was so tall.When he rose up again, the dwarf had got the start of him.Hans hurried after him as far as the forest, and saw him slip into a hole in the rock.Hans now went home, but he had marked the spot.When the two others came back, they were surprised that Hans was so well.He told them what had happened, and then they no longer concealed how it had fared with them.Hans laughed and said, “It served you quite right; why were you so greedy with your meat?It is a disgrace that you who are so big should have let yourselves be beaten by the dwarf.”Thereupon they took a basket and a rope, and all three went to the hole in the rock into which the dwarf had slipped, and let Hans and his club down in the basket.When Hans had reached the bottom, he found a door, and when he opened it a maiden was sitting there who was lovely as any picture, nay, so beautiful that no words can express it, and by her side sat the dwarf and grinned at Hans like a sea-cat!She, however, was bound with chains, and looked so mournfully at him that Hans felt great pity for her, and thought to himself, “Thou must deliver her out of the power of the wicked dwarf,” and gave him such a blow with his club that he fell down dead.Immediately the chains fell from the maiden, and Hans was enraptured with her beauty.She told him she was a King’s daughter whom a savage count had stolen away from her home, and imprisoned there among the rocks, because she would have nothing to say to him.The count had, however, set the dwarf as a watchman, and he had made her bear misery and vexation enough.And now Hans placed the maiden in the basket and had her drawn up; the basket came down again, but Hans did not trust his two companions, and thought, “They have already shown themselves to be false, and told me nothing about the dwarf; who knows what design they may have against me?”So he put his club in the basket, and it was lucky he did; for when the basket was half-way up, they let it fall again, and if Hans had really been sitting in it he would have been killed.But now he did not know how he was to work his way out of the depths, and when he turned it over and over in his mind he found no counsel.“It is indeed sad,” said he to himself, “that I have to waste away down here,” and as he was thus walking backwards and forwards, he once more came to the little chamber where the maiden had been sitting, and saw that the dwarf had a ring on his finger which shone and sparkled.Then he drew it off and put it on, and when he turned it round on his finger, he suddenly heard something rustle over his head.He looked up and saw spirits of the air hovering above, who told him he was their master, and asked what his desire might be?Hans was at first struck dumb, but afterwards he said that they were to carry him above again.They obeyed instantly, and it was just as if he had flown up himself.When, however, he was above again, he found no one in sight.Fir-twister and Rock-splitter had hurried away, and had taken the beautiful maiden with them.But Hans turned the ring, and the spirits of the air came and told him that the two were on the sea.Hans ran and ran without stopping, until he came to the sea-shore, and there far, far out on the water, he perceived a little boat in which his faithless comrades were sitting; and in fierce anger he leapt, without thinking what he was doing, club in hand into the water, and began to swim, but the club, which weighed a hundredweight, dragged him deep down until he was all but drowned.Then in the very nick of time he turned his ring, and immediately the spirits of the air came and bore him as swift as lightning into the boat.He swung his club and gave his wicked comrades the reward they merited and threw them into the water, and then he sailed with the beautiful maiden, who had been in the greatest alarm, and whom he delivered for the second time, home to her father and mother, and married her, and all rejoiced exceedingly.
神奇的蓝灯 The Blue Light
很久很久以前，有一个忠心耿耿为国王战斗多年的士兵。可是，战争结束后，他却由于满身的伤口而无法继续服役了。国王对他说：“你可以回家去，我不再需要你了，我也不会给你钱，因为只有为我效力的人才能拿我的钱。”士兵不知如何才能养活自己，他很是烦恼地离开了，他走啊走，走了一整天，到晚上的时候走进了一片大森林。天色渐渐暗下来，他看到有一点灯光，便朝着灯光走去，来到了一座巫婆居住的房前。他对巫婆说：“请让我在这里借宿一夜吧，给我一点吃的和喝的，我快要饿死了。”巫婆答道：“是吗？谁会帮助一个逃跑士兵啊？可我是个有同情心的人，只要你听我的话，我愿意收留你。”士兵说：“你让我做什么？”“明天你给我把花园的土翻一遍。”士兵同意了，第二天他卖力地干了一天，可到晚上都没能干完活儿。巫婆说：“我看你今天是完不成了，不过我还是会再收留你一夜的，作为回报，你明天要给我砍一堆的柴火，并劈成小块。”士兵又干了整整一天，到了晚上，巫婆打算再收留他一夜。“明天你就给我干一件很轻松的活儿吧。在我的房子后面有一口干涸的古井，我的灯掉了进去，那盏灯燃烧着永不熄灭的蓝色火焰，你去把它给我拿上来。”第二天，老巫婆把士兵带到井边，让他坐在一个筐子里进入了井下。他找到了那盏发蓝光的灯，然后就示意老巫婆把他拖上去。老巫婆开始的确往上拉他，可是快到井口时，她便伸手去抢他手里的那盏灯。士兵发觉到了巫婆的恶意，便说道：“不行，在我双脚落地之前，我不会把灯给你的。”巫婆发怒了，一下扔掉手中的绳子，独自走开了。 There was once on a time a soldier who for many years had served the King faithfully, but when the war came to an end could serve no longer because of the many wounds which he had received.The King said to him, “Thou mayst return to thy home, I need thee no longer, and thou wilt not receive any more money, for he only receives wages who renders me service for them.”Then the soldier did not know how to earn a living, went away greatly troubled, and walked the whole day, until in the evening he entered a forest.When darkness came on, he saw a light, which he went up to, and came to a house wherein lived a witch.“Do give me one night’s lodging, and a little to eat and drink,” said he to her, “or I shall starve.”“Oho!” she answered, “who gives anything to a runaway soldier?Yet will I be compassionate, and take you in, if you will do what I wish.”“What do you wish?” said the soldier.“That you should dig all round my garden for me, tomorrow.”The soldier consented, and next day labored with all his strength, but could not finish it by the evening.“I see well enough,” said the witch, “that you can do no more today, but I will keep you yet another night, in payment for which you must tomorrow chop me a load of wood, and make it small.”The soldier spent the whole day in doing it, and in the evening the witch proposed that he should stay one night more.“Tomorrow, you shall only do me a very trifling piece of work.Behind my house, there is an old dry well, into which my light has fallen, it burns blue, and never goes out, and you shall bring it up again for me.”Next day the old woman took him to the well, and let him down in a basket.He found the blue light, and made her a signal to draw him up again.She did draw him up, but when he came near the edge, she stretched down her hand and wanted to take the blue light away from him.“No,” said he, perceiving her evil intention, “I will not give thee the light until I am standing with both feet upon the ground.”The witch fell into a passion, let him down again into the well, and went away.
可怜的士兵又落到了湿润的井底，他并没有受伤。那盏灯仍旧发出蓝光，可这对他来说有什么用呢？他很清楚，自己逃不掉死亡的。他难过地坐着，无意间触碰到口袋，发现里面还有一个装有半袋烟丝的烟斗。士兵心想：“这就是我最后的享受了。”他掏出烟斗，在蓝灯上点燃后抽了起来。当烟圈在井里环绕时，忽然冒出来一个身穿黑衣的小矮人，问道：“主人，你有什么吩咐？”士兵很惊讶，反问道：“我有什么吩咐？”小矮人说：“我会听从你的吩咐。”士兵说：“太好了，先把我带出这口井吧。”小矮人抓着他的手，领他穿过一条地下通道，士兵并是没有忘记随身带着那盏蓝灯。途中，小矮人不断地给士兵看老巫婆收藏在那里的金银财宝。士兵拿了金子，能搬多少就搬走了多少。出了井后，他对小矮人说：“现在去把那老巫婆捆绑起来，等候裁决。”不一会儿，巫婆像风卷过的野猫似的，发出可怕的喊叫从士兵面前跑过，又过了不一会儿，小矮人回来了。他说：“都处理好了，巫婆已被吊在了绞刑架上。我的主人，你还有什么吩咐？”小矮人问道。士兵回答说：“现在还没有，你可以回家了，只要我叫你，你就要立即现身。”“你只需用蓝灯点燃烟斗，我就会马上现身了。”接着，小矮人就消失不见了。 The poor soldier fell without injury on the moist ground, and the blue light went on burning, but of what use was that to him?He saw very well that he could not escape death.He sat for a while very sorrowfully, then suddenly he felt in his pocket and found his tobacco pipe, which was still half full.“This shall be my last pleasure,” thought he, pulled it out, lit it at the blue light and began to smoke.When the smoke had circled about the cavern, suddenly a little black dwarf stood before him, and said, “Lord, what are thy commands?”“What commands have I to give thee?” replied the soldier, quite astonished.“I must do everything thou biddest me,” said the little man.“Good,” said the soldier, “then in the first place help me out of this well.”The little man took him by the hand, and led him through an underground passage, but he did not forget to take the blue light with him.On the way the dwarf showed him the treasures which the witch had collected and hidden there, and the soldier took as much gold as he could carry.When he was above, he said to the little man, “Now go and bind the old witch, and carry her before the judge.”In a short time, she with frightful cries, came riding by, as swift as the wind on a wild tomcat, nor was it long after that before the little man reappeared.“It is all done,” said he, “and the witch is already hanging on the gallows.What further commands has my lord?” inquired the dwarf.“At this moment, none,” answered the soldier; “Thou canst return home, only be at hand immediately, if I summon thee.”“Nothing more is needed than that thou shouldst light thy pipe at the blue light, and I will appear before thee at once.”Thereupon he vanished from his sight.
士兵又返回到他被国王赶走前住的城市。他住最好的旅馆，为自己订做了很多华丽的衣裳，还让店主为他准备一间最气派的屋子。一切安排妥当后，士兵住了进去，他叫来穿黑衣的小矮人，说：“我曾忠心耿耿地为国王效力，可他却赶走了我，让我忍饥挨饿，现在我要报仇了。”小矮人问道：“我要怎么做？”“夜深的时候，等到公主睡熟了，你就悄悄把她带到这里，我要她像个佣人一样来伺候我。”小矮人说：“对我来说这太容易做到了，可对你来说这样做却很危险啊，因为一旦被发现，你可就惨了。”十二点的钟声敲响时，门砰的一声打开了，小矮人带着公主进来了。 The soldier returned to the town from which he had come.He went to the best inn, ordered himself handsome clothes, and then bade the landlord furnish him a room as handsomely as possible.When it was ready and the soldier had taken possession of it, he summoned the little black mannikin and said, “I have served the King faithfully, but he has dismissed me, and left me to hunger, and now I want to take my revenge.”“What am I to do?” asked the little man.“Late at night, when the King’s daughter is in bed, bring her here in her sleep, she shall do servant’s work for me.”The mannikin said, “That is an easy thing for me to do, but a very dangerous thing for you, for if it is discovered, you will fare ill.”When twelve o’clock had struck, the door sprang open, and the mannikin carried in the princess.
“啊哈！你终于来了呀？”士兵喊道，“赶快去干活！拿扫帚扫扫房间。” “Aha! art thou there?” cried the soldier, “get to thy work at once! Fetch the broom and sweep the chamber.”
公主扫完房间后，士兵又把她叫到跟前，然后他伸出双脚，说道：“给我把鞋脱掉。”随后他把鞋朝公主的脸上扔去，再让公主把鞋捡起来擦干净擦亮。公主睡眼惺忪地按他的吩咐默默做好了每件事，毫无反抗。当响起第一声鸡鸣声时，小矮人就把公主背回宫去，放到了她的床上。 When she had done this, he ordered her to come to his chair, and then he stretched out his feet and said, “Pull off my boots for me,” and then he threw them in her face, and made her pick them up again, and clean and brighten them.She, however, did everything he bade her, without opposition, silently and with half shut eyes.When the first cock crowed, the mannikin carried her back to the royal palace, and laid her in her bed.
第二天早上，公主起床后便去告诉国王，说她做了一个很奇怪的梦。她说：“我被人背过街道，像闪电一样快。后来来到了一个士兵的房里，我被迫像佣人一样地伺候他，要打扫房间，给他擦鞋，做所有下人做的活儿。这只是一个梦，可我感觉像真的干了那么多活儿一样疲惫。”国王说：“说不定这个梦是真的呢，我给你出个主意吧。你把口袋里塞满豌豆，再在口袋上戳一个小洞，这样的话，如果你被人带走就会有豌豆落下来，可以引路。”可是，国王看不到隐身的小矮人，当时他正站在国王身边，全都听到了。晚上，熟睡着的公主又被背走了，她口袋里的确沿途落下了一些豌豆，可是这些豌豆却无法引路，因为狡猾的小矮人之前已在每条街上都撒上了豌豆。公主又被迫伺候了士兵一夜，直到天明鸡叫。 Next morning when the princess arose, she went to her father, and told him that she had had a very strange dream.“I was carried through the streets with the rapidity of lightning,” said she, “and taken into a soldier’s room, and I had to wait upon him like a servant, sweep his room, clean his boots, and do all kinds of menial work.It was only a dream, and yet I am just as tired as if I really had done everything.”“The dream may have been true,” said the King, “I will give thee a piece of advice.Fill thy pocket full of peas, and make a small hole in it, and then if thou art carried away again, they will fall out and leave a track in the streets.”But unseen by the King, the mannikin was standing beside him when he said that, and heard all.At night when the sleeping princess was again carried through the streets, some peas certainly did fall out of her pocket, but they made no track, for the crafty mannikin had just before scattered peas in every street there was.And again the princess was compelled to do servant’s work until cock-crow.
第二天早上，国王派人去寻路，可无济于事，因为穷孩子们正坐在大街小巷上拾豌豆呢，他们说：“昨晚一定下了一场豌豆雨。”国王说：“我们得想个其他办法了，今晚你穿着鞋子睡觉，你被带回来之前藏一只鞋子在那里，我很快会设法找到它的。”穿黑衣的小矮人又听到了国王的诡计。晚上士兵又要求他去背公主来的时候，他便把这件事情告诉了士兵，说他没有应急手段对付国王的策略了，还说如果在士兵的房子里找到了那只鞋，他一定会遭殃的。士兵回答说：“只要按我说的去做就行了。”于是，公主又第三次做了一夜的粗活，可是她离开前，在床下藏了一只鞋子。 Next morning the King sent his people out to seek the track, but it was all in vain, for in every street poor children were sitting, picking up peas, and saying, “It must have rained peas, last night.”“We must think of something else,” said the King; “keep thy shoes on when thou goest to bed, and before thou comest back from the place where thou art taken, hide one of them there, I will soon contrive to find it.”The black mannikin heard this plot, and at night when the soldier again ordered him to bring the princess, revealed it to him, and told him that he knew of no expedient to counteract this stratagem, and that if the shoe were found in the soldier’s house it would go badly with him.“Do what I bid thee,” replied the soldier, and again this third night the princess was obliged to work like a servant, but before she went away, she hid her shoe under the bed.
第二天早上，国王命人全城寻找公主的鞋子。最后在士兵的床底下找到了，小矮人说服士兵逃出城去，可很快还是被抓回来投进了监狱。士兵匆忙逃走的时候忘了带上他最珍贵的东西，也就是那盏蓝灯和金子，现在口袋里只剩下一个硬币了。他拖着铁链，站在大牢的窗前向外张望，碰巧看到一个熟人经过。士兵敲打窗户玻璃将那人叫了过来，对他说道：“你要是能帮我取回落在旅店的小包袱就太好了，我会给你一个金币作为报酬的。”他的朋友便跑去旅店，帮他取回了包袱。士兵在独自一人的时候，赶紧用蓝灯点燃了烟斗召唤来小矮人。小矮人对他的主人说：“不要怕。他们带你去哪儿你就去哪儿，他们想干什么就让他们干什么，只要带上这盏小蓝灯就行了。”第二天，士兵接受了审判，虽然他没干什么邪恶的事情，可法官还是判他死罪。当被带往刑场的时候，他请求国王再满足他一个心愿。国王问道：“什么心愿？”“让我在路上再抽一斗烟吧。”国王答道：“你抽多少斗都可以，但别妄想我会饶了你。”于是，士兵拿出烟斗，在蓝灯上点燃了。几个烟圈一冒出来，小矮人就出现了，手里还拿着一根短棍，他问道：“我的主人，你有什么吩咐？”“把那些不公正的法官、警察，还有那个对我很坏的国王都打倒在地。”于是，小矮人像闪电一般冲向他们，到处挥舞着手中的短棍，被他的短棍打到的人都瘫倒在地，不敢再动弹一下。国王很害怕，他倒在地上请求士兵宽恕，说只要能饶他一命，他愿意把整个王国都给士兵，还要把女儿嫁给士兵。 Next morning the King had the entire town searched for his daughter’s shoe.It was found at the soldier’s, and the soldier himself, who at the entreaty of the dwarf had gone outside the gate, was soon brought back, and thrown into prison.In his flight he had forgotten the most valuable things he had, the blue light and the gold, and had only one ducat in his pocket.And now loaded with chains, he was standing at the window of his dungeon, when he chanced to see one of his comrades passing by.The soldier tapped at the pane of glass, and when this man came up, said to him, “Be so kind as to fetch me the small bundle I have left lying in the inn, and I will give you a ducat for doing it.”His comrade ran thither and brought him what he wanted.As soon as the soldier was alone again, he lighted his pipe and summoned the black mannikin.“Have no fear,” said the latter to his master.“Go wheresoever they take you, and let them do what they will, only take the blue light with you.”Next day the soldier was tried, and though he had done nothing wicked, the judge condemned him to death.When he was led forth to die, he begged a last favor of the King.“What is it?” asked the King.“That I may smoke one more pipe on my way.”“Thou mayst smoke three,” answered the King, “but do not imagine that I will spare thy life.”Then the soldier pulled out his pipe and lighted it at the blue light, and as soon as a few wreaths of smoke had ascended, the mannikin was there with a small cudgel in his hand, and said, “What does my lord command?”“Strike down to earth that false judge there, and his constable, and spare not the King who has treated me so ill.”Then the mannikin fell on them like lightning, darting this way and that way, and whosoever was so much as touched by his cudgel fell to earth, and did not venture to stir again.The King was terrified; he threw himself on the soldier’s mercy, and merely to be allowed to live at all, gave him his kingdom for his own, and the princess to wife.
水牛皮靴 The Boots of Buffalo Leather
有一个士兵，他天不怕地不怕，也总是无忧无虑的。士兵退役后，由于没有手艺，便难以维持生计了，他便四处游荡，向好心人乞讨。他穿着一件破雨衣和那双留下来的水牛皮靴。一天，他漫无目的地晃荡着，走到野地去了，最后来到一片森林里。他不知道自己到了哪里，只是看到一棵被砍开的树干上坐着一个衣着光鲜的男子，他穿着一件绿色的打猎服。士兵同他握手问候，然后坐在他身边的草地上，把两腿伸开。他对猎人说：“我看你穿的这双黑亮的靴子挺不错的，不过，你要是像我这样四处游荡的话，肯定穿不久。看看我的靴子，这可是水牛皮的，我都穿了很久了呢，可是还可以继续穿着它们跋山涉水。”过了一会儿，士兵起身说道：“我不能再呆下去了，因为很饿，我得继续赶路了，不过，皮靴黑亮的兄弟，这条路通向哪里呢？”猎人答道：“我也不知道，我在森林里迷路了。”士兵便说：“那你和我一样陷入困境了呀，我俩真是难兄难弟啊，我们就一起寻找出路吧。”猎人微微笑了一下，于是他们一起上路了，走啊走，一直走到夜幕降临了。士兵说：“我们走不出这片森林了，不过我看到远处有一点灯光在闪烁，或许在那里可以找到点吃的。”他们来到了一间石头小屋前，敲了敲门，一个老婆婆开了门。士兵说：“我们要找个地方过夜，还得吃点东西填填肚子了，我的肚子就像个破背包一样空荡荡的。”老婆婆回答说：“你们不能留在这里；这是个强盗窝，你们最好赶在他们回来之前离开这里，不然就要送命了。”士兵答道：“事情不会那么糟糕的，我已经两天没吃过东西了。对我来说，被强盗杀死和在森林里饿死没什么两样。让我进去吧。 A soldier who is afraid of nothing, troubles himself about nothing.One of this kind had received his discharge, and as he had learnt no trade and could earn nothing, he travelled about and begged alms of kind people.He had an old waterproof on his back, and a pair of riding boots of buffalo leather which were still left to him.One day he was walking he knew not where, straight out into the open country, and at length came to a forest.He did not know where he was, but saw sitting on the trunk of a tree, which had been cut down, a man who was well dressed and wore a green shooting-coat.The soldier shook hands with him, sat down on the grass by his side, and stretched out his legs.“I see thou hast good boots on, which are well blacked,” said he to the huntsman; “but if thou hadst to travel about as I have, they would not last long.Look at mine, they are of buffalo leather, and have been worn for a long time, but in them I can go through thick and thin.”After a while the soldier got up and said, “I can stay no longer, hunger drives me onwards; but, Brother Bright boots, where does this road lead to?”“I don’t know that myself,” answered the huntsman, “I have lost my way in the forest.”“Then thou art in the same plight as I,” said the soldier; “birds of a feather flock together, let us remain together, and seek our way.”The huntsman smiled a little, and they walked on further and further, until night fell.“We do not get out of the forest,” said the soldier, “but there in the distance I see a light shining, which will help us to something to eat.”They found a stone house, knocked at the door, and an old woman opened it.“We are looking for quarters for the night,” said the soldier, “and some lining for our stomachs, for mine is as empty as an old knapsack.”“You cannot stay here,” answered the old woman; “this is a robber’s house, and you would do wisely to get away before they come home, or you will be lost.”“It won’t be so bad as that,” answered the soldier, “I have not had a mouthful for two days, and whether I am murdered here or die of hunger in the forest is all the same to me. I shall in.”
猎人不愿和他一起进屋，可士兵拽着他的衣袖将他拉了进去。“快进来吧，兄弟，我们不至于那么快就没命的。”老婆婆很同情他们俩，便说：“悄悄藏到火炉后面吧，如果他们剩下了吃的，我就趁他们睡着时偷偷拿给你们。”他们刚躲到角落里面，十二个强盗就闯进了屋子，他们坐在早已备好的饭桌前，粗暴地让老婆婆端上饭菜。老婆婆端来几大盘烤肉，强盗们津津有味地享用起来。饭菜的香味传到了士兵的鼻孔里，他对猎人说：“我真是坚持不下去了，我也要坐到桌子旁，和他们一起吃。”猎人说：“你会让我们送命的。”他拖住了士兵的胳膊。可士兵却开始大声咳嗽起来。强盗听到声音后，纷纷丢下刀叉跳起来，发现了藏在炉子后面的两个人。他们喊道：“啊哈，两个人，你们藏在角落里？你们到这里干什么？有人派你们来做密探吗？等着，你们很快就会被吊死了。”士兵说：“别那么凶，我只是饿了，给我点吃的吧，然后随你们怎么处置我都行。”强盗们很吃惊，强盗头说道：“我看你还够大胆，好吧，就让你吃点东西，不过之后你就等死吧。”士兵说：“再看吧。”他坐到桌旁，大口大口地吃起烤肉来。他还朝猎人喊道：“靴子黑亮的兄弟，你肯定也跟我一样饿了，在家里可吃不到这么好吃的烤肉啊。”可是，猎人并不想吃。强盗们吃惊地望着士兵，说道：“这家伙倒是真不客气啊。”过了一会儿，士兵又说：“我已经吃饱了，现在给我点好喝的吧。”强盗头愿意再迁就他一次，便朝老婆婆喊道：“到地窖里去拿一瓶最好的酒来。”士兵砰地一声打开了瓶塞，然后拎着酒瓶来到猎人跟前，说道：“注意了，兄弟，你会觉得惊讶的，我现在要为这些人永远健康而喝了这瓶酒。”说罢，他拿着酒瓶在强盗们的脑袋上挥舞来挥舞去，还嚷着：“你们所有人都长生不老，张开你们的嘴巴，举起你们的右手。”说完他痛快地喝了一大口酒。他刚说完这些话，强盗们都像石像一样呆在那里了，他们张着嘴巴，擎着右手。猎人对士兵说：“我觉得你还会用其它法术啊，不过，现在我们还是回家吧。”“唉，我亲爱的兄弟啊，现在走还太早了。我们已征服了敌人，首先得得到些战利品啊。强盗们只能一动不动地坐在那里，吃惊地张大着嘴巴，在我允许他们动起来之前他们是不会活动的。快点，吃点喝点吧。”老婆婆只得再去拿一瓶最好的酒，士兵吃了差不多能让他撑三天的食物后才站起身来。最终天亮了，他说：“现在我们该离开了，因为我们得尽快走出去，就让老婆婆给我们指一条通向城里的最近的路吧。”他们到达城里后，士兵去找他的老战友，说：“我在森林里找到了一个强盗窝，跟我一起去歼灭他们吧。”士兵为大家领路，他对猎人说：“你得跟我回去看看，看我们提起他们的脚时他们能颤抖成什么样子。”他让战友们把强盗包围在中间，然后他拿起酒瓶，喝了一口酒，又把酒瓶放在他们的脑袋上挥舞一番，喊道：“你们可以活过来了。”土匪们立即恢复了活动能力，却马上被士兵们按倒，绑住了手脚。然后，士兵命令大家像扔麻袋一样将土匪们扔到了马车上，说道：“现在把他们运到牢房去。”然而，猎人将一个士兵喊到一边，告诉了他另外一件事。士兵说：“皮靴黑亮的兄弟，我们已经成功地押送敌人了，也都吃饱喝足了，现在我们就像落伍士兵一样跟在他们后面走就好了！”他们到达城里后，士兵看到很多人涌出城门，他们高兴地大声喊叫着，挥舞着手中的绿树枝。接着，他看到整个护卫队都朝他们走过来。他问猎人：“这是怎么回事？”猎人答道：“你不知道吗？国王已经离开王宫很久了，今天他要返回宫去，大家都出来欢迎他啊。”士兵又问：“可是国王在哪里呢？我没看到他啊。”猎人回答说：“他就在这儿啊，我就是国王，我让人通知大家我回来了。”说罢，他脱下猎服，露出了里面的国王的礼服。士兵吓呆了，他双膝跪下，请求国王饶恕他的无知，把国王看做同自己一样的人，还用那样的外号称呼他。可是，国王却与他握了握手，说道：“你是一个英勇的士兵，曾经救过我的命。以后你不会再生活窘迫了，我会关照你。如果你又想吃像强盗窝里那样好吃的烤肉了，就到御膳房去吧。不过，你要是想祝别人长生不老的话，可要事先得到我的准许啊。” The huntsman would not follow, but the soldier drew him in with him by the sleeve.“Come, my dear brother, we shall not come to an end so quickly as that!”The old woman had pity on them and said, “Creep in here behind the stove, and if they leave anything, I will give it to you on the sly when they are asleep.”Scarcely were they in the corner before twelve robbers came bursting in, seated themselves at the table which was already laid, and vehemently demanded some food.The old woman brought in some great dishes of roast meat, and the robbers enjoyed that thoroughly.When the smell of the food ascended the nostrils of the soldier, he said to the huntsman, “I cannot hold out any longer, I shall seat myself at the table, and eat with them.” “Thou wilt bring us to destruction,” said the huntsman, and held him back by the arm.But the soldier began to cough loudly.When the robbers heard that, they threw away their knives and forks, leapt up, and discovered the two who were behind the stove.“Aha, gentlemen, are you in the corner?” cried they, “What are you doing here?Have you been sent as spies?Wait a while, and you shall learn how to fly on a dry bough.”“But do be civil,” said the soldier, “I am hungry, give me something to eat, and then you can do what you like with me.”The robbers were astonished, and the captain said, “I see that thou hast no fear; well, thou shalt have some food, but after that thou must die.”“We shall see,” said the soldier, and seated himself at the table, and began to cut away valiantly at the roast meat.“Brother Bright boots, come and eat,” cried he to the huntsman; “thou must be as hungry as I am, and cannot have better roast meat at home,” but the huntsman would not eat.The robbers looked at the soldier in astonishment, and said, “The rascal uses no ceremony.”After a while he said, “I have had enough food, now get me something good to drink.”The captain was in the mood to humour him in this also, and called to the old woman, “Bring a bottle out of the cellar, and mind it be of the best.”The soldier drew the cork out with a loud noise, and then went with the bottle to the huntsman and said, “Pay attention, brother, and thou shalt see something that will surprise thee; I am now going to drink the health of the whole clan.”Then he brandished the bottle over the heads of the robbers, and cried, “Long life to you all, but with your mouths open and your right hands lifted up,” and then he drank a hearty draught.Scarcely were the words said than they all sat motionless as if made of stone, and their mouths were open and their right hands stretched up in the air.The huntsman said to the soldier, “I see that thou art acquainted with tricks of another kind, but now come and let us go home.”“Oho, my dear brother, but that would be marching away far too soon; we have conquered the enemy, and must first take the booty.Those men there are sitting fast, and are opening their mouths with astonishment, but they will not be allowed to move until I permit them.Come, eat and drink.”The old woman had to bring another bottle of the best wine, and the soldier would not stir until he had eaten enough to last for three days.At last when day came, he said, “Now it is time to strike our tents, and that our march may be a short one, the old woman shall show us the nearest way to the town.”When they had arrived there, he went to his old comrades, and said, “Out in the forest I have found a nest full of gallows’ birds, come with me and we will take it.”The soldier led them, and said to the huntsman, “Thou must go back again with me to see how they shake when we seize them by the feet.”He placed the men round about the robbers, and then he took the bottle, drank a mouthful, brandished it above them, and cried, “Live again.”Instantly they all regained the power of movement, but were thrown down and bound hand and foot with cords.Then the soldier ordered them to be thrown into a cart as if they had been so many sacks, and said, “Now drive them straight to prison.”The huntsman, however, took one of the men aside and gave him another commission besides.“Brother Bright boots,” said the soldier, “we have safely routed the enemy and been well fed, now we will quietly walk behind them as if we were stragglers!”When they approached the town, the soldier saw a crowd of people pouring through the gate of the town who were raising loud cries of joy, and waving green boughs in the air.Then he saw that the entire body guard was coming up.“What can this mean?” said he to the huntsman.“Dost thou not know?” he replied, “that the King has for a long time been absent from his kingdom, and that today he is returning, and every one is going to meet him.”“But where is the King?” said the soldier, “I do not see him.”“Here he is,” answered the huntsman, “I am the King, and have announced my arrival.”Then he opened his hunting-coat, and his royal garments were visible.The soldier was alarmed, and fell on his knees and begged him to forgive him for having in his ignorance treated him as an equal, and spoken to him by such a name.But the King shook hands with him, and said, “Thou art a brave soldier, and hast saved my life.Thou shalt never again be in want, I will take care of thee.And if ever thou wouldst like to eat a piece of roast meat, as good as that in the robber’s house, come to the royal kitchen.But if thou wouldst drink a health, thou must first ask my permission.”
金孩儿 The Gold-Children
从前，有一对贫穷的夫妻，他们除了有一间小小的茅屋以外它一无所有。他们靠打鱼为生，常常是吃了上顿没有下顿。一天，渔夫坐在水边下网捕鱼，当他收网时发现捞起一条全金的鱼。就在他满心惊奇地打量着那条鱼的时候，金鱼开口说话了：“渔夫，你听我说，如果你把我放回水里，我将会把你的小茅屋变成一座豪华的城堡。”渔夫答道：“我连饭都吃不饱，要座城堡有什么用呢？”金鱼接着说：“这个我也应该考虑到了，到时候城堡里有一个大柜子，当你打开大柜子时，里面会放着各种各样的最精美的食物，而且你想要多少就有多少。”“如果这是真的，”渔夫说，“那我一定要帮你这个忙了。”“是真的，”金鱼说，“但是有个条件，就是你不能将这件事告诉任何人你的好运是哪里的，不管是谁。如果你泄露了一个字，这一切就都消失了。”于是渔夫就把这条神奇的金鱼放回水里，然后就回家了。之前那座小茅屋的所在之处，现在果真矗立着一座大城堡。他睁大眼睛走了进去，看见他妻子穿着漂亮的衣服，坐在一间豪华的房间里。她非常高兴，问她丈夫：“夫君，这是怎么来的啊？对我是再合适不过了。”“是的，”渔夫说，“对我也一样，不过我饿得要命，你先给我弄点吃的吧。”妻子回答：“我可没吃的，在这新房子里我不知道去哪找东西。”“这你就不用管了，”渔夫说，“我看见那边有一个大柜子，你去打开看一看。”当他老婆把柜子打开，里面放着蛋糕、肉、水果和酒，简直是一桌丰盛的宴席。 There was once a poor man and a poor woman who had nothing but a little cottage, and who earned their bread by fishing, and always lived from hand to mouth.But it came to pass one day when the man was sitting by the water-side, and casting his net, that he drew out a fish entirely of gold.As he was looking at the fish, full of astonishment, it began to speak and said, “Hark you, fisherman, if you will throw me back again into the water, I will change your little hut into a splendid castle.”Then the fisherman answered, “Of what use is a castle to me, if I have nothing to eat?”The gold fish continued, “That shall be taken care of, there will be a cupboard in the castle in which, when you open it, shall be dishes of the most delicate meats, and as many of them as you can desire.”“If that be true,” said the man, “then I can well do you a favour.”“Yes,” said the fish, “there is, however, the condition that you shall disclose to no one in the world, whosoever he may be, whence your good luck has come, if you speak but one single word, all will be over.”Then the man threw the wonderful fish back again into the water, and went home.But where his hovel had formerly stood, now stood a great castle.He opened wide his eyes, entered, and saw his wife dressed in beautiful clothes, sitting in a splendid room, and she was quite delighted, and said, “Husband, how has all this come to pass?It suits me very well.”“Yes,” said the man, “it suits me too, but I am frightfully hungry, just give me something to eat.”Said the wife, “But I have got nothing and don’t know where to find anything in this new house.”“There is no need of your knowing,” said the man, “for I see yonder a great cupboard, just unlock it.”When she opened it, there stood cakes, meat, fruit, wine, quite a bright prospect.
妻子高兴地大叫起来：“亲爱的，你还奢求什么呢？”于是他们坐下来一起大吃大喝。他们吃饱以后，妻子问：“但是这些好东西是从哪儿来的呢？”“哎，”渔夫答道，“别问我了，我是不敢告诉你的。如果我向别人透露这件事，我们的一切财富就会消失了。”“好吧，”她说，“我不应该知道的事，我还是不知道为好。”然而，她说的并不是真心话。她一天到晚缠着她丈夫，直到把她丈夫缠得失去了耐心，他只好说这一切都是一条神奇的金鱼所赐，他抓住了它，后来为了回报它就给了它自由。这个秘密一说出，那豪华的城堡连同大柜子马上就消失得无影无踪，夫妻俩又一次坐在从前的小茅屋中，渔夫只好重操旧业去捕鱼了。可是他很幸运，他又一次捕到了那条金鱼。“听着，”金鱼说，“如果你再把我放回水中，我还会给你城堡和装满烤肉和炖肉的大柜子。但是，这一次千万记住，看在你的生活的份儿上，不要再泄露你从哪儿得到这些的，否则你将会再次失去这一切！”“我一定会非常注意的。”渔夫一边回答一边把金鱼放回水里。现在家里的一切又重新恢复到以前的辉煌了，渔夫的妻子对他们的好运感到十分高兴，可是好奇心折磨得她坐立不安，没过几天，她又开始追问事情的经过，问他是怎样设法弄到这些的。渔夫保持沉默，但是没过多久，他就被妻子纠缠得很生气，于是他违背了誓言，泄露了秘密。转眼间，城堡就消失了，他们又住回了他们从前那破旧的茅屋。“现在你得到你想得到的了，”渔夫说，“可我们又得过那光啃骨头没肉的日子了。”“唉，”妻子说，“如果我不知道那些东西是从哪来的，我宁愿不要，因为那样我会坐立不安的。” Then the woman cried joyfully, “What more can you want, my dear?” and they sat down, and ate and drank together.When they had had enough, the woman said, “But husband, whence come all these riches?”“Alas,” answered he, “do not question me about it, for I dare not tell you anything; if I disclose it to any one, then all our good fortune will fly.”“Very good,” said she, “if I am not to know anything, then I do not want to know anything.”However, she was not in earnest; she never rested day or night, and she goaded her husband until in his impatience he revealed that all was owing to a wonderful golden fish which he had caught, and to which in return he had given its liberty.And as soon as the secret was out, the splendid castle with the cupboard immediately disappeared, they were once more in the old fisherman’s hut, and the man was obliged to follow his former trade and fish.But fortune would so have it, that he once more drew out the golden fish.“Listen,” said the fish, “if you will throw me back into the water again, I will once more give you the castle with the cupboard full of roast and boiled meats; only be firm, for your life’s sake don’t reveal from whom you have it, or you will lose it all again!”“I will take good care,” answered the fisherman, and threw the fish back into the water.Now at home everything was once more in its former magnificence, and the wife was overjoyed at their good fortune, but curiosity left her no peace, so that after a couple of days she began to ask again how it had come to pass, and how he had managed to secure it.The man kept silence for a short time, but at last she made him so angry that he broke out, and betrayed the secret.In an instant the castle disappeared, and they were back again in their old hut.“Now you have got what you want,” said he; “and we can gnaw at a bare bone again.”“Ah,” said the woman, “I had rather not have riches if I am not to know from whom they come, for then I have no peace.”
渔夫只得又去捕鱼，过了一会儿，他第三次捕到了那条金鱼。“听着，”金鱼说，“看来我是命中注定要被你抓住了，带我回家吧，把我切成六片，让你老婆吃两片，让你的马吃两片，剩下两片埋在地下，这样它们就会赐福于你。”渔夫带着金鱼回到家里，并且按金鱼吩咐的做了。过了一些时候，在那片埋着两片鱼肉的地上长出了两朵金百合花，渔夫的马生产下了两匹金马驹，而渔夫的妻子生下了两个全身金灿灿的孩子。孩子们一天天长大，长成了高大英俊的小伙子，那两朵金百合和两匹金马驹也同样长大了。他们对渔夫说：“父亲，我们想骑上我们的金马，出去见见世面。”渔夫很忧伤地回答说：“要是你们都走了，我怎么能受得了呢？我怎么能知道你们的情况呢？”儿子们说：“那两朵金百合还在这里呢。你看看它们，就能知道我们的情况了。如果它们鲜艳美丽，我们就是身体健康；如果它们枯萎了，那我们就是生病了；如果它们凋谢了，那我们就是死了。”于是他们骑着马出发了。他们来到一家旅店，里面有很多人，人们一看见两个金孩儿就开始嘲笑他们。一个金孩儿听到人们的嘲笑，感到不好意思，便不想再出去见世面了。他调头回了家，回到了爸爸身边。另一位金孩儿却坚持往前骑，来到了一大片森林前。他正准备催马进去，旁边有人劝他说：“你骑着马穿过森林可不安全啊。林子里全是匪徒，他们会欺负你的。如果你运气不佳，让他们发现你是金的，你的马也是金的，他们肯定会杀了你。” The man went back to fish, and after a while he chanced to draw out the gold fish for a third time.“Listen,” said the fish, “I see very well that I am fated to fall into your hands, take me home and cut me into six pieces; give your wife two of them to eat, two to your horse and bury two of them in the ground, then they will bring you a blessing.”The fisherman took the fish home with him, and did as it had bidden him.It came to pass, however, that from the two pieces that were buried in the ground two golden lilies sprang up, that the horse had two golden foals, and the fisherman’s wife bore two children who were made entirely of gold.The children grew up, became tall and handsome, and the lilies and horses grew likewise.Then they said, “Father, we want to mount our golden steeds and travel out in the world.”But he answered sorrowfully, “How shall I bear it if you go away, and I know not how it fares with you?”Then they said, “The two golden lilies remain here.By them you can see how it is with us; if they are fresh, then we are in health; if they are withered, we are ill; if they perish, then we are dead.”So they rode forth and came to an inn, in which were many people, and when they perceived the gold-children they began to laugh, and jeer.When one of them heard the mocking he felt ashamed and would not go out into the world, but turned back and went home again to his father.But the other rode forward and reached a great forest.As he was about to enter it, the people said, It is not safe for you to ride through, the wood is full of robbers who would treat you badly.You will fare ill, and when they see that you are all of gold, and your horse likewise, they will assuredly kill you.’
可是这个金孩儿一点也不怕，他说：“我必须骑过去，而且我能够骑过去。”然后他拿出熊皮穿在身上，也用熊皮盖在金马的身上，这样他们的金身就不会被人发现了。于是他毫无畏惧地骑进了那片森林。他骑马走了不远，听见树丛中沙沙作响，又听见几个人的说话声。一边有人喊：“过来一个人。”另一边答：“放他过去吧，他是个懒散的家伙，比教堂里的耗子富不到哪儿去，我们能从他身上得到什么？” But he would not allow himself to be frightened, and said, “I must and will ride through it.”Then he took bear-skins and covered himself and his horse with them, so that the gold was no more to be seen, and rode fearlessly into the forest.When he had ridden onward a little he heard a rustling in the bushes, and heard voices speaking together.From one side came cries of, “There is one,” but from the other, “Let him go, ‘tis an idle fellow, as poor and bare as a church-mouse, what should we gain from him?”
就这样金孩儿高高兴兴地穿过了森林，没有发生任何意外。有一天，金孩儿来到一个村子，见到一位非常漂亮的姑娘，他认为是她就是世界上最漂亮的人了。他顿时被爱情的力量所征服，便走到她面前对她说：“我是全心全意地爱你，你愿意嫁给我吗？”他同样让姑娘很欢喜，于是姑娘同意了，她回答说：“是的，我愿意嫁给你，我会永远忠于你！”于是他们就举行了婚礼，正当他们沉浸在幸福之中时，新娘的父亲回到了家。他看到女儿正在举行婚礼，非常吃惊，问道：“新郎在哪儿？”旁人给他指了指仍然穿着熊皮的金孩儿。父亲一看便勃然大怒：“一个流浪汉决不能娶我的女儿！”说完就要动手去杀金孩儿。新娘竭力恳求她的父亲，说：“他是我的丈夫，而且我全心全意地爱他！”直到劝得她的父亲终于平静了下来。可是他仍然不肯罢休。第二天一大早，他就爬起来，想看一看他的女婿是不是真的是一个衣衫褴褛的乞丐。他往屋里面一望，只见床上躺着一个华丽的、金色的男人，地上扔着那张熊皮。他退回去，暗中感叹道：“我能及时克制住自己的愤怒真是万幸！否则，我可真是罪不可赦啦！”此时，金孩儿正在睡梦中，他梦见自己骑马外出狩猎，猎到一只漂亮的雄鹿。早上醒来后，他对妻子说：“我必须出去打猎。”她感到有些不安，求他呆在家里，并且劝他：“你也许会遭遇不测。”可金孩儿答道：“我非去不可。” So the gold-child rode joyfully through the forest, and no evil befell him.One day he entered a village wherein he saw a maiden, who was so beautiful that he did not believe that any more beautiful than she existed in the world.And as such a mighty love took possession of him, he went up to her and said, “I love thee with my whole heart, wilt thou be my wife?”He, too, pleased the maiden so much that she agreed and said, “Yes, I will be thy wife, and be true to thee my whole life long.”Then they were married, and just as they were in the greatest happiness, home came the father of the bride, and when he saw that his daughter’s wedding was being celebrated, he was astonished, and said, “Where is the bridegroom?”They showed him the gold-child, who, however, still wore his bear-skins.Then the father said wrathfully, “A vagabond shall never have my daughter!” and was about to kill him.Then the bride begged as hard as she could, and said, “He is my husband, and I love him with all my heart!” until at last he allowed himself to be appeased.Nevertheless the idea never left his thoughts, so that next morning he rose early, wishing to see whether his daughter’s husband was a common ragged beggar.But when he peeped in, he saw a magnificent golden man in the bed, and the cast-off bear-skins lying on the ground.Then he went back and thought, “What a good thing it was that I restrained my anger!I should have committed a great crime.”But the gold-child dreamed that he rode out to hunt a splendid stag, and when he awoke in the morning, he said to his wife, “I must go out hunting.”She was uneasy, and begged him to stay there, and said, “You might easily meet with a great misfortune,” but he answered, “I must and will go.”
他站起身来，骑上马进了森林，没过多久，他发现一只漂亮的雄鹿从他面前的路穿过，和梦中的那只一模一样。他瞄准了正准备开枪时，那只鹿跑开了。他越过篱笆，翻过壕沟，不知疲倦地追了一整天，可是到了晚上，那只鹿从他视线里消失了。金孩儿环顾四周，发现自己正站在一座小房子前，里面有个女巫。他敲了敲门，那矮小的老女巫走了出来，问道：“这么晚了你还在这大森林里干什么呢？”“您有没有见过一只鹿？”“有啊，”她回答道，“我很了解那只鹿。”就在这时，从房子里跑出一只小狗，跟在女巫身边，冲着金孩儿恶狠狠地叫个不停。“别叫了，你这可恶的家伙！”金孩儿说，“否则我就一枪打死你。”不料，女巫发火了，嚷道：“什么！你敢杀我的小狗？”说完就把金孩儿变成了一块石头，就那样躺在地上。这时他的新娘左等右等，也不见金孩儿的影子，心中暗想：“一定是一直压在我心上的、最让我害怕的事情发生了！”留在家里的另一个金孩儿站在金百合旁边，看到其中一朵突然枯萎了。“天哪！”他喊道，“我的兄弟一定是遭到不幸了！我必须去看看我有没有可能拯救他。”他的父亲说：“别去了，要是我也失去了你，那我该怎么办呢？”可是金孩儿答道：“我非去不可。” Thereupon he got up, and rode forth into the forest, and it was not long before a fine stag crossed his path exactly according to his dream.He aimed and was about to shoot it, when the stag ran away.He gave chase over hedges and ditches for the whole day without feeling tired, but in the evening the stag vanished from his sight, and when the gold-child looked round him, he was standing before a little house, wherein was a witch.He knocked, and a little old woman came out and asked, “What are you doing so late in the midst of the great forest?”“Have you not seen a stag?”“Yes,” answered she, “I know the stag well,” and thereupon a little dog which had come out of the house with her, barked at the man violently.“Wilt thou be silent, thou odious toad,” said he, “or I will shoot thee dead.”Then the witch cried out in a passion, “What!will you slay my little dog?” and immediately transformed him, so that he lay like a stone, and his bride awaited him in vain and thought, “That which I so greatly dreaded, which lay so heavily on my heart, has come upon him!”But at home the other brother was standing by the gold-lilies, when one of them suddenly drooped.“Good heavens!” said he, “my brother has met with some great misfortune!I must away to see if I can possibly rescue him.”Then the father said, “Stay here, if I lose you also, what shall I do?”But he answered, “I must and will go forth!”
于是他骑上金马，来到他的兄弟被变成石头的那片大森林。那个老女巫从小屋中走出来叫住他，也想对他施魔法，可是他并不靠近那女巫，只是说：“要是你不让我的兄弟重新活过来，我就射死你。”虽然那女巫极其不情愿，但她不得不用食指点了一下那块石头，让他兄弟马上恢复了人形。两个金孩儿一见面，就高兴地拥抱着亲吻起来，然后他们一起骑马走出了森林，一个回到他的新娘家里，一个回到父亲身边。他的父亲说：“我知道你已经解救了你的兄弟，因为我看见那株金百合突然间又竖起来了，还开了花。”从此以后，他们一直过着幸福而富足的生活。 Then he mounted his golden horse, and rode forth and entered the great forest, where his brother lay turned to stone.The old witch came out of her house and called him, wishing to entrap him also, but he did not go near her, and said, “I will shoot you, if you will not bring my brother to life again.”She touched the stone, though very unwillingly, with her forefinger, and he was immediately restored to his human shape.But the two gold-children rejoiced when they saw each other again, kissed and caressed each other, and rode away together out of the forest, the one home to his bride, and the other to his father.The father then said, “I knew well that you had rescued your brother, for the golden lily suddenly rose up and blossomed out again.”Then they lived happily, and all prospered with them until their death.
金鸟 The Golden Bird
从前有位国王，在他的宫殿后面，有一座美丽的花园，那儿有棵苹果树，会结出金色的苹果。苹果成熟后，人们数清了果实的个数。但是就在第二天早上，人们发现少了一个金苹果。他们把这件事禀告给国王，国王下令每天晚上必须有人在果树下看守。 In the olden time there was a king, who had behind his palace a beautiful pleasure-garden in which there was a tree that bore golden apples.When the apples were getting ripe they were counted, but on the very next morning one was missing.This was told to the King, and he ordered that a watch should be kept every night beneath the tree.
国王有三个儿子。第一天夜幕降临之时，他就派自己的大儿子去果树下看守。然而半夜时，他抵挡不了浓浓睡意睡着了，第二天早上才发现又有一个金苹果不见了。 The King had three sons, the eldest of whom he sent, as soon as night came on, into the garden; but when midnight came he could not keep himself from sleeping, and next morning again an apple was gone.
第二天夜里，国王的二儿子被派去看守。他比哥哥好不了多少。午夜钟声刚刚敲响，他就睡着了。第二天早上醒来一看，又有一个金苹果不见了。 The following night the second son had to keep watch, it fared no better with him; as soon as twelve o’clock had struck he fell asleep, and in the morning an apple was gone.
第三天夜里轮到国王的小儿子去看守。他信心满满，国王却并不怎么信任他，觉得他还不如两个哥哥呢。不过最后，国王还是派他去了。这个年轻人躺在树下面，却努力克服着浓浓睡意，保持清醒。午夜钟声刚刚敲响，他就听到空中窸窣作响。借着月色，他看到一只鸟儿飞向金苹果树，浑身羽毛都散发着金色的光芒。小鸟停在树上。就在它刚刚叼下一个金苹果时，年轻人就朝它射了一箭。小鸟逃走了，但箭还是射到了它的羽毛，一片金色的羽毛飘落在地。年轻人把这片羽毛捡了起来。第二天一早，他就把它呈给国王，并禀告了夜里发生的事情。国王把所有的大臣都召集在一起商量对策。每个人都说这片羽毛比整个王国的财富还要珍贵。“如果这片羽毛如此珍贵的话，”国王说道，“那么只拥有一片羽毛可不行，我要得到那整只鸟！” Now it came to the turn of the third son to watch; and he was quite ready, but the King had not much trust in him, and thought that he would be of less use even than his brothers; but at last he let him go.The youth lay down beneath the tree, but kept awake, and did not let sleep master him.When it struck twelve, something rustled through the air, and in the moonlight he saw a bird coming whose feathers were all shining with gold.The bird alighted on the tree, and had just plucked off an apple, when the youth shot an arrow at him.The bird flew off, but the arrow had struck his plumage, and one of his golden feathers fell down.The youth picked it up, and the next morning took it to the King and told him what he had seen in the night.The King called his council together, and everyone declared that a feather like this was worth more than the whole kingdom.“If the feather is so precious,” declared the King, “one alone will not do for me; I must and will have the whole bird!”
听了国王的话，他的大儿子出发了。他自认为聪明过人，认为捉住金鸟对他来说轻而易举。他走了一会儿，看到有只狐狸坐在一片树林旁边。于是他端起枪，瞄准了那只狐狸。狐狸叫道：“不要开枪！作为报答，我可以给你一些忠告。顺着这路走下去，你就能找到金鸟。今天傍晚，你会路过一个小村庄。在那里，有两家面对面的旅店。其中一家灯火通明，所有人都会满心欢喜地去这家投宿。但是你不要去，去它对面的那家看似破旧的旅店过夜。”“这样愚蠢的动物能给出什么好建议呢？。”国王的大儿子想。于是他扣动了扳机。不过他没有打中，狐狸翘起尾巴，一下子钻进了树林。 The eldest son set out; he trusted to his cleverness, and thought that he would easily find the Golden Bird.When he had gone some distance he saw a Fox sitting at the edge of a wood, so he cocked his gun and took aim at him.The Fox cried, “Do not shoot me!and in return I will give you some good counsel.You are on the way to the Golden Bird; and this evening you will come to a village in which stand two inns opposite to one another.One of them is lighted up brightly, and all goes on merrily within, but do not go into it; go rather into the other, even though it seems a bad one.”“How can such a silly beast give wise advice?” thought the King’s son, and he pulled the trigger.But he missed the Fox, who stretched out his tail and ran quickly into the wood.
他继续前行，在傍晚时分来到了那个有两家旅店的小村庄。其中一家里面的人唱着歌跳着舞，而另外一家看起来又破旧又寒酸。他想：“如果我不去住那么好的旅店，反倒去住破旧的那家，那我真是个笨蛋了。”于是他就走进了那家充满着欢声笑语的旅店住了下来，从此沉湎于寻欢作乐，把金鸟、父王以及所有的忠告都抛在了脑后。 So he pursued his way, and by evening came to the village where the two inns were; in one they were singing and dancing; the other had a poor, miserable look.“I should be a fool, indeed,” he thought, “if I were to go into the shabby tavern, and pass by the good one.”So he went into the cheerful one, lived there in riot and revel, and forgot the bird and his father, and all good counsels.
几个月过去了，始终不见国王的大儿子回来。国王的二儿子又出发了，希望能找到金鸟。和哥哥一样，他也遇到了那只狐狸，而且同样也没有听进狐狸的忠告。他来到那两家旅店，听到音乐从其中一家传来，他的哥哥正站在那家的窗户前召唤自己。他控制不住地走进那家旅店，从此过着花天酒地的生活。 When some time had passed, and the eldest son for month after month did not come back home, the second set out, wishing to find the Golden Bird.The Fox met him as he had met the eldest, and gave him the good advice of which he took no heed.He came to the two inns, and his brother was standing at the window of the one from which came the music, and called out to him.He could not resist, but went inside and lived only for pleasure.
又过了一段时间，国王的小儿子也想动身去试试运气，可是国王不准。“没用的，”国王说，“他的哥哥们都找不到金鸟，他怎么能找到？万一发生什么意外怎么办？他呆头呆脑，肯定不知道如何应对。”但是最后国王被小儿子缠得受不了了，只能同意了。 Again some time passed, and then the King’s youngest son wanted to set off and try his luck, but his father would not allow it.“It is of no use,” said he, “he will find the Golden Bird still less than his brothers, and if a mishap were to befall him he knows not how to help himself; he is a little wanting at the best.”But at last, as he had no peace, he let him go.
同样的，他也遇到了那只坐在树林边的狐狸，它向他告饶，并给了他忠告。小王子心地善良，他对狐狸说：“小狐狸，不要害怕，我不会伤害你的。”“你不会后悔今天如此对我的，”狐狸说，“坐到我的尾巴上来，我带你去会快得多。”他刚在狐狸尾巴上坐好，狐狸就飞奔起来。它越过树干，越过岩石，身上的毛发被风吹得沙沙作响。他们来到那个小村庄，小王子从狐狸身上下来。他听从了狐狸的忠告，看都没看一眼就走进那家破旧的客栈，在那里度过了平静的一晚。 Again the Fox was sitting outside the wood, and begged for his life, and offered his good advice.The youth was good-natured, and said, “Be easy, little Fox, I will do you no harm.”“You shall not repent it,” answered the Fox; “and that you may get on more quickly, get up behind on my tail.”And scarcely had he seated himself when the Fox began to run, and away he went over stock and stone till his hair whistled in the wind.When they came to the village the youth got off; he followed the good advice, and without looking round turned into the little inn, where he spent the night quietly.
第二天一早，他走出村庄来到旷野，看到狐狸已经坐在那里等着他，它说：“我会告诉你接下来应该怎么做。一直往前走就会看到一座城堡，在城堡前有一群士兵躺在地上。不要担心他们，因为他们全都在呼呼大睡。从他们中间穿过，进入城堡，穿过所有的房间，最后就会找到金鸟所在的房间，它就在一个悬挂着的木质鸟笼里。在那个木制的鸟笼旁边，有一个空的供观赏用的金质鸟笼。记住不要把金鸟从木制鸟笼里拿出来放到金质鸟笼里，不然的话它会冲你发火的。”狐狸说完，又伸出尾巴，让小王子坐在上面。然后它又飞奔起来，越过树干，越过岩石，身上的毛发被风吹得沙沙作响。 The next morning, as soon as he got into the open country, there sat the Fox already, and said, “I will tell you further what you have to do.Go on quite straight, and at last you will come to a castle, in front of which a whole regiment of soldiers is lying, but do not trouble yourself about them, for they will all be asleep and snoring.Go through the midst of them straight into the castle, and go through all the rooms, till at last you will come to a chamber where a Golden Bird is hanging in a wooden cage.Close by, there stands an empty gold cage for show, but beware of taking the bird out of the common cage and putting it into the fine one, or it may go badly with you.”With these words the Fox again stretched out his tail, and the King’s son seated himself upon it, and away he went over stock and stone till his hair whistled in the wind.
他们来到城堡，小王子发现一切尽如狐狸所言。他来到金鸟所在的房间，发现它被关在一个木制鸟笼里，紧挨着一个金质鸟笼，丢失的那三个金苹果就散落在地上。“但是，”他想，“把这么美丽的鸟儿放在这么普通丑陋的鸟笼里太不合适了。”于是他把鸟笼打开，握住金鸟，把它放到了金质鸟笼里面。与此同时，金鸟发出尖利的叫声。呼呼大睡的士兵们醒了过来，冲进城堡，把他抓进监狱。第二天一早，他被带到法庭。他供认了自己的所作所为，即将被处以死刑。 When he came to the castle he found everything as the Fox had said.The King’s son went into the chamber where the Golden Bird was shut up in a wooden cage, whilst a golden one stood hard by; and the three golden apples lay about the room.“But,” thought he, “it would be absurd if I were to leave the beautiful bird in the common and ugly cage,” so he opened the door, laid hold of it, and put it into the golden cage.But at the same moment the bird uttered a shrill cry.The soldiers awoke, rushed in, and took him off to prison.The next morning he was taken before a court of justice, and as he confessed everything, was sentenced to death.
然而，国王告诉他，有个方法可以保住性命，只要他可以找来比风跑得还快的金马。那样他不仅可以保住性命，作为奖励，还可以带走金鸟。 The King, however, said that he would grant him his life on one condition namely, if he brought him the Golden Horse which ran faster than the wind; and in that case he should receive, over and above, as a reward, the Golden Bird.
小王子出发了，他悲伤不已，不住地叹气，因为他不知道怎么才能找到金马。但是突然间，他发现自己的老朋友——那只狐狸正坐在路上。“看看你，”狐狸说，“就是因为你当初没有听从我的忠告，才会落得这番田地。不过，你还是要勇敢一些。我会帮助你，告诉你怎样找到金马。沿着这条路继续往前走，你会看到一座城堡，那匹金马就在城堡的马厩里。马夫就躺在马厩外面呼呼大睡。他们不会醒来，你可以悄悄地走进马厩把金马牵出来。但是有一件事你必须记住，给它套上用木头和皮革制作的普通马鞍，而不是就挂在旁边的金质马鞍，不然的话它会对你不利的。”狐狸说完，伸出尾巴，让小王子坐在上面。它飞奔起来，越过树干，越过岩石，身上的毛发被风吹得沙沙作响。 The King’s son set off, but he sighed and was sorrowful, for how was he to find the Golden Horse?But all at once he saw his old friend the Fox sitting on the road.“Look you,” said the Fox, “this has happened because you did not give heed to me.However, be of good courage.I will give you my help, and tell you how to get to the Golden Horse.You must go straight on, and you will come to a castle, where in the stable stands the horse.The grooms will be lying in front of the stable; but they will be asleep and snoring, and you can quietly lead out the Golden Horse.But of one thing you must take heed; put on him the common saddle of wood and leather, and not the golden one, which hangs close by, else it will go ill with you.”Then the Fox stretched out his tail, the King’s son seated himself upon it, and away he went over stock and stone until his hair whistled in the wind.
一切正如狐狸所言。小王子来到金马所在的马厩。正准备给它套上马鞍时，他想：“如果不给它用一副好马鞍，就亏待了这么美丽的马儿。那副金质的马鞍正适合它。”然而，金质马鞍一碰到金马，它就发出高声嘶叫。马夫们醒了过来，抓住这个年轻人，把他投入监狱。第二天一早，法庭决定将他处以死刑。然而，这个国家的国王说可以不杀他，并给他金马，只要他能从金宫里把美丽的公主带回来。 Everything happened just as the Fox had said; the prince came to the stable in which the Golden Horse was standing, but just as he was going to put the common saddle upon him, he thought, “It will be a shame to such a beautiful beast, if I do not give him the good saddle which belongs to him by right.”But scarcely had the golden saddle touched the horse than he began to neigh loudly.The grooms awoke, seized the youth, and threw him into prison.The next morning he was sentenced by the court to death; but the King promised to grant him his life, and the Golden Horse as well, if he could bring back the beautiful princess from the Golden Castle.
这个年轻人心情沉重地上路了。不过幸运的是，他很快就又看见了那只忠诚的狐狸。“我真应该就让你自生自灭，”狐狸说道，“不过看你可怜，我就再帮你一次。这就是去金宫的路，天黑之前就能赶到。夜里，一切归于沉寂之后，美丽的公主就会到浴室洗浴。待她走进浴室，你就跑去吻她，她就会顺从于你，这时你就带她离开。只是千万别让她跟父母告别，否则就会对你不利。” With a heavy heart the youth set out; yet luckily for him he soon found the trusty Fox.“I ought only to leave you to your ill-luck,” said the Fox, “but I pity you, and will help you once more out of your trouble.This road takes you straight to the Golden Castle, you will reach it by eventide; and at night when everything is quiet the beautiful princess goes to the bathing-house to bathe.When she enters it, run up to her and give her a kiss, then she will follow you, and you can take her away with you; only do not allow her to take leave of her parents first, or it will go ill with you.”
狐狸说完，伸出尾巴，让小王子坐到上面。它飞奔起来，越过树干，越过岩石，身上的毛发被风吹得沙沙作响。 Then the Fox stretched out his tail, the King’s son seated himself upon it, and away the Fox went, over stock and stone, till his hair whistled in the wind.
他们到达金宫，一切尽如狐狸所言。小王子一直等到午夜。一切归于沉寂之后，美丽的公主走向浴室。王子奔向公主，并吻了她。公主说愿意随他走。但是她两眼含泪，楚楚可怜地请求让她在走之前去跟父母告个别。刚开始小王子不为所动，但是公主哭得越来越厉害，并跪在地上苦苦哀求，他还是同意了。然而，公主一来到父王身边，城堡里所有的人就都醒了过来。他们抓住了这个年轻人，并把他投入了监狱。 When he reached the Golden Castle it was just as the Fox had said.He waited until midnight, when everything lay in deep sleep, and the beautiful princess was going to the bathing-house.Then he sprang out and gave her a kiss.She said that she would like to go with him, but she asked him pitifully, and with tears, to allow her first to take leave of her parents.At first he withstood her prayer, but when she wept more and more, and fell at his feet, he at last gave in.But no sooner had the maiden reached the bedside of her father than he and all the rest in the castle awoke, and the youth was laid hold of and put into prison.
第二天一早，国王对他说：“我本来要治你的死罪。不过如果你可以在八天之内，把我窗前那座碍眼的大山搬走，你的死罪就可以获免。除此之外，作为奖励，我还可以把女儿许配给你。” The next morning the King said to him, “Your life is forfeited, and you can only find mercy if you take away the hill which stands in front of my windows, and prevents my seeing beyond it; and you must finish it all within eight days.If you do that you shall have my daughter as your reward.”
小王子开始干活，他一刻不停地挖啊铲啊，然而七天过去了，他看到自己才弄了一点点，他所做的一切对眼前这座山根本不会有任何影响。他极度悲伤，陷入了绝望。然而，在第七天的夜幕降临之时，那只狐狸又出现了，对他说：“你真不值得让我每次都帮你幸免于难。不过，你别管了，去睡觉吧，我会来帮你的。” The King’s son began, and dug and shovelled without leaving off, but when after seven days he saw how little he had done, and how all his work was as good as nothing, he fell into great sorrow and gave up all hope.But on the evening of the seventh day the Fox appeared and said, ‘You do not deserve that I should take any trouble about you; but just go away and lie down to sleep, and I will do the work for you.”
第二天一早，当他醒来从窗户里向外看时，那座大山已经不见了。小王子高兴至极，奔向国王，告诉他任务已经完成了。不管国王愿不愿意，他都必须遵守诺言，把女儿许配给他。 The next morning when he awoke and looked out of the window the hill had gone.The youth ran, full of joy, to the King, and told him that the task was fulfilled, and whether he liked it or not, the King had to hold to his word and give him his daughter.
小王子带着美丽的公主踏上了归途。不一会儿，忠诚的狐狸就追上了他们。“毫无疑问，你已经得到了这世上最珍贵的东西。”它说，“不过，金马理应属于金宫的公主。”“那我怎么样才能得到它？”年轻人问道。“我会告诉你怎么做的。”狐狸答道，“先带着美丽的公主去见派你去金宫的那位国王。他们会兴奋至极，会很乐意把金马牵出来赠于你。你要骑上金马，越快越好，然后伸出手来与所有人告别，最后再与美丽的公主告别。你一握住她的手，就把她拽上马，策马离开。这样，就没有人能追得上你，因为金马比风跑得都快。” So the two set forth together, and it was not long before the trusty Fox came up with them.“You have certainly got what is best,” said he, “but the Golden Horse also belongs to the maiden of the Golden Castle.”“How shall I get it?” asked the youth.“That I will tell you,” answered the Fox; “first take the beautiful maiden to the King who sent you to the Golden Castle.There will be unheard-of rejoicing; they will gladly give you the Golden Horse, and will bring it out to you.Mount it as soon as possible, and offer your hand to all in farewell; last of all to the beautiful maiden.And as soon as you have taken her hand swing her up on to the horse, and gallop away, and no one will be able to bring you back, for the horse runs faster than the wind.”
小王子照狐狸所言行事，一切都很顺利。他骑着金马，带走了美丽的公主。 All was carried out successfully, and the King’s son carried off the beautiful princess on the Golden Horse.
狐狸一路随行。它对小王子说：“现在我帮你得到金鸟。你到达金鸟所在城堡附近后，先把公主放下来，我来照看她。你骑着金马进入城堡大院，他们看到金马，肯定兴奋不已，就会把金鸟拿出来给你。你一拿到鸟笼，就策马回到我们身边，然后带着公主离开。” The Fox did not remain behind, and he said to the youth, “Now I will help you to get the Golden Bird.When you come near to the castle where the Golden Bird is to be found, let the maiden get down, and I will take her into my care.Then ride with the Golden Horse into the castle-yard; there will be great rejoicing at the sight, and they will bring out the Golden Bird for you.As soon as you have the cage in your hand gallop back to us, and take the maiden away again.
小王子依狐狸所言，又得到了金鸟。正当他带着所有珍宝准备回家时，狐狸对他说道：“现在是该你报答我的时候了。”“你想让我怎么报答你呢？”小王子问。“你一到那边的那片树林，就用枪把我打死，并砍下我的头和脚。” When the plan had succeeded, and the King’s son was about to ride home with his treasures, the Fox said, “Now you shall reward me for my help.”“What do you require for it?” asked the youth.“When you get into the wood yonder, shoot me dead, and chop off my head and feet.”
“这算什么报答呀？”小王子说，“我是不可能对你做那样的事情的。” “That would be fine gratitude,” said the King’s son.“I cannot possibly do that for you.”
狐狸说：“如果你不同意的话，那我就必须离开你了。不过走之前，我要再给你一个忠告。记住两件事情。不要买绞刑架上面的肉，也不要坐在任何一个井边。”说完这些，狐狸就跑进了树林。 The Fox said, “If you will not do it I must leave you, but before I go away I will give you a piece of good advice.Be careful about two things.Buy no gallows’-flesh, and do not sit at the edge of any well.”And then he ran into the wood.
小王子想：“这真是一只奇妙的动物。它的想法着实奇怪，怎么会有人去买绞刑架上面的肉呢？而且我也从来没有过坐在井边的想法。” The youth thought, “That is a wonderful beast, he has strange whims; who is going to buy gallows’-flesh?and the desire to sit at the edge of a well it has never yet seized me.”
他带着美丽的公主，骑着金马继续前行。然后他路过了他的两位哥哥所停留的村庄。村里聚集了很多村民，人声鼎沸。小王子问村民发生了什么事，村民告诉他有两个人要被送上绞刑架。他走近一看，发现那两人正是自己的哥哥。他们做尽坏事，并把钱财都挥霍光了。王子上前询问可否释放他们两个。“如果你肯出钱就行。”人们回答，“不过你何必为这两个奸人浪费钱财呢？”他不假思索就拿钱换回了他两位哥哥的自由，带着他们一起踏上了回家的路。 He rode on with the beautiful maiden, and his road took him again through the village in which his two brothers had remained.There was a great stir and noise, and, when he asked what was going on, he was told that two men were going to be hanged.As he came nearer to the place he saw that they were his brothers, who had been playing all kinds of wicked pranks, and had squandered all their wealth.He inquired whether they could not be set free.“If you will pay for them,” answered the people; “but why should you waste your money on wicked men, and buy them free.”He did not think twice about it, but paid for them, and when they were set free they all went on their way together.
他们路过那片遇到狐狸的树林，里面清爽怡人，他的两位哥哥说道：“我们在井边稍微休息一下吧，吃点东西。”小王子同意了。他们聊天的时候，小王子忘记了狐狸的忠告，毫无戒备地在井边坐了下来。两位哥哥把他向后推，推到了井里，然后带上公主、金马和金鸟回去见了父王。“我们不仅为您找到了金鸟，”两个王子说，“我们还带回了金马和金宫里的公主。”王宫上下一片欢腾。然而，金马不愿进食，金鸟不愿歌唱，金宫公主也一直坐在那里哭泣。 They came to the wood where the Fox had first met them, as it was cool and pleasant within it, the two brothers said, “Let us rest a little by the well, and eat and drink.”He agreed, and whilst they were talking he forgot himself, and sat down upon the edge of the well without thinking of any evil.But the two brothers threw him backwards into the well, took the maiden, the Horse, and the Bird, and went home to their father.“Here we bring you not only the Golden Bird,” said they; “we have won the Golden Horse also, and the maiden from the Golden Castle.”Then was there great joy; but the Horse would not eat, the Bird would not sing, and the maiden sat and wept.
不过，他们的弟弟却没有死。幸运的是，那是一口枯井。他摔到了柔软的苔藓上面毫发无伤，不过却苦于无法出来。即便是在这样的处境下，忠诚的狐狸也没有弃他于不顾。它只是责备王子把自己的忠告置之脑后。“不过我不能见死不救，”它说，“我一定要把你救上来，让你重见天日。”它让小王子抓住自己的尾巴，并一直抓牢，然后把他拉了上来。 But the youngest brother was not dead.By good fortune the well was dry, and he fell upon soft moss without being hurt, but he could not get out again.Even in this strait the faithful Fox did not leave him: it came and leapt down to him, and upbraided him for having forgotten its advice.“But yet I cannot give it up so,” he said; “I will help you up again into daylight.”He bade him grasp his tail and keep tight hold of it; and then he pulled him up.
“不过你还没有完全脱离险境。”狐狸说。“你的哥哥们唯恐你还活着，就派看守人把这片树林围了起来，嘱咐他们一见到你就把你杀死。”不过有个穷人坐在路上，小王子与他互换了衣服。就这样，他回到了王宫。 “You are not out of all danger yet,” said the Fox.“Your brothers were not sure of your death, and have surrounded the wood with watchers, who are to kill you if you let yourself be seen.”But a poor man was sitting upon the road, with whom the youth changed clothes, and in this way he got to the King’s palace.
没有人能认得出他。然而，金鸟开始歌唱，金马开始进食，美丽的公主也止住了哭泣。国王震惊不已，问道：“这是怎么回事？”公主说：“我也不知道。我之前很难过，但现在却很开心。我感觉到我真正的新郎已经到了。”尽管国王的大儿子和二儿子威胁公主如果她说出真相就要杀死她，但公主还是把路上发生的一切都原原本本地告诉了国王。 No one knew him, but the Bird began to sing, the Horse began to eat, and the beautiful maiden left off weeping.The King, astonished, asked, “What does this mean?”Then the maiden said, “I do not know, but I have been so sorrowful and now I am so happy!I feel as if my true bridegroom had come.”She told him all that had happened, although the other brothers had threatened her with death if she were to betray anything.
国王下令把城堡里的人全都带到他的面前，小王子身着破烂衣衫站在人群里，但公主一眼就认出了他，扑到了他的怀中。他两个狠毒的哥哥被抓了起来并被处死了。他迎娶了美丽的公主，还成为了国王的继承人。 The King commanded that all people who were in his castle should be brought before him; and amongst them came the youth in his ragged clothes; but the maiden knew him at once and fell upon his neck.The wicked brothers were seized and put to death, but he was married to the beautiful maiden and declared heir to the King.
那可怜的狐狸又怎么样了呢？过了很长一段时间，小王子在那片树林里散步，又遇到了那只狐狸。狐狸对他说：“现在你得到了梦想的一切，我却要遭受永无止境的折磨。现在只有你才能让我解脱。”说完，它流下泪来，再次恳求王子用枪把它打死，并把它的头和脚砍下来。王子同意了。他刚一做完，狐狸就变成了一个人。他不是别人，正是那位美丽的金宫公主的哥哥。他之前被施了魔法，现在终于解脱了。从那以后，他们什么都不缺，一直过着幸福快乐的日子。 But how did it fare with the poor Fox?Long afterwards the King’s son was once again walking in the wood, when the Fox met him and said, “You have everything now that you can wish for, but there is never an end to my misery, and yet it is in your power to free me,” and again he asked him with tears to shoot him dead and chop off his head and feet.So he did it, and scarcely was it done when the Fox was changed into a man, and was no other than the brother of the beautiful princess, who at last was freed from the magic charm which had been laid upon him.And now nothing more was wanting to their happiness as long as they lived.
井边的养鹅女 The Goose-Girl at the Well
很久以前，有位老婆婆和一群鹅住在大山之间的荒野里，那儿有她的一间小房子。荒野四周环绕着一片大森林，每天早晨，老太太都会拄着拐杖，蹒跚地到森林里去。她在那儿忙个不停，别人都无法相信她这样的年纪还能做那么多事情：她给鹅割草，采摘所有能采到的野果，还把所有这些都背回家去。别人一定以为这么重的东西会把她压倒在地，可是她每次都能安全地把东西背到家。要是有谁碰到她，她都和蔼地打招呼。“你好啊，亲爱的乡亲，今天天气不错呢。哦！你肯定会惊讶我背着这么多草，不过每个人都得背起他自己的负担呀。”不过，大家宁愿绕弯路，也不想碰见她。一位父亲带着儿子走过她身边时，他小声对儿子们说：“当心这个老太婆。她心怀鬼胎，是个巫婆。”一天早晨，一个英俊的年轻人在森林中漫步。阳光明媚，鸟儿歌唱，凉风轻拂着树叶，年轻人神清气爽，心旷神怡。一路上，他一个人都没遇上，却突然看见了老巫婆正跪在地上用镰刀割草。她已经割好整整一布包草了，身边还放着两个装满野苹果和野梨的篮子。“嗨，老婆婆，”年轻人说，“你怎么能搬得动呀？”“我不搬不行呀，亲爱的先生，”她答道，“富家公子不必干这种活，而贫民百姓有句俗语，不要转身看，你的背跟弯弓一样！” There was once upon a time a very old woman, who lived with her flock of geese in a waste place among the mountains, and there had a little house.The waste was surrounded by a large forest, and every morning the old woman took her crutch and hobbled into it.There, however, the dame was quite active, more so than any one would have thought, considering her age, and collected grass for her geese, picked all the wild fruit she could reach, and carried everything home on her back.Any one would have thought that the heavy load would have weighed her to the ground, but she always brought it safely home.If any one met her, she greeted him quite courteously.“Good day, dear countryman, it is a fine day.Ah! you wonder that I should drag grass about, but every one must take his burthen on his back.”Nevertheless, people did not like to meet her if they could help it, and took by preference a round-about way, and when a father with his boys passed her, he whispered to them, “Beware of the old woman.She has claws beneath her gloves; she is a witch.”One morning, a handsome young man was going through the forest.The sun shone bright, the birds sang, a cool breeze crept through the leaves, and he was full of joy and gladness.He had as yet met no one, when he suddenly perceived the old witch kneeling on the ground cutting grass with a sickle.She had already thrust a whole load into her cloth, and near it stood two baskets, which were filled with wild apples and pears.“But, good little mother,” said he, “how canst thou carry all that away?”“I must carry it, dear sir,” answered she, “rich folk’s children have no need to do such things, but with the peasant folk the saying goes, don’t look behind you, you will only see how crooked your back is!”
“你愿意帮我吗？”见年轻人站着没走，她便问道。“你的背挺直，腿脚灵活，干这个肯定不费劲。再说，我家离这儿不远，就在山后的荒野地。你很快就能到。”年轻人非常同情老婆婆。“我父亲虽然不是农民，而是位有钱的伯爵，”他说道，“但你会看到并不是只有农民才能搬东西，我愿意帮你把东西背回去。”“如果你愿意试试，”她说，“那我会非常高兴。你得走一个小时的路程，可这对你算得了什么呢，苹果和梨你也给捎上？”年轻人一听要走一个小时，就有点犹豫。但是老婆婆不放过他，把草捆到他的背上，把两个篮子挎到他胳膊上。“看吧，东西挺轻。”她说。“不，一点儿都不轻。”年轻的伯爵满面愁容地答道。“实际上，背上的草捆很沉，像是装了石头一样，苹果和梨也像灌了铅似的！我都快喘不上气了。”他很想把这些东西都放下，但是老婆婆不让。“看哪，”她嘲讽道，“我老太婆常干的事，年轻的绅士却不愿干。说漂亮话在行，可真干起来，就想打退堂鼓了。你怎么还站在那儿？”她接着说道。“快走吧。没人会帮你把东西取下来的。”如果是平路，年轻人还能忍住，可一到山脚，他们开始爬坡，脚下的石头就好像活了一样，一直往下滚，这时年轻人就有点吃不消了。他的额头冒出了汗珠，流到背上，背上一阵冷汗一阵热汗。“老婆婆，”他说，“我实在走不动了。我想休息一下。”“在这儿不行，”老婆婆答道，“我们到达之后，你才能休息；现在你必须继续走。谁知道你打的什么主意呢？”“老婆婆，你好不讲理呀！”年轻人边说边试图扔下草捆，可是徒劳无益；草捆就像长住似的紧紧压在背上。他转过来转过去，怎么都甩不掉它。老婆婆放声大笑，兴奋地拄着拐杖手舞足蹈。“别生气，年轻人，”她说，“你脸红得像火鸡似的！耐心地背着你那捆草。咱们到家后，我会给你一样好礼物的。” “Will you help me?” she said, as he remained standing by her.“You have still a straight back and young legs, it would be a trifle to you.Besides, my house is not so very far from here, it stands there on the heath behind the hill.How soon you would bound up thither.”The young man took compassion on the old woman.“My father is certainly no peasant,” replied he, “but a rich count; nevertheless, that you may see that it is not only peasants who can carry things, I will take your bundle.”If you will try it,” said she, “I shall be very glad.You will certainly have to walk for an hour, but what will that signify to you; only you must carry the apples and pears as well?”It now seemed to the young man just a little serious, when he heard of an hour’s walk, but the old woman would not let him off, packed the bundle on his back, and hung the two baskets on his arm.“See, it is quite light,” said she.“No, it is not light,” answered the count, and pulled a rueful face.“Verily, the bundle weighs as heavily as if it were full of cobble stones, and the apples and pears are as heavy as lead!I can scarcely breathe.”He had a mind to put everything down again, but the old woman would not allow it.“Just look,” said she mockingly, “the young gentleman will not carry what I, an old woman, have so often dragged along.You are ready with fine words, but when it comes to be earnest, you want to take to your heels.Why are you standing loitering there?” she continued.“Step out.No one will take the bundle off again.”As long as he walked on level ground, it was still bearable, but when they came to the hill and had to climb, and the stones rolled down under his feet as if they were alive, it was beyond his strength.The drops of perspiration stood on his forehead, and ran, hot and cold, down his back.“Dame,” said he, “I can go no farther.I want to rest a little.”“Not here,” answered the old woman, “when we have arrived at our journey’s end, you can rest; but now you must go forward.Who knows what good it may do you?”“Old woman, thou art becoming shameless!” said the count, and tried to throw off the bundle, but he laboured in vain; it stuck as fast to his back as if it grew there.He turned and twisted, but he could not get rid of it.The old woman laughed at this, and sprang about quite delighted on her crutch.“Don’t get angry, dear sir,” said she, “you are growing as red in the face as a turkey-cock!Carry your bundle patiently.I will give you a good present when we get home.”
年轻人无可奈何。他只好认命，只好跟在老婆婆后面耐心地走。她似乎越走越轻快，但是他背上的包袱却越来越沉。突然，她往上一跳，跳上了草捆并坐了下来，她虽然枯瘦如柴，但却比乡下最胖的姑娘还要重。年轻人的膝盖打颤，可要是不往前走，老婆婆就会用鞭子和荨麻杆抽打他的腿。他呻吟着继续爬山，终于到了老婆婆的家，他也几乎要倒下了。那些鹅看见老婆婆，都拍打着翅膀，伸长脖子，咯咯叫着跑向她。一个上了年纪的女人手里拿着根棍子，走在鹅群后面。她又高又壮，像黑夜一样丑陋。“好妈妈，”她问老婆婆，“出什么事了么，你在外头呆这么久？”“没什么，我的好女儿，”她说，“没遇上什么麻烦，相反，这位好心的绅士帮我背东西；我走累了，你想想，他还连我也背上。这段路对我们来说一点都不远，我们一路很开心，还一直互相开玩笑呢。”终于，老婆婆从年轻人身上滑下来，把年轻人背上的那捆草取下来，把他胳膊上的篮子摘下来，十分亲切地看着他，说道：“现在你可以坐到门前长凳上休息了。你理应得到你那份报酬，肯定少不了你的。”接着她对放鹅女孩说：“进屋去吧，我的好女儿，你不该和一位年轻的绅士单独呆在一起；咱们不应火上浇油，他会爱上你的。”年轻人听了哭笑不得。“这样一个活宝，”年轻人心想，“即使再年轻三十岁，也不会打动我的心。”这时，老太太像抚摸自己孩子一样，抚摸着她的鹅，随后和她的女儿一起进屋里去了。年轻人躺在一棵野苹果树下的长凳上。空气温暖宜人，四周围是绿色的草地，草地上开满樱草、野麝香和许多各种各样的花。一条清澈的小溪从草地中间穿过，阳光照在水面上闪闪发光，有的白鹅在草地上来来回回地散步，有的白鹅在水中嬉戏。“这儿真是太赏心悦目了，”他说，“可我累得眼都睁不开了；我得睡一小会儿。”但愿别刮风，不然我的腿会被吹走，因为我的腿软得跟火绒一样。” What could he do.He was obliged to submit to his fate, and crawl along patiently behind the old woman.She seemed to grow more and more nimble, and his burden still heavier.All at once she made a spring, jumped on to the bundle and seated herself on the top of it; and however withered she might be, she was yet heavier than the stoutest country lass.The youth’s knees trembled, but when he did not go on, the old woman hit him about the legs with a switch and with stinging-nettles.Groaning continually, he climbed the mountain, and at length reached the old woman’s house, when he was just about to drop.When the geese perceived the old woman, they flapped their wings, stretched out their necks, ran to meet her, cackling all the while.Behind the flock walked, stick in hand, an old wench, strong and big, but ugly as night.“Good mother,” said she to the old woman, “has anything happened to you, you have stayed away so long?”“By no means, my dear daughter,” answered she, I have met with nothing bad, but, on the contrary, with this kind gentleman, who has carried my burthen for me; only think, he even took me on his back when I was tired.The way, too, has not seemed long to us; we have been merry, and have been cracking jokes with each other all the time.”At last the old woman slid down, took the bundle off the young man’s back, and the baskets from his arm, looked at him quite kindly, and said, “Now seat yourself on the bench before the door, and rest.You have fairly earned your wages, and they shall not be wanting.”Then she said to the goose—girl, “Go into the house, my dear daughter, it is not becoming for thee to be alone with a young gentleman; one must not pour oil on to the fire, he might fall in love with thee.”The count knew not whether to laugh or to cry.“Such a sweetheart as that,” thought he, “could not touch my heart, even if she were thirty years younger.”In the meantime the old woman stroked and fondled her geese as if they were children, and then went into the house with her daughter.The youth lay down on the bench, under a wild apple-tree.The air was warm and mild; on all sides stretched a green meadow, which was set with cowslips, wild thyme, and a thousand other flowers; through the midst of it rippled a clear brook on which the sun sparkled, and the white geese went walking backwards and forwards, or paddled in the water.“It is quite delightful here,” said he, “but I am so tired that I cannot keep my eyes open; I will sleep a little.If only a gust of wind does not come and blow my legs off my body, for they are as rotten as tinder.”
刚睡了片刻，老婆婆就出来把他摇醒。“起来吧，”她说，“你不能留在这里，我是把你整得很惨，但是还不至于危及生命。金钱和土地你并不需要，我送你样别的东西。”说着就把一个用整块绿宝石雕刻的小匣子递给了他。“好好保管，”她说，“它会给你带来好运的。”伯爵跳了起来，因为他感到自己精神抖擞，重新恢复了体力，他感谢老婆婆送他礼物，都没回头看那个漂亮的女儿一眼就离开了。走出一大段路，他还能听见鹅的欢叫声。 When he had slept a little while, the old woman came and shook him till he awoke.“Sit up,” said she, “thou canst not stay here; I have certainly treated thee hardly, still it has not cost thee thy life.Of money and land thou hast no need, here is something else for thee.”Thereupon she thrust a little book into his hand, which was cut out of a single emerald.“Take great care of it,” said she, “it will bring thee good fortune.”The count sprang up, and as he felt that he was quite fresh, and had recovered his vigor, he thanked the old woman for her present, and set off without even once looking back at the beautiful daughter.When he was already some way off, he still heard in the distance the noisy cry of the geese.
伯爵在荒野走了三天才找到出去的路。后来，他来到一座大城市里，因为人们都不认识他，就把他带进了王宫，国王和王后坐在宝座上。他单膝跪地，掏出绿宝石雕刻的小匣子，放在王后脚下。王后命令他起来，并把小匣子递给她。王后刚把匣子打开看上一眼，就晕倒在地，像死去了一般。国王的侍从把伯爵抓了起来关进监狱，王后醒来后，命令放了他，并叫所有人都出去，只和伯爵单独说话。 For three days the count had to wander in the wilderness before he could find his way out.He then reached a large town, and as no one knew him, he was led into the royal palace, where the King and Queen were sitting on their throne.The count fell on one knee, drew the emerald book out of his pocket, and laid it at the Queen’s feet.She bade him rise and hand her the little book.Hardly, however, had she opened it, and looked therein, than she fell as if dead to the ground.The count was seized by the King’s servants, and was being led to prison, when the Queen opened her eyes, and ordered them to release him, and every one was to go out, as she wished to speak with him in private.
剩下王后自己一人，她痛苦地哭了起来，说：“我身边的荣华富贵有什么用呢，每天早晨我都伴着痛苦和悲伤醒来。我有三个女儿，其中小女儿非常美丽，人们都说她简直是个奇迹。她似雪一样白净，像苹果花一样娇艳，她的头发好比灿烂的阳光。她哭泣的时候，眼里流下的不是眼泪，而是珍珠和宝石。在她十五岁的的时候，国王把三个女儿叫到宝座前。当小女儿走进来时，你真该看看在场的人们是怎么瞪大了眼睛，她就像是初升的太阳！国王说：“我的孩子们，我不知道我的末日什么时候到来，我想今天决定在我死后你们能得到什么。你们都爱我，但最爱我的那个应得到最好的东西。”每个女儿都说自己最爱他。“你们能不能告诉我，”国王说，“你们有多爱我，这样，我就知道你们的想法了？”大女儿说：“我爱父王，如同爱最甜的点心。”二女儿说：“我爱父王，如同爱我最漂亮的衣服。”但是小女儿却沉默不语。父亲就问她：“你呢，我亲爱的孩子，你有多爱我？”“我不知道，没有任何东西能跟我对您的爱相比。”但是父亲坚持让她说些什么。于是她最终说：“没有盐，再好的佳肴我也不喜欢，所以，我爱父亲就像爱盐一样。”国王听后勃然大怒，说：“既然你爱我像爱盐一样，那就用盐来回报你的爱好了。”于是，他将王国分给大女儿和二女儿，而将一袋盐绑在小女儿背上，让两个侍从将她押到荒野的森林里。“我们大家都为小女儿求情，”王后说，“但是没法让国王消气。当她不得不离开我们的时候，她哭得是多么伤心呀！整条路都洒满了从她眼里落下的珍珠。过了没多久，国王就对自己的严厉做法感到很后悔，他让人在整个森林里寻找那个可怜的孩子，可是没人找得到她。每当我想到她可能被野兽吃掉，便伤心得不能自已。有的时候，我又以此安慰自己，想着她还没死，可能是藏在山洞里，或者被好心人收留了。但是，你想想，当我打开你的绿宝石匣子，发现里面的珍珠和我女儿眼里掉出来的一样，你准能想象我内心多么激动。你一定要告诉我你是怎么得到这颗珍珠的。”伯爵告诉王后他是从森林里的一个老婆婆那儿得到的，在他看来，老婆婆有些非同一般，肯定是个巫婆，但是他没有看见或听说关于王后女儿的任何事。国王和王后决定去找那个老婆婆。他们觉得能从有珍珠的地方打听到小女儿的消息。 When the Queen was alone, she began to weep bitterly, and said, “Of what use to me are the splendours and honours with which I am surrounded;
